After I have completed this book for you, O Sons, which is the last one concerning knowledge in medicine with its complement, and having reached the end of it by expositions and explanations, it appeared to me to be fitting that I complete it for you with this Treatise, which forms part of operation, i.e., surgery with hand.
Since operation with hand is laid low in our region and during our time entirely removed: perhaps the knowledge of it has perished, and its trace vanished; and only small descriptions of it remain in old books, which have been altered by hands; and error and hesitation have arisen until the intention is closed and the force waned: It seemed to me fitting that I bring it to life again with the organization of this Treatise according to the way of exposition, explanation, and abbreviation; and that I come with forms of iron tools of Cautery, and other instruments of work, when it is made by addition of declarations, and by the proper use of what is necessary.
The reason why a good craftsman with his hand is not found in this time is because the art of medicine is long, and its author must exercise himself before that in the knowledge of anatomy as Galen narrated, until he knows the aid of members, their forms, their connection, separation, and the knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their number, their departure, veins pulsating and quiet, and their outlets.
And for that reason, Hippocrates said that much is the name with a name, and little is the work, especially in the art of hand.
We have already spoken about it at the beginning of this book.
Whoever is not knowing what we said about anatomy, will immediately fall into error, in which people are killed: as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science, boasting about it without knowledge and without experience.
I have seen a stupid physician cut an aposteme (boil) on a woman's neck and accidentally cut some arteries in the neck: therefore, blood flowed from the woman until she fell dead at his hands.
I have seen another physician who dared to remove a stone from an old man who had grown it, and the stone was large. So he came to him, and removed it along with part of his bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
I had already been called to remove it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die.
I have seen another physician who received a staff at some Duke's land for medicine, and it happened to him a eunuch black, who was with him, suffered a fracture near his heel: and the physician, in his ignorance, bound up the fracture over a wound with splints, strong bandages, and needles, and did not let the wound breathe.
Then he cured him according to his own devices. Then he released him after some days, and ordered him not to undo the binding: and it stood thus until a boil came on his leg, and on his foot, and it led to his destruction.
I was then called to him: and I hastened to undo the binding: and peace came upon him, and he was freed from his pains.
However, the corruption had already been confirmed in the member: and I could not stop it.
Stop then the corruption to walk in the member, until it perishes.
And I saw another physician who pierced a malignant ulcer (apostema), and it became worse over days until the wickedness of it was manifested with its master (lord).
Because when a cancer is pure from the melancholic humor, then it is not appropriate to approach it with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can endure, so that the whole of it is cut off.
And because of this (saying) O Sons (of the Prophet), it is necessary for you to know that an operation is divided into two divisions, namely, an operation which is associated with safety: and an operation with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already awakened throughout this entire book, where the operation comes which has fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that (matter) and separate it from itself: so that fools do not find a way to speak about it and shame it.
Take then the measure with care and protection, and your sick ones with ease and firmness, and use a better way leading by the grace of God to health and praiseworthy success: and let go of terrible illnesses difficult to heal; and free your souls from what causes you fear, so that hesitation in faith and comfort may not enter upon you.
For it remains more to your glory, and it is higher in this world, and finally to your wealth.
Galenus indeed said so in some of his advisories. Do not heal the evil sickness, lest you be called an evil physician.
Now however, I have divided this Treatise according to three Chapters.Â¶
Chapter One.
On Cautery with fire, and Cautery with sharp medicine, is discussed, and ordered from head to feet, and the forms of instruments and tools for Cautery, and all that is necessary in the procedure.
Chapter second.
On sectioning and perforating, phlebotomy and wounding, as well as arrow extractions and similar matters; and the entire chapter ordered in forms of instruments.
Chapter third.
On restoration, dislocation, treatment of twisting, and similar matters; discussed and ordered from head to feet, and the forms of instruments.
Before I remember the operation with him, it is necessary that I say the qualities of his remedies and his harms, and in which compound they are displayed.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the cautery and its harm is a long, subtle, learned discourse, a secret hidden thing.
Also, there was a multitude of wise ones in it, and they disagreed among themselves; and for me, it is enough with little from their discourses, fearing prolongation.
I say therefore that the cautery applies generally to every compound, which is with matter, and without matter; except for two compounds, which are a hot compound without matter, and a dry compound without matter.
But in the hot and dry compound with matter they disagreed. For some, it was said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the contrary to that one, namely that the cautery is not suitable in a disease which is from heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat, and it is inconvenient to be healed from a hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
And he who says the contrary to that one said: by the cautery, it is a remedy for every hot and dry disease which happens in the bodies of men; because when you compare the body of man and his humidity, to the compound of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I certainly say through his discourse: because from experience he has already revealed that to me several times.
Nevertheless, it is not necessary for him to come to that, unless he who has already been proven and exercised in the last chapter of cautery, and knows the diversity of human complexions, and the constitution of diseases within himself, and the causes of them, and their symptoms, and the space of time of them.
From the remaining temperaments, there is no fear for you: and particularly in cold and moist diseases. Indeed, all physicians agree on them: and they have not disagreed in their treatment with Cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing by Cautery with fire and its goodness upon the Cautery with a medicine burning, because fire is simple, whose action does not penetrate except to the member being cauterized: and it does not harm another adjacent member unless with minor damage.
The action of burning medicine reaches to that which is distant from the members: and perhaps it causes difficulty in healing in the member, and perhaps it kills.
But fire, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
Indeed, we have come to know that through experience, due to the length of service and devotion to art, and steadiness concerning the truth of things: and because of this I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not that it is not allowed for this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret hidden in fire and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases demonstrated by philosophical discourse, which would be clear to your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves disagree in time, when it is fitting to make a cautery, and they put the better time according to truth.
And I say that a cautery is fitting at all times: therefore, because damage occurring by time is immersed in the benefit which is drawn with the cautery. And particularly if a cautery is for pains arising from necessary, strong, urgent pains that cannot tolerate delay: therefore because it is feared that evil which is greater than small damage due to time may occur.
And that saying does not enter your minds, O sons, except for the common people and foolish physicians, namely that they do not always return to health by cauterization: and they place this as a consequence, but matters are not as they think: therefore because cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which alters the temperament, and drives out humors that are the causes, wherefore pains occur.
However, cauterization is superfluous over medicine because of the swiftness of its health, and the power of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that illness may return at some hour of time according to the temperament of the sick person, and the location of his illness, and the power of his illness: and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in him: and what reaches him for acquisition through food and similar things from those causes, unless illness occurs, where cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in a member of small superfluities and humors, such as cauterization of the tooth, due to pain and similar things, it is possible that this pain will not return in him. But this happens rarely.
However, the speech of the common people is again correct that cauterization is the last medicine: not with regard to what they intend in this matter, since they believe that there is no healing that comes with medicine, nor with anything after the end of cauterization.
But the matter is the opposite of that speech and intention, namely that cauterization is the last medicine, is not except when we administer modes of healing for some illnesses, and they do not come from medicine: then at the end of the matter, we apply cauterization, and it heals: thus it happens that cauterization is the last medicine, not according to the intention that the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that cautionery with gold is better than cautionery with iron; and they did not say this unless on account of the equality of gold, and the nobility of its substance; and they said, that it does not cause a place of cauterization to produce pus. It is not this absolutely: because I have already proven it, and I found that it does not do this in certain bodies without others.
And cautionery with it (gold) is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you make the cautionery in fire from gold, it is not made clear to you when it burns according to the quantity that you want, due to the redness of gold; and when it runs towards it (the fire), and if you add more ignition on top of it, it liquefies in the fire, and turns into layers.
Therefore the craftsman falls into this task (of making cautionery with iron); and because of this, cautionery with iron is more swift and near for us in terms of rightness for the operation.
And I myself have already organized this Chapter on Cauterization, according to chapters; and I have ordered it from the beginning to the end, so that it will be easy for the one seeking what he wants from it.
Chapter II.
Here Cauterization is against the dominion of humidity and coldness on the brain; which are two causes of swelling, and abundance of flow of fluids from the head to the eyes and ears, and abundance of sleep, and pain in teeth, and pain in throat; and universally all illness that comes from coldness, such as paralysis, sodae (a type of seizure), epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ones from these illnesses.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the sick person: that it should be evacuated first with a solution of medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the sick person, and his age, and his custom.
Then instruct him to make radii on his head with a cupping glass. Then have him sit between your hands square, so that he has placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger comes, mark that spot with an unburnt (or uncauterized) mark.
Then heat the cautery in oil: whose form is as follows.
Then place it on the marked spot with the unburnt (or uncauterized) part, descending gradually as your hand is tightened, and you turn it. Then release your hand quickly, and look at the spot.
If you see that a quantity of bone or pus has emerged from the skull, then release your hand. And if not, press your hand again with the iron itself, or with another tool if it becomes cold: until you see the bones which I have told you.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and immerse the cup in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then put the immersed cup over the spot, and leave it until the scab of the fire is destroyed. Then treat it with the ointment tetrapharmacon until it is healed.
They have said that the more an ulcer remains open, the more it discharges pus: wherefore it is better and more helpful.
They said that some should be cauterized down to the bone: and the cautery must be held until something of thickness of the bone is heated.
Then it is scraped after what has been burned from the bone, then it is cured.
And others say that when the cautery reaches the bone, an impression should be made on it for as long as the bone falls out, so that it becomes like the shape of a knife: or an instrument that women place in a small amount of infused alphabet: and they believe that the vapors of the head will expire from this place and the open wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it is cured until it consolidates.
But I do not see these two types of cautery at all, except in certain people according to the way of fear.
And let it be left alone, in my opinion it is better for its own health.
For the head becomes weak from the dissolution of its own natural continuity; as we have testified in other members: and above all when the head of a sick person is naturally weak: and the first species of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore operate with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the head and it persists in an ill person and he uses herbs, chickens, leeches, bloodletting, oils and plasters. And particularly if the head has already been cauterized with a single cautery as we have mentioned and it does not improve with any of these: then consider. If the head of the sick person is strong by nature and not weak, and it finds excessive coldness: then cauterize with another cautery slightly. Then cauterize it over the entire horn of his head with a cautery, so that the skin is not pierced through and a quantity of bone is exposed as we have mentioned. Cauterize it with a single cautery on the occiput of his head, in the place called "vas": it is the place where wind is placed: and pour your oil in this, and do not expose bone. For the sick person finds, on account of that violent pain, it is different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And I shall say that this cautery is in its place: and it must be a cautery with which horns of the head are cauterized, and the occiput more delicately with the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in part of the head or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is treated with cleansing medicines and other treatment as I have said in the division of diseases, and it does not improve completely: then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with the burning medicine, is to take one clove of garlic, peel it and cut off its ends from both sides. Then divide the place of pain at the time with a wide leech, until there is a place beneath the skin where a tooth can be captured.
Insert it (the tooth) beneath the skin there and let it be concealed; then bind above it with a suitable ligature and leave it for fifteen hours and afterwards dissolve it; then extract the garlic clove and wait two or three days; subsequently place the hot iron (cautery) submerged in butter upon it until a pus forms; then treat the place with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to perform this (procedure) with certain burning medications which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, on the Middle Ages.
However, cauterization of this kind is as follows: Hot Iron Cautery, whose shape is this.
It is called a Clavilis because the head of it resembles a nail, and there is something curved on it, and in the middle, there is a small projection.
Then place it on the location and hold your hand; and you turn the iron slowly with speed: and the amount to be burned should be of the thickness of the skin, as its middle part. And lift your hand so that an artery below is not burned and blood flow occurs.
Then immerse the cotton in brine water, and place it on the location and leave it for three days; then immerse the cotton with butter; afterwards care with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this half-skull fracture with the second part of the Cautery. Be careful not to cut an artery in this half-skull fracture, not old ones specifically.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in an old half-skull fracture.
When you treat a half-skull fracture as we have said in the previous cure, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not help; and you see from the disease that what we have said with the first cautery with medicine or with cautery with fire does not suffice, then it is necessary that you burn the Cautery knife, until it whitens after you mark the location of pain with a line, whose length should be half the finger or similar to that; and place your hand aside for a moment, and press it until you cut an artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary that you be careful not to burn the jawbone which moves during chewing, so as not to burn the side or the nerve that moves it, thus causing a spasm.
And this is about the care and caution concerning the flow of blood from a severed artery. When it is cut (the artery), there is fear; especially of him who does not know what he is doing and is not skilled or experienced. Therefore, the operation is abandoned with it first.
And I will come again with a reminder of the regulation for controlling the flow of blood from an artery according to its own method, and in its place in this book.
If you see that this Cautery does not suffice for him because of his sickness, and you see the body of the weak person bearing a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, care for the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish to administer a cautery, do so as we have said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two blades. For cautionery is better this way and more effective.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing an earache.
When pain occurs in the ear due to coldness and is treated with solvents, and the rest of the treatment as we have said in the division, and yet the pain does not subside, then cauterization by fire: and this is what is called Punctum, whose form is as follows.
Then, after the cauterization, make small incisions around the entire ear, as one revolves it: or around both ears if pain is present on both sides. Then, with the cauterizer, extend slightly from the root of the ear after marking the spots with pitch: and let the amount of cauterization be ten punctures on the entire ear, approximately like that.
Then, care for the marked spots until they heal.
Chapter: Method of Cauterization in Strangulation.
Chapter 7.
Strangulation which is treated with cauterization, is not except when it occurs from phlegmatic conditions, as we have said in the division of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for conditions arising from exhaustion or spasm of a nerve.
If treatment of this type of strangulation with herbs, cleansing, gargles does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the weakened person with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, and second slightly below the earlobe, and third at the junction of the two lips.
Place your cauterizer on the weakened side. Since softening does not occur unless in the healthy portion.
The form of cauterization is to cauterize the spot with the cauterizer directly on the end of the upper part of the ear, just below the tip of the skull a little: and another at the earlobe; whose length should be the same as the length of a thumb. Place your hand with the cautery until it is burned to the depth of half the thickness of the skin.
This is the form of Cautery, and it is a species from the knife, whose shape is given below: however, it should not be too fine as you can see; and it must have a knife in it that is not excessively thick.
Then take care of the place with it (the cautery) until it heals.
Chapter on the Method of Cauterizing in Ancient Aphasia.
When apoplexy occurs and your care with what we have said does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him four times with the cautery on all the corners of his head, and with the cautery in the middle of the head, as previously described, and with the cautery on the back of the head, according to what has been said; and the method of cauterizing should be as previously described.
Also, it is cauterized with the Cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and this is the final remedy.
Then take care of it with what has been said before.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in drink there are first of all large amounts of hyssop, and cleansing pills for the brain.
Then shave completely the head of the sick person, and place on his occiput ointment made from sinapis (mustard) described in the treatise of ointments; place it on him frequently.
For this is the method of cautery; and make it according to the order as I said there.
If therefore he is healed by that, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauterizations on the back part of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and place between every cauterization a thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cautery, with that which preceded.
If however you wish an additional treatment, and the sick person can endure it; then make a cauterization in the middle. And if you wish an additional treatment: then cauterize him over two horns (i.e., temples).
Then care for it until he is healed; and let the cautery be anointed according to the shape that was given before.
Chapter on method of cauterizing in Paralysis, and softening (i.e., treatment for paralysis).
Chapter X.
It is necessary to proceed with the cleaning of the head with hyssop and as I said before.
Then shave completely the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize him with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over all the horn of the head, and over the back part of it, and over three on the neck.
If in sickness there is a need for softening of the body by more than these, and the sick person can endure it, and the sickness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauterizations on the vertebrae, and the last one with a cautery until he burns most from his skin, and loosen your hand. Then take care of [the patient], until he is cured: and so cauterize with oil.
On the method of cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to cleanse the brain of the patient first, with the herbs mentioned earlier, and with the remainder of the treatment as we have described in the division. When the patient is seriously ill or is intolerant of the application of drugs.
If the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medicine, then administer gargarisma, and cleansing mastication, before that, for many days with good food.
Then shave the patient's head, then cauterize him with a single cautery in the middle of the skull, according to what was described earlier: and with another cautery on his occiput, and over all the horn of his skull. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries mentioned in treating paralysis, and soften the body on the spondylus of the neck, and the spine: and let the cautery be olive oil as described earlier.
If the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery, according to this method.
On the method of cauterization for melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with the cauteries, which we mentioned in the presence of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivities leading to melancholy and the body is damp, then give him a drink that purifies his brain, according to what was said earlier in division: then shave the head of the sick man, and make afterwards a well-made tourniquet from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and let the sick man sitting square be held from all sides.
Then apply a liniment. And it is more suitable with old olive oil butter. And heat it over a gentle fire, using a measured temperature that the finger can bear when it is inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and let it be until it cools down.
Do this to the sick man every week once, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize him by making small holes in many places of his body, apart from holding the cautery in your hand: it should smell good.
For this type of cautery dampens the brain with its quality.
Then place on him a cloth soaked in butter or chicken fat.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in water flowing to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are informed of the origin of water in the eye through the signs that were said earlier in division, then begin and give the sick man a drink, with what purifies his head.
And keep him away from all moisture, and make him sit in a bath for some days of fasting.
Then order him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his own head. Then cauterize it over two temples with two cauteries, if there is no opening for the descent of water in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an opening for water in one eye: and cut off with the cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width like the temples: and avoid bleeding.
If you see something from it (the affected area), then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes it (the affected area) is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two cauteries brought to the extreme.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in the eyes (anciently).
When the tears of the eyes are ancient and continuous: and they are over veins and arteries that are manifest on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from an excess of cold, phlegmatic humors: then cauterize with the same cautery as was narrated in the opening of water descent, cauterize in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries over two temples, and with two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if additional help is needed, then cauterize it (the affected area) on all sides carefully around the eye, over the outer edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in nasal foulness.
When you are treating it, as we said in division, and the medication does not help: then hurry, and give infirmocochias for three nights in drink; afterwards shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with the oil-filled cautery. Then cauterize it with two cauteries and a clawed cautery, over the two eyebrows under the hair slightly.
And beware of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the clawed cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it over the two eyebrows slightly in every part; and they will extend from both temples; and let the entire length of the cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not place your hand with the cautery at the very end, but rather according to the amount that is burnt by the third eyelash.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn inward, pricking the eye.
The cautery is in this way according to two methods: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, command the sick person to release his hairs beforehand, if he is among those who clean them, until they are long and even. If the hairs prick him at their origin: then bind his eyes with a plaster, so that they do not move, until they grow out.
When they are born and equalized, then place the head of the weak in your lap; afterwards mark on the eyelids of his eyes with wax, mark it like the shape of a myrtle leaf; let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then pour boiled wool into goat's milk or psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then heat the cautery, whose shape is as follows: (There are no further details provided on the shape of the cautery.)
Then cauterize slowly in several places according to the mark you made, until the surface of the skin burns and appears like the shape of a myrtle leaf entirely.
And the sign of your health is that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and hairs rising at the point of the eye.
Then raise your hand then, and let him go for three days.
Then place the wool over it with butter until the eschar is removed. Then take care of him with an ointment until he is healed.
If any hair returns after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then cauterize that place again, just as you did before.
If there are hairs below it: then cauterize it until the hair grows back to its natural place and is equalized so that it does not poke the eye.
You must instruct the weak person to pluck out his hairs until they grow long and are equalized. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from parchment.
Then take from known soap and from unslaked lime each a pound or about that amount; then grind them together with good pressure, and make it quickly so it does not become cold. Then spread it out on a piece of parchment that you have made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over one or both eyelids. Place a cup containing soaked cotton wool in the albumen of an egg, and have the head of the sick person be in your lap.
Place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly. You move it whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, for its bite is like fire.
While it continues to feel this bite that it senses from the medicine, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
Then look to see if the eyelid is rising, as it rises when heated by fire or cut, this is good: and if not, then repeat the application of medicine on the place where the medicine does not press or discolor, until your operation is even and the eye contracts.
Then put the cotton wool over it with butter until the burnt skin is removed. Then treat him with diaphine ointment or another one until he is cured.
It is necessary for you to keep the last protection during the operation so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes softened after days and some hair falls into the eye from it, then repeat the medicine on that place which has become soft from the eyelid, as you did at first. Then take care of him until he is cured.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore your consideration should be such that the path of righteousness is not concealed from him who is devoted to this art.
On the method of cauterization for a lacrimal fistula.
When treating a fistula, as mentioned earlier in the classification of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then it is necessary to cauterize it in this manner.
Command the sick man to place his head in your lap, and let one of his attendants hold his head thus between his hands so that it is not moved or shaken with his head.
Then place a cotton soaked in oil or in the mucilage of psyllium on his eye: then hold a cautery iron over it whose shape is this.
Let it be concave like the form of a swan's feather from one end, with which the cautery iron is made: and if you wish it to penetrate to the other end as well, or if you wish it to be raised up in this manner.
However, this concave shape is better for your use.
Then press the fistula open if it is open and drain the pus from it, and excise it: but if it is not open, then you should open it and drain the pus out of it.
Then place the cautery iron on it when it has been heated very strongly.
And hold your hand near the cautery iron from the eye towards the nose, so that your hand does not wander or shake the sick man: and place the cautery iron on the eyelid fat, and destroy it.
If you therefore reach the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be good. But if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice, as needed; and let it lie for three days.
Then place cotton with butter on it, and treat it with an ointment for ulcers until it heals.
If it exceeds forty days and is not cured: then place sharp corrosive medicine upon it until the bone appears; and shave it according to its own chapter.
And here is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some early authors have described. Direct yourself to the location of the fistula and find it; then place a thin cannula (camahan) in the fissure itself, namely, a fine tube whose form is as follows. Pour into it an amount of drachmas made from melted lead, and hold the cannula firmly with a good retainer, so that the weak one does not move at all, lest the molten lead runs to his eye.
It is necessary that you place a warm poultice on the weak one's eye, either in egg white or in water.
For lead burns the location of the fistula and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed, as we have said by cauterization and treatment, that is good. If not, then it is necessary to make a nasal opening and redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to its own place.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in facial fissures.
Many times, fissures occur on the lip, which are called Pilae, and especially in children's lips.
When you treat these fissures, as we have said in the division of diseases, and treatment does not help, then use small hot cautery (cauterium) with a knife, according to this shape.
And let its indentation be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it hastily into the fissures while the hot cautery reaches the depth of the fissure.
Then take care of him with pitch, until he is healed.
On the method of cauterization for a mouth fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gums, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and breaks, later it becomes old and pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then take care of the fistula itself and do not apply treatment to it, then it is necessary that fire cauterization be done according to the quantity that can enter the fistula. Then introduce the fire into the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron heated reaches its depth and end: do this once or twice.
Then take care of it afterwards, as I said regarding treatment, until it is cured.
If therefore the pus separates and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the rotten bone according to what comes in its head.
On the method of cauterization on softened gums and teeth.
When the gum becomes soft due to moisture, and the teeth move, and treating it with medicine does not help; then put the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then take a cautery, whose shape will come later, so that you place the Cannula on the tooth; and insert the heated Cauterium quickly into it: and hold your hand for a short while, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And clean your hand; then repeat the cautery as often as you wish.
Then let the sick person rinse his mouth with water and salt, and hold it for an hour; and then spit it out.
The tooth moves to become firm, and the softened gum contracts, and the corruption of moisture dries up.
Method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
When the tooth pain is due to coldness or there is coldness itself, or worms, and treatment with medicine does not help; then cautery is done in two ways: either cautery with butter, or cautery with fire.
Cauterium however with butter is, that you receive the waxed butter and boil it in an iron cauldron or copper vessel. Then take a cup and fold it over the end of the wound. Then immerse it (the cup) in melted butter; place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools down; then repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or a cup in cold butter; place it on the painful tooth and put hot iron on top of it until the heat reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
The cauterization with fire is done using a copper pipe or an iron pipe. There should be something thick (a barrier) in the body to prevent the sharpness of the fire from reaching the weak bone.
Then apply a hot iron (cautery) with the appropriate shape to the tooth; hold it until it cools down.
Do this several times because the pain will gradually disappear, either on the same day or on another day.
And it is necessary to fill the weakened bone with good butter during the application of the cautery and hold it for an hour; then spit it out.
This is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize using any shape you wish, provided that it is possible; this is the form of the pipe (cannula).
Chapter on how to cauterize ulcers.
When ulcers are caused by phlegm and cold humors, and do not respond to medication, and you wish to treat them quickly, then use a concave hot iron (cautery) with this shape:
Having two open ends so that smoke exits from one end at the Cautery and place it burning once on top of the ulcer; and if you need it, put it again, until it reaches the depth of the ulcer.
If the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then leave it for three days and place a covered cup filled with butter on top of it until the burn caused by fire is removed.
Then treat it with a tooth ointment until the form of the canal is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in laryngitis and constriction of breath.
When dampnesss attack the channel of the lung and especially when it is accompanied by coldness of constitution, then the sick person should be evacuated first with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the neck at the root of the throat in a depressed place and be careful not to reach the throat with the cautery nor the skin unless something from it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the joint of the neck at the end of the hip bone and let the cautery be a nail as described earlier.
Then treat it with what was previously mentioned until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the lung and cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are from cold dampness, and the sick person does not have fever, nor phthisis, and the illness is old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, smooth, empty places. And cauterize it with another one in the middle of the chest between two breasts and let the cautery be a canal as described earlier.
If your treatment is cauterization by puncturing with a cautery called "Punctum," which shape was described earlier in the procedure for ear pain; and if there are punctures from thirty punctures up to others.
Then heal it with that method (the cauterization) until it heals.
Now let the cautery have three branches in this shape. Therefore, when you use the cautery, alleviate (the pain) with it as if you were using three separate cauteries.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the arm is dislocated due to the cause of humidity and it does not reposition itself within an hour after its dislocation, until this becomes a habit for it, then it should be dislocated again by a slight movement that occurs as we have already testified; afterwards, in such case, you should immediately restore the dislocation. Then the sick person lies down on his back or on a healthy side. Then loosen the skin that is inside the Titillicus (the affected area) towards the upper part with your left hand fingers; and if it is connected and dislocated towards the internal parts.
Then take a cautery with two prongs. This is its shape:
Then cauterize the skin, until it penetrates it on the other side, and the figure of cauterization with four cauteries will come.
And sometimes the cauterization is made with a cautery having three points, for this reason the figure of the cauterization will be with six cauteries: and they are the points according to the delicacy of the skin touched.
And this is the form of the cautery having three points.
And sometimes one is added to this method, for this reason there are eight cauteries.
Then place on top of the cautery split rods with salt. Then make the patient rest in peace so that a limb is not moved at any time until it recovers.
And if the dislocation is towards the upper part (shoulder), and this rarely occurs, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a pointed cautery or many cauteries poking.
For union strengthens, and moisture is removed; and the sick person recovers.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture occur in the stomach, until it expels itself from its composition, and catarrh multiplies towards it, and persistent methods of treatment, and this does not help; then the patient should lie on his back with his legs extended, and his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries: one cautery in the size of a cochlea of the breast, another cautery like a nail, and two cauteries below the sides of one cautery's base, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And stretch it between each (part) so they do not join, when pus forms.
Let the depth of the cautery be the size of two fingers breadth of the skin.
Let the figure of the cauteries be as such without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape, let the cautery which is used for this have the shape of a circle according to this shape.
The stomach is cauterized by pricking it with a cautery that presses against it; and it is as if signs are placed on the stomach according to the size you wish with encaustic: then cauterize the place with the cautery for the point, then care for it with the treatment that preceded until it heals.
Paragraph on the method of cauterizing Epirrhus (Epirus).
When there is pain in the liver due to coldness and moistness, or from gross flatulence, until it expels its superfluous excretion through its natural discharge, and the patient does not get better by what was said above: then the patient must lie down on his back on his neck, and mark three cauteries with encaustic according to this figure, and the same size below Epirrhus where the elbow of a man reaches; and let the space between each cautery be the size of a finger; and let the cautery be as long as the body; and do not press your hand too much with the cautery.
Let its (the cautery's) size which is heated be the thickness of the skin plus half of it; and let the patient stand on his feet.
If it is not standing, then let it lie (down), which already extended its legs, and raised its arms.
This is the form of cautery.
And indeed it is possible for you to use this cautery with a sharp surgical knife when subtlety and wisdom are present in your art.
Be careful that you do not advance too far in cauterization so that the thickness of the skin is burned completely, for then the entire body is burnt and it reaches the bowels; because there the skin is delicate, therefore know this.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When there is a discharge and the desire to know if this abscess is in the liver flesh or its membrane; then, if it is in the liver flesh, a mild pain and heaviness occurs without sharpness; but if it is in the liver membrane, with pain there is strong sharpness; and you see that the treatment of it has already exhausted the doctors.
Therefore, the sick person must lie on their neck. Then place the position of the abscess with the hot iron; then heat the cautery similar to a small rod. And this is its shape. And use the cautery with it until the entire skin is burned and reaches the pus sac, until all the pus comes out; then take care of the wound by treating the discharge, until it heals.
And it is not appropriate to use this cautery method unless one's passion for the art of medicine is prolonged; and through whose hands these diseases frequently occur with experience; then he may dare on such an operation.
But it is better to let go of it (the abscess), in my opinion.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing pleurisy.
The ancients said, cautery with the roots of Aristolochia for a cold pleurisy in this manner. And it is to receive from the dried roots of Aristolochia, one longer root which can be found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one hot iron in what is between the joining of the collarbone with the neck, and with two small irons under the chin a little below where the beard is.
And with two irons also in what is between the fifth and sixth ribs a little below towards the back; and with another iron in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three irons from the back; one in what is between the scapulas; and with two irons on the sides of the chest, the lower iron being what is between the scapulas.
And you must not press your hand with the iron, but rather let it smell freely of the skin.
And some ancients have said that there are humans who use an iron similar to a ray and burn it, and push it inside what is between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and let pus come out; as we said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with iron is feared that either the weak person will die immediately or a fistula occurs at the place which does not heal.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the spleen, Head XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we said in the treatment of diseases and your treatment is not effective, then cautery on it is in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of them is to make three or four cautery points, arranging them along the length of the spleen according to the shape of Epate's cauteries, whose preceding figure it is.
And let the size between each cautery be that of a finger, or more or less.
The method of cauterization on the liver, which I mentioned in the liver cautery, shall be equal.
Do not press your hand with the cautery, and let the patient be weak lying on his back.
Another method of cauterization is: holding the cautery with two prongs, as I said in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and peel off the skin that is directly on the spleen, where the arm of the weak person arrives; and your peeling should be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two prongs heated very hot until they penetrate the skin from the other side; then remove the cautery; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
Then take care of the cautery after you release it to emit pus for many days; for it is more helpful than the other methods that preceded it in treatment.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
A cautery does not fall in dropsy unless it is properly applied.
When treating a dropsy with the methods of treatment that I mentioned in the division, and if the treatment is not helpful, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one on the stomach, another on the liver, another on the spleen, two behind the loins, and one on the breast and another on the stomach; and the size of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery, so that it may emit pus over a long time.
And do not evacuate the weak from treatment after cautery, for it is necessary that two intentions be gathered to him: and healing will hasten towards him with God's help.
The form of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be clavils, according to its preceding form; and the one with which the back is cauterized should be oliuaris, according to its preceding form.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When they are amputated in hydropicus and filled with citrine water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the nocrati, which is between the auricular and anular; then lift your hand with the cautery, do not twist it; then lift your hand; do not touch it again.
The water of citrine will boil, and let the cautery be in this shape.
Then make two cauteries for each leg, and let the cautery be with the end of a small cautery at the end; and let the cautery be along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other lower by about half the length of the leg; and over the entire hip, place two cauteries; and release the open cautery without treatment for a long time, so that something boils out of it; then treat it with the rest as we have said.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in the solution of the abdomen.

When the solution of the abdomen is due to cold and humidity, until the powers retained and digestive ones, which are in the stomach and intestines, weaken; and it is treated with methods of treatment, but does not heal; and you see the weak enduring a cautery with excessive strength, then cauterize it with a large cautery over the stomach, according to what was preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle clavils cautery; and a large cautery or two cauteries over the alcatin above the alhosos.

The treatment is advancing, whose benefit is not in error.

When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, either one and they are from thick, cold or corrupted fluids, which cannot be cured as we have said in the division, then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower part of the back of the hipbone slightly triangularly under the almeidati, and cauterize under the navel about two fingers.

Chapter XXXVII.

On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter XXXVIII.
If the sick person does not obey the incision and operation as we have described earlier, and is afraid of it, perhaps he will heal with a cautionery.
When there occurs a fistula, and it becomes old, pus runs out of it, and the surrounding tissues are corrupted. Therefore, it is appropriate to examine it with a thin probe. Then recognize the depth of it using a probe.
Then apply fire cautery which is similar to a rod. Then you introduce yourself with the fire cautery into the fistula and determine the depth where it was inserted.
And repeat the cautery on it until all the corrupted tissues are burned away, once or twice or thrice, according to your need.
And be careful not to burn the nerve or large vein if there is one; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or intestine, then beware of these places altogether.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshly place; and consider that it does not penetrate.
Then care for the place until it heals.
If the place is covered and the material removed from it and it remains for a long time; then know that it has healed completely.
And if the material is not removed from it, then know that it penetrates or there is a deep corruption of bone in it, or something similar from those which will be remembered in their places.

On the Cauterization of the Anus in Dislocation.
When the mucous discharges flow towards Ancha's plaster and cause it to leave its place: and a sign of this is that the leg extends over the other when they are compared one against the other: and there is an empty spot found at the dislocation in it.

On the method of cauterizing in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in Ancha's plaster and the cause is coldness and humidity: and it is treated with what was said above, but the treatment does not help and it worsens: then it is necessary to dissolve the weak part from thick humors with fetid pills or artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cauterization is according to two methods: either with a cautery with medicines that drive it out, or with fire.
The cautery with fire is in many ways.
One of them is to cauterize over Ancha's plaster with three triangular cauteries in this shape. Make a good or bad depth for them. Let the space between every cautery of any size be that of a finger's breadth; and let the cautery be made of oil.
Sometimes, a cautery is made in the middle of the anus itself. Why are there four cauteries?
If you wish to cauterize with a ring, the shape of which preceded in the cauterization of an anus dislocation, let it be one: so that the ring encloses the entire anus.
Burn the thickness of the skin all over.
This is the method for cautery in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the anus itself and does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, at the place indicated by the patient where the pain is, and with your cautery four fingers' length towards the outer part: let the cautery be a knife-shaped one.
Let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends near the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where the patient indicates with a cautery point, three, four or more if necessary.
If he indicates that the pain is under the knee turned towards the leg, then cauterize it there with a knife-shaped cautery.
Be careful with all your cauteries that you do not burn a nerve or the major artery, and attract harm to the patient through it, or cause contracture.
I myself have already seen one and another of those who cauterized above the calf, and burnt in the cauterization, and the leg swelled up until it reached the foot, and was perforated completely, and the whole foot rotted: then there followed a rupture of the stomach, and death afterwards.
If pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize both according to this method.
And some wise men said in the cauterization of the anus, whose cauterization this is the method. Make a similar object of iron, whose diameter is half the width of the palm; and it should be at its place according to the size of the knuckle, or slightly less; and within that small object, there should be another small object.
And there should be a space that is between every small object according to the size of a knuckle; and the small objects should be open on both sides; and their height should be like a knuckle, or two knuckles; and make handles of iron properly fitted in the small objects.
Then it is heated in fire until it glows and sparks; then it should be placed on the cushion of the anus resting weakly on the healthy side. Cauterize therefore with three round cauteries at once.
Then, let it be for three days. Then pack it with butter; and let the open wound remain for many days. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says: in this way of cauterization, O sons, we have not been sufficiently accustomed to it due to the fear of its appearance; and for that reason, we find few who dare upon it.
However, it is one of the good cauteries for him who can endure it, and it has a place in that condition.
The cautery with stimulating medicines is to make two small objects having a perforated armillary sphere, into which descends the key of its door from brass or iron, the length of the wall; whose height should be two knuckles, or as if they themselves.
And let there be a space that is between each quantity of the finger's thickness, and let it be open below and above; and let it contain each other in this manner.
Then place it on a boxwood plank, with the weak one lying on its healthy side. And press your hand on the boxwood plank strongly. Then pour water into two circles between them which is heated slightly by fire, and hold it for the amount of an hour; let the weak one bear the bite of it, and its burning, for he himself has found that biting like fire until the biting stops.
Then scrape your hand with a tool and remove warm water from the plank along with sweet water; then let it be for three days.
And place butter on it until the blackness of the burning is removed; and let it be for some days, and pus will run out from it. For it is the ultimate treatment.
Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg: make a setting for it in that which contains water, according to what you have made on the plank equally.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it in the treatment of rectifying remedies. Take alkali and powdered unburnt lime, mix them in equal parts; grind each of them and put them into a new pot, the bottom of which is pierced with a small hole according to the size that the radius enters; and put another pot underneath it which is covered; throw over the alkali and lime from sweet water, so that each of them immerse by a finger depth; then press them with good pressure using your hand; and let the pot be until the acid water goes down in the bottom of the earthenware pot.
Then gather all that water and pour it over another leg: and boil, until it returns.
For indeed, it will then be very strong and sharp, which is given in many operations of medicine, and in the cauterization of other members. Because it effects the operation of fire itself.
And among the medicines with which cauteries are made, such as alum and tesisie, and honey from the nut tree, and chalk with soap, so that each be mixed together. (Â¶ is a paragraph symbol)
And Galen himself, in his narrative, reported a cure of a certain man from among the ancients, who was healed of pain in the anus and the sciatic vein: and he praised it very highly. And he said that it did not require another cure, and because he was healed from a single application, until he reported that perhaps he himself entered the bath and came out of it already healed.
And it is to be taken from the green seed of seitaragus: and if green seed is not found, dry one should be taken, fresh: and grind it very much with a little fat, and place it on the anus, where there is pain, or leg, or in the hip: and tie it and let it stay for the quantity of three hours, or as much as it feels weak from the heat of the cauterization. Then introduce it into a bath.
When his body becomes warm, introduce him into the sun. For pain departs, and it heals.
And know that no one should use a cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who said that the feces of goats, when it is cauterized with them on the sciatic vein, add it: and the cautery is made in this manner. Take flax, and let it be soaked in ancient oil, and place it on a deep place which is between the toe of the foot and the heel, and closer to the heel.
Then take dry goat dung, and ignite it until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the flax, and let it rest until it goes out. Repeat that procedure. Do not cease to do that until sensation reaches the marrow, and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called Vaccine cautery.
Chapter on the Cauterization of Back Pain.
Whenever there is pain in the back due to multiple causes, either from an accident, or a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, due to the influx of cold and moist matter; and cauterization does not apply except in this single case which is made by the influx of cold matter.
Therefore, after the evacuation of the sick with fetid pills and similar things, they should be placed on the back where there is pain, three lines wide according to the palm of the hand, after marking them with encaustic in every line of five cauteries or more according to the amount that comes from the strength of the patient; and the cauterization should be done with cauterion puncti.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries together with the middle clavile cautery, in this manner.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing humpback deformity.
This disease often occurs in young children.
The sign of the beginning of this deformity in children is that it happens above them when they breathe deeply during elevation and movement; and you find at the end of the vertebrae of the back and their knots, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When you see that [thing], and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is in the shape of a circle.
Take the cautery over the whole mussel shell equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the mussel shell with a pointed cautery, take two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Then care for that place until it heals as we have said.
Beware not to administer the cautery on a hump which is caused by a spasm of the nerve.
On the method of cauterization for gout and joint pains.
When the pains of joints are caused by cold humidity that flows into any part of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary among physicians to call this gout properly.
When gout caused by cold is treated with methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then cautery removes them.
And it is that you should cauterize [the affected area] after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauteries, and let the cautery be Olivary.
And if you need points on the sole of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it on the entire knee with three or four cauteries from all sides, with this same cautery of Clavius.
But if you require more of this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin.
If the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what was said in its own chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then make incisions around the joints of the fingers, as two lines are rolled up.
If pain persists in the fingers, then pierce them all over every knot and on the back of the hand.
If pains rise after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate a sick person by good regimen or by taking medicine. For if the regimen is good and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with this cautery aid from God.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing ruptures.
If there is a rupture in the groins and the intestine or spermatic cord descends towards the testicle, which is beginning to appear nearby: then it is necessary to order the sick person to fast on his own day. And let him use the laxatives so that feces will descend from his belly.
Then let him sit on your hands upon his back: and command him to hold his breath until it comes out or appears pus or intestine.
Then put your fingers on him and sign with wax under the wound on his neck, with a mark whose end resembles half of a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then heat the cautery, which has this shape, until it turns white, and throw sparks at it. Then pull the intestine or pus into its hollow. Then let the servant place his hand on the spot to keep the intestine from coming out: and you have already opened between the legs of the sick man, and placed a pan under him, and one servant is serving at his legs, and another at his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. Hold him until you follow the bone with it: or hold him again with another instrument, if you do not reach the bone with it in the first attempt.
And observe carefully that the intestine does not come out during your cautery work, lest you burn him and something happens to the sick person or great harm.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your operation is of no use.
The cautery for children must be delicate, according to their measure.
Then treat with ointments, until he is healed.
The sick man should lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is healed.
It is necessary to put food for him according to the length of his healing time, so that his stomach is softened and nothing comes out from it during the operation or evacuation.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a properly made ligament and hold him for another forty days.
And it should be diminished by labor, and filled with food and drink, and vehement voices.
When using this regimen, healing occurs in its entirety.
I will say the cure of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the remaining abdomen and are new, and the force is not added, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and that which is burned should be as the third part of it from then on. Then cure itself, when I said so: do not add anything.
And it was said by some first ones: to cauterize the rupture with a triangular cautery according to this shape.
After it is signed with pitch and a line is placed that is across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line downwards. And place your hand in the middle with the nail-cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Chapter on the manner of cauterizing in pains caused by fall or blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When it happens in certain limbs due to a fall or blow and the pain persists for a long time, and no cure occurs with medicines: then it is necessary that it should be cauterized with the puncture cautery.
And let the cautery be for all members according to its size and its weakness, and its power, and the looseness of the torsion, and the pain from it.
If it is cured by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then apply another cautery on top of it.
Because it is the custom of these pains that they are changed from one member to another nearby. Therefore it is necessary that you follow them with a cautery until the sick one is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes greatly benefited by cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that is caused by decomposition of phlegm and black bile; therefore consider cauterizing it.
If the leprosy is beginning and you have treated it as we said in the division, and it does not subside or stabilize; and you fear that corruption will spread over his entire complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, known as the fontanelle, and the second lower towards the forehead at the end of the hairline, and two above the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally press your hand with the cautery slightly until it makes a smaller impression on the bone, and the cortexes separate from it; in order to alleviate the expiration of gross vapors from it, and cauterize with the cautery also over the spleen, according to what has preceded.
But if the leprosy is already spread over the sick person, and it appears clearly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries which we said in the head, and with a cautery over the extremity of the nose, and with two cauteries over the cheeks, and with two cauteries over the spondyles of the neck, and six over the spondyles of the back, and one large over the alhahosos at the base of the tail and one on it, in the almeidat: and two over the ankles; namely over all the ankle with one, and two over the knees, and two over the elbows, and two over the wrists, and two over the softnesses of his chest: and cauterize him over all the joints, from the joints of his fingers of his hands to his feet: and cauterize over all the calcanei of his feet, and the follia of his hands.
Beware lest you burn the nerves that are above the last calcaneus.
And sometimes cauterized by a cautery on the ear lobe, and another on the belly of the stomach, and another on the epigastrium.
Know that the more you apply the cautery, the more it is helpful, and the more it conforms.
Know that the sick do not find pain in the cautery as the healthy do; therefore because his body is already stunned.
It is necessary that the cauteries should be of size and weight according to the members and joints; according to the kinds of tools that preceded them.
Then care for the cautery with flour of herbs and honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in stupor.
When a limb is numbed and treated with medicines, oils, plasters, but does not heal, then cauterize the numbed limb with cauteries, according to the size of the limb or its smallness.
Let your cautery penetrate slightly into the skin's thickness. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And sometimes when cauterization is performed for numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, in the joints of the back at the exits of nerves that move that limb: the numbness is removed.
But let him not presume to do this, unless he is wise in the anatomy of limbs and the exit of nerves moving the body.
Title LXI.
When Albaraz (a type of ulcer or lesion) hardens and does not yield to any medicine: then cauterize it deeply with a cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and the color changes.
Then treat it with a mixture of grain from herbs and lentils with rose oil, arnoglossus leaves, dove blood, and frog blood: each ingredient in equal parts: mix all these together, soak them on a cloth, and apply them to the place until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterization in Cancer.
When a cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as it is usually done.
The wise ones said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
It does not seem good to me (that is, to cauterize in the middle): I fear that it would ulcerate; and I have already seen this happen many times.
It is better to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we said; or with several cauteries.
Chapter on the manner of cauterization in Adubelati.
Chapter LIII. When someone has an Adubelati (a kind of tumor) that is slow in maturation, or because it is caused by excess, or because the person is old and weak, or because of time, and wishes to hasten the maturation of the Adubelati, then cauterize around its circumference with several small cauteries, puncturing it. Then let it be. For it will hasten with the maturation itself.
If you wish to perforate it (the tumor) with a cautery, then heat the cautery with fire, and this is its shape.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be weak, so that its course may be alleviated with purifying.
Then care for it until it heals.
Chapter on the manner of cauterization in a rotting tumor.
Chapter LIIII.
Corrosion is not but corruption walking in a limb and consuming it; just as fire eats dry wood.
If you see corrosion in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then apply much cautery, small and large clamps according to what is appropriate for the place where there is corrosion.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you root out the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains deep within.
Then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized places ground sulfur with oil until all scabs are removed and all corruption is completely gone.
Then treat it with ointments that stimulate flesh growth.
If you see after three days that flesh is growing in a healthy manner without corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on what remains from the corrupted places.
And corrosion is treated sometimes with strong medicine. But it arises in place of cautery itself.
Nevertheless, cautery with fire is quicker help; and I have already said that cauterization of it with strong medicine is used in division; therefore take it there when you need it.
[Section title] On Cauterizing in Nails and Warts.
Chapter 50.
Often occurs in the lower parts of the feet this disease: and it is a large, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And there is indeed cautionery for them according to two modes: cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
As for the cauterization with fire, it should be done as follows: make a hollowed-out cautery similar to the beak of a vulture from iron, according to its size so that it contains a nail from all sides; and let it have sharp edges.
Then place the heated one on the nail. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply ointments of forest malva crushed with salt; and leave the ointment on it at night. For it will be rooted out from its roots.
Then care for the place with a salve made of fresh flesh until it heals.
If they have not been converted [changed?], and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet: then administer cauterization with hot water; and it is, that you take a tube made from copper or iron or from the beak of a vulture; and place it on the nail or on the cuticle. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube; hold your hand and rotate it slightly so that the tip of the tube presses on the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail; and let the patient wait for a while under the pressure of the hot water for about an hour.
Then release it, for the nail will be rooted out along with its roots.
Follow it thus one after another, until you reach upon all who are from them in the body.
Then care for them when they are eradicated, with that which generates flesh from unguents.
On the method of cauterizing in tremor.
When trembling occurs to someone due to cold in a nerve, or quartan fever, or another reason: then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauteries, or five on the back of a dorsal spondyle, and between every spondyle with a cautery, and in its chest with a cautery, and above its stomach with a cautery.
For trembling quiets down when cauterized with oil, and hastens the health of cold illness.
On the method of cauterizing albathir.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes, in the body, albathirs (abscesses) that are foul, i.e., pustules, which are produced by corrupted matter, are expelled.
Therefore, when they appear first, it is necessary to cauterize on every head of the pustule with a subtle cautery and with myrtle wood whose end is set alight with fire. Or with the root of aristolochia (long). Or with a lenticular cautery.
And sometimes cauteries are applied to adomenes (the abdomen) at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; and they do not increase; and excess is broken, making them, and healed from them.
Nevertheless, it must be done after evacuation with phlebotomy (bloodletting).
On the method of cauterizing during blood flow from an artery in a wound.
Multiple times occurs the flow of blood from an artery, which is cut near a wound, this happens externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or cauterization of a member, and similar to these: and it becomes difficult to separate it.
When this happens to anyone, then immediately place your finger on the orifice of the artery, and press hard upon it; so that the blood is held under your finger, and nothing comes out from there.
Then place a small oil lamp cautery on the fire, and many of them, in large number; and blow upon them until they are very hot.
Then take one of them, small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is broken; and place the cautery on the vein, after you remove your finger quickly; hold the cautery until the blood separates.
If the blood is forced out when you remove your finger from the orifice of the artery, and extinguish the cautery, then immediately take another cautery, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore do not cease to perform this with one after another until the blood separates.
And beware, lest you burn the nerve which is there, and some other evil befall the weak man.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to separate it; especially because the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is pulled out, its extremities contract and the blood separates. Or it is tied with a strong thread. Or medicines are placed upon it, which have the property to separate blood; and it is pressed with a suitable tourniquet.
Whoever administers amputation with a ligature, and constriction with cloth, or placement of burning things, and similar [procedures], does not fully heal it, except rarely.
If it happens to someone and the doctor is not present nor medicine available: then let him begin with the positioning of the index finger over the opening of the vein itself, as we have said, and its tightening very much, until the blood is blocked from above the wound, and on the artery. And the finger shall not be removed, above it with cold water of violent cold always, until the blood freezes, thickens, and is cut off.
And meanwhile let him consider in that, what needs cautery, or medicine.

And for this reason, caution must be greater, because in the operation which is in this chapter, evacuation with blood often occurs, with which life remains open at the opening of the vein, or incision over an abscess, or the opening of drainage, or treatment of a wound, or extraction of arrows, or incision over a stone, and similar [issues]: from all of these the tremor and fear occur, and death occurs in many of them.
And I warn you not to let it fall upon you where there is hesitation, for sometimes in this art modes of humans fall upon you with the modes of weaknesses. For there is one who gets angry with his illness and death is easy for him; because of the vehemence he finds from his weakness and the length of his wickedness. Chapter on the treatment of water accumulating in children's heads.
Chapter 1:
Know that this weakness often occurs in children at birth or when the midwife squeezes the child's head without ease.
