Sometimes it also occurs due to hidden causes which are not known.
I myself have never seen this sickness in any but children, and death followed all whom I saw of them; for that reason it seemed to me that the operation should be abandoned in such a case.
I myself have seen a child whose head was full of water and whose head swelled every day until he could not sit up himself, because of the size of his head; and the moisture increased until he died.
This moisture, it accumulates between skin and bone or it accumulates under the bone above the forehead.
And the operation in that case, if there is moisture between skin and bone and the abscess is small, then a slit should be made in the middle of the head, one fissure wide enough, its length like two knuckles, until the moisture runs out.
And this is a form of trepanation (spatulum).
If the moisture is more increased and the abscess is larger, then make these two slits according to this form.
If the moisture is under the bone and there is a sign that you see that the skull openings are wide open from all sides; and water sinks when you press it with your hand towards the inside, and it is not hidden from you, then make three slits in the middle of the head according to this method.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture. Then suture the slits with bandages and lint. Then apply oil and wine to it until the fifth day.
Then loosen the sutures, take care of the wound with ointments and salves.
Do not omit to tie the head with equality. Feed the ill man with dry food of little moisture until he is strengthened and cured.
Another method of incision is to consider where the size of the abscess appears, and the collection of water.
Whenever it is more, either in the head, or in the skull, or in the right, or in the left.
Therefore advance with an incision where it appears to you that there is an abscess and fill with water: and cut it as much as possible.
And observe, do not cut an artery, and let the flow of blood occur, and let the sick person die from that flow with the evacuation of moisture.
Section on the incision of arteries that are behind the ears.
Chapter II.
When catarrh occurs to someone's eyes or chest, and it grows old and medical treatment does not help: then the final cure is more in that, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when one wants to cut them (the arteries), it is necessary for the sick person to shave his head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick person press his neck with any cloth of his. Then consider where the vein throbs. And these places are the places that are depressed behind each ear: and they are rarely hidden except in some men.
Then mark both (the places) with pitch: and cut one on each side with a spoon-shaped knife, the incision reaching to the bone: and make this opening through the width of the head.
And if you want, insert the spoon-shaped knife under the artery, and cut it towards the top with the incision.
Let the length of the incision be as long as two fingers joined together.
For when the vein is cut, blood flows out with a pulsating discharge, which jumps to the inside with frequent leaps.
If the artery is not visible to the senses, then it is necessary for measurements from the ear to determine the amount of space of three fingers. Then mark with pitch and cut until the bone.
And what must be released from the blood is about 6 ounces, perhaps you will release more or less from it. Entire this according to the quantity that appears to you from the strength of the sick person and the filling of the artery.
Then consider about the wound. Then if there is something left on the bone from the siphon, then cut it, so that a hot abscess does not occur: then press the wound with flax from linen cloths.
Then care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
On the extraction of arteries which are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemicrania or acute catarrh due to acrimonious humidities and warmth in the neck of time, or an old soda, severe, and similar to these occur in a man: and it is treated with methods of curative medicine, but that does not help; then we are experienced in dealing with such maladies, extraction of arteries from the neck, or cauterization of them, as we have described.
And the method of operation for their extraction is that the sick person shaves hairs which are in the neck, and bends to the visible artery in the neck. Moreover, it is shown to you by its pulse, and it rarely hides except in a few men, or severe coldness.
If it is hidden to you, then let the sick person tighten his head with any cloth of his; then rub the place with a rough cloth. Or boil the place with hot water, until it appears to you in a clear appearance. Then take a spoon, which I previously made. Then peel the skin with it easily until you reach the artery. Then insert a hook into it and draw it out towards the top until you draw it out from the skin, and make it come out from all sides of the layers beneath it.
But if the artery is delicate: then insert it with the tip of the hook. Then cut from that part according to the amount by which its ends will be extended and contracted, and there should not be a blood flow. For if it is not cut, and if it is not separated, the blood does not rise deeply.
Then evacuate from the blood six ounces, up to three.
If the artery is large: then it must be tied in two places with strong thread, double filament, silk, or cord of alhohod, so that rot and decay do not occur before the wound is consolidated, and there should not be a blood flow.
Then cut off the excess, which is between two ligaments. Do that at that hour, or another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautionery to the bone, with a small knife-shaped cauterization; until its ends are cut off, and it remains in the same place as the operation.
And it is a better operation, unless the patient has fever, or suffers from cold conditions. Because cautionery comes from those things that help to stop wetness. Therefore it is a help.
And after the extraction of the artery, the place should be filled with old boiled material; and fine powdered lice should be placed on top of it.
And after the solution, it is to be cleaned with dry medicines that cause new flesh to grow and with linen until it heals.
If there happens to be bleeding from the artery while you are operating, then hasten to cut it with cautionery or fill the place with wax; and press your hand until the bleeding stops. If there is nothing from those present, then place your finger on the place until the blood freezes. And immerse the place with water of strong cold, until the sharpness subsides and it is pressed as necessary.
And because the vein is lighter and easier to extract, it is to cauterize the vein with this cautionery having two small knives; and the sharpness of the two knives should be similar to almandine. Nevertheless, they are much less sharp than two knives. Because if they are as sharp as two knives, cold should be applied to both of them; and they will not cut flesh swiftly. Since there is a certain thickness in them, heat of fire should be applied to them; and the flesh is cut off swiftly; when this operation is thus performed, it is better than any operation, and lighter and easier.
This is the form of the cautery.
And let the space between two knives be of the size of a finger's width, after you mark two places with encaustum (wax); and place both extremely hot ones, until they reach the bone, and cut the vein in two places: to expel what is between its extremities. They are not consolidated with this cautery thoroughly.
Head IV.
Chapter on the treatment of continuous, acute tears from the eyes.
When the tears are continuous and there is a flow from veins on the outside of the skull; and no medicine for treatment is applied to them with medicines, and you see the face of the sick person blushing, and it feels like the crawling of ants on the forehead; and his eyes are sunken, wet, so that the hairs of their eyelashes have already been corroded by the corrosion; and his eyelids are heated due to the acuity of the tears: then the ancients resorted to this treatment for them, and they called it treatment with a knife.
And it is, that you order (the patient) to shave the hairs which are on his forehead. Then make three equal incisions in the forehead: and let the length of the incision be as two fingers, and let one incision be equidistant from the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second slightly below the movement of the arms, and the third on the other side: and avoid cutting the arteries which are on both sides. And extend your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the space of all incisions be the size of three finger joints connected: and have a piece of sponge prepared, or dry cloth multiplied, with which you can absorb blood.
Then insert the pointed end of two pieces, whose following shape is: From the incision which is from the temple, up to the second incision: and scrape with it the entire skin that is between two incisions, together with the fat that is above the eye. Then do the same from the middle incision up to the second incision. Then remove the pointed end and insert another tool, called a sharp knife, from one side gently, not sharp on the other side. And this is its shape.
And place its sharp side facing the attached flesh with skin, and its blunt side facing the bone: and push it until it reaches the middle incision: and cut off with it all vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, except for the incision which appears on the skin.
Then do the same in the middle incision up to another incision.
And when an equal amount of blood flows out, squeeze the places from clotted blood pieces.
Then place a linen cloth from an old pot on every fissure, and place over them small pieces that have been soaked in wine, oil, or vinegar. And ensure that no hot abscess occurs.
On the third day, loosen the ligature and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then take care of that with the ointment of basilicon, and the others that heal wounds until it is healed.
Chapter V.
Chapter on the treatment of acute tear ducts and nasal catarrh from inside the head.
When someone has frequent, severe, and persistent catarrhs or acute tears, you notice their eyes are weakened, small, and their appearance is already poor: and the eyelids have ulcers, hairs fall out from them, and there is a sharp pain deep within the head, which causes sneezing: then take from these symptoms, those substances that catarrhs or tears do not come unless from many veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And it should be prescribed to the sick person to shave their forehead. Then make one incision in the middle of the forehead, or slightly to the right or left in width, starting from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision extend to the bone: and stretch out your hand away from the temples that move during chewing until the bone is exposed: and remove all blood with a sponge.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with a heated iron or with linen cloths. Then tie on top with thread: and soak the thread with wine and oil to prevent a hot abscess from forming.
And when you release it and see that the hot abscess is about to decrease: then you must break the bone, until meat begins to grow in it.
Then care for it with a drying treatment that promotes growth of flesh: just as if you take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of resin: and prepare a plaster from them, and apply it to promote growth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter VI.
Section on treatment for the one falling into the ear.
Every thing that falls into the ear is one of four kinds: either it is a mineral stone, or something similar to a stone like iron and wood; or it is from a plant such as chickpea and beans; or it is liquid such as water, vinegar, and similar substances; or it is an animal.
When a stone falls into the ear or something of that kind which does not grow in the ear, expose only the ear: if you see a stone, then pour something from broken oil, or sesame into the ear. Then administer the extraction of it and make him sneeze with powder and apply opium to the nostrils near the onset of sneezing, when you put around the ear fragments from cloth or wool and stretch the ear towards the upper parts.
Often it comes out with this care.
If it does not come out, then administer the extraction of it with Geisa (meaning Pizigir), that is subtle Pizigarols: whose shape is this.
If it comes out with Geisa, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction of it with a fine blunt hook few times.
If it does not come out through that, then make a tube from iron and introduce the end of the tube into the ear opening a lot and apply opium around the tube with softened wax so that only the way is open to the wind; then extract it with your strong pull of the wind.
Often it comes out with what we have said. If it does not come out in this way: then take some helkalimbate or distilled water, that is wheat gluten prepared with which birds are caught, a small amount; and place it on the end of the radius after you have placed a suitable lid over it well; then introduce it into the ear opening with ease, when you remove the ear from moisture.
If it does not come out with all that I have mentioned, then hurry to cut, before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
The method of lancing is to first use the lancet on the weak, in the head region: and draw out from his blood according to its power. Then make the weak person sit between your hands, and turn his ear upward, and make a small lancing wound at the base of the ear near its fatty tissue in the depressed place: and let the wound be in the shape of the moon until you reach the stone: then remove it with whatever is possible for you using the instruments.
Then let the lancing wound heal from your own time and care until it heals.
If a grain falling into the ear is one that grows and swells, then administer its removal.
But if it does not obey you for evacuation, then take a thin, delicate probe of this shape.
And administer with it the removal of that type from grains which fall into the ear, and do not do this when you think that the grain is already moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you put many fragments on it: then remove them with forceps, or with a subtle probe, or with suction, as we have said, for the removal of it is relieved.
In water which enters the ear, the weak should use sneezing with it in the first place: and already the ear has filled itself with some hot water: and it lies on top of that ear where the water is. If it comes out through this, it is good.
And if not: then take many small, soft, warm stones according to the length of a finger and heat them slightly: and the weak person should insert one from these into the ear canal of his: and sprinkle one foot with it on that side, and strike with another stone against the stone in the ear. "Therefore, it should not cease to be done with a stone and a stone, until all the water comes out.
"And now the water flows out in such a way that you take one from balsam or reed, and insert its tip into the ear; and light the other end with fire until it burns as much of it as possible. "Then take another reed and do this repeatedly until all the water comes out; and draw it out with a cannula as described earlier using the stone.
"In the extraction of an animal that has entered it, if it is of small body size, like a louse, and similar to what was said in the division, care should be taken for it as I have stated.
"But if it is of large body size, which can be perceived by the sense: then administer the extraction of it with tweezers and hooks; and its removal is easier for all who hold in the ear.
"In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when care for it is not effective as I have said in division and in the treatment of distillations, then you should look at the ear in sunlight. "Therefore, if something appears there from worms, then draw it out with tweezers or delicate hooks.
"But if nothing appears there, then take a cannula with this shape: narrow at the bottom and wide at the top; insert its fine tip into the ear according to the size that the sick person can tolerate; then suck it with strong suction. "Do this repeatedly until all worms come out.
"But if they do not obey your command to leave, then wrap the tip of a cannula with wax as I have said using the stone.
"If they do not come out as I have said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have been experienced with in the treatment of worms; and you will find it in the treatment of distillations.
And let your flow (be) that which you pour oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose shape is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or bronze, narrow below, where there should be a small hole, wide above.
Therefore, let the thing (that is) pressed within the hollow of the cannula be made of bronze properly. And if you wish, take radium (a mixture of copper and zinc), and wrap its end with a wrapping properly; then pour oil, or juice, or whatever medicine you want into the cannula; and let it be in the ear; then insert radium with the wrapper on top, and press it with your hand moderately, until the oil is pressed out in the hollow of the ear, and the sick person feels it inside: and whatever is poured into the ear, let it be already heated slightly; and take care that there is no substance that distills excessively cold into it; medicines cannot tolerate that.
Chapter VII.
Chapter on the treatment of auricular impaction (ear blockage).
Whenever some infants emerge from their mother's womb without perforated eardrums.
And it also happens to some people that ear impaction occurs due to a wound or tissue born in the ear.
And this impaction sometimes occurs in the deep ear canal, which is not visible; and sometimes it occurs near the outer ear canal, which can be seen.
Therefore, that which occurs in the deep ear and is not perceptible by sight, is difficult to cure in many dispositions (positions).
And in the one which is visible by sight, it is necessary that you place the sick person's ear on the sun and look at it; then if you see the impaction appearing, open it with a thin spatula whose shape is as follows, its end should have a small hollow, part of which should be sharp: and the rest of the spatula should be two sides that are gentle so as not to harm the ear.
If therefore an abscess is born from the flesh within the ear: then hold it with a subtle hook, and cut it easily and powerfully until all the flesh is removed.
If therefore an abscess has gone deep into the ear: then take a thin probe, warm it slightly with fire: then put it into the ear.
If you should feel an abscess which is accompanied by weakness and difficulty of hearing, try to open it gently: and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
Then put linen in the ear according to the size of the hole you made, wrapped in Egyptian ointment: do this for several days until you are certain that the wound has healed.
Or take linen and soak it in rose water, powderize on it ground alum, and use it.
If you see that the ear is beginning to decay: then it is necessary to extract the linen, and allow it to remain with another piece of linen which you have wrapped in a pot made with rose oil, until the decaying matter becomes warm: then take care of it until it heals.
If there is bleeding, immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear: and use the rest of the treatment that removes the described bleeding in the section on distillation.
Chapter on the care of Althelia's Eyes (Eyelids).
Chapter VIII.
Those Altheli that occur on the eyelids of the eyes are sometimes wet and sometimes dry.
Therefore it is necessary to hold them with tweezers or with a hook, and cut them from their roots. Then apply powdered alum.
If blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautionery.
To cauterize them is better after the incision. Often they return when something remains from their roots. And when cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Chapter on the treatment of inflammation of the eyelids of the eye.
Section IX.
Often something happens on the eyelids resembling Grandinosity in its firmness and hardness, and it is called a Grandino; it is an accumulation of thick humidity on the upper eyelid and lower eyelid.
Therefore the operation is to determine if it is a Grandino that appears on the eyelid and moves in all directions; its matter is easy to remove.
Make an incision above it with sufficient width. Then scrape it from all sides easily until it comes out. Then hold it with a hook and cut it off.
If the removal of it is not prepared for you unless after you have penetrated the eyelid with a small incision, then it harms the weak in some way.
If the incision is large: then gather it up with stitching; and care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from that. Ointment restores and fills it in.
And if the Grandino is inclined towards the inner part of the ear and the surface turns inwards, then turn the eyelid over, hold the Grandino with a hook; apart from that you will need an incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched by the incision, it does not harm the weak in any way.
Then wash the eye after snow-blowing incision with salted water; and take care of the place until it heals when the patient is sick.
On the cure of the Eyelids.
Chapter X.
The axirnath is a boil that arises in the upper eyelid; and it mostly happens to children; and it weighs down their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot see the light of the sun, because tears run towards them, and for this reason you see them lying on their faces constantly, and sleeping on them, and their eyelids are always moist under the eyebrows, which have already been swollen; and the appearance of the axirnath is visible to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel the axirnath between them.
And the method of treatment is for the patient to put his head in your lap.
Then take a linen cloth, and prepare on it a linen square according to the size of what contains axirnath from all sides. Then put it on top and press with your fingers from all sides, so that axirnath gathers in the middle of the circle.
Then find in the center of that moisture with a thin-bladed knife-like instrument, and let the incision not be larger than the one made during venesection in depth.
Or it is necessary that you make an incision of the entire skin until you reach axirnath, because axirnath proceeds from the incision in various dispositions, for axirnath comes out from the incision like the shape of a white grease ball.
Then remove it with a cloth that you have infused between your fingers towards the outside; and you turn your hand to right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to add to the incision so as not to reach with the knife-like instrument to the eye, and damage it.
If however the Axirnath does not appear to you at the beginning of the split, you shall add a little into the split with ease, until the Axirnath comes out. Then extract it, as we have said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the site, and bind it with threads.
And among men there are those who grind salt and place it in the hollow of the split to dissolve what remains from that moisture.
Then care for it until it heals.
If however an abscess occurs at the site which is hot, then care for it with soothing plasters until it heals.
\*\*Methods of Ataxmira for the eye, that is, when the eyelid becomes soft so that it weeps as it should not.\*\*
Chapter XI.
When hairs appear in the eyelids beyond the natural course of hair growth and turn grey, then they harm the eye and cause diseases such as constant weeping, softening of the eyelid, and clouding, until it causes the destruction of the eye.
And Ataxmira for the eye is treated according to four methods. Or by cautery with fire. (This means using a hot instrument to burn away the excess hair.) Or with sharp medicine, according to what has been said in the chapter on cautery. (The "sharp medicine" refers to chemicals or agents that can burn away the excess hair.) Ataxmir is treated by incision and suture. By reeds, as I shall say.
You must place the head of the sick man on your lap. Then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it is turned, that is good. And if not: insert the point into it, where there is a thread from below the eyelid; let the point penetrate with the thread from above, and let this be near the hairs themselves, that is, near the edge of the eyelid, where the hairs grow: and draw the thread upward along with the eyelid, and turn it with a spatula.
Then find on the inside of the eyelid below the added hairs, with the probe inserted from the greater lacrimal sac to the lesser lacrimal sac.
Then draw out the thread, and place under the eyelid a small piece of cotton or cloth; then mark the eyelid with wax, so that it resembles the figure of a myrtle leaf.
However, it is necessary that the figure be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid; because it varies greatly among humans.
For there are those who require that the incision be made according to a large size of the eyelid, according to the amount that is softened by the eyelid.
Then with the probe find on top of the two lines you marked, and start from the greater lacrimal sac to the lesser lacrimal sac; let there be one fissure near the natural hairs, like a thick vein.
Then insert the hook into one of the two corners of the skin. Then scrape the whole thing. Then join together with a suture the two lips, using a sharp needle and fine wool; wipe away the blood, and let the excess from the threads adhere to the eyebrows, if you wish to do this: and if not, do nothing.
Then release the suture and the threads for three or four days; afterwards, take care of it.
And if you wish, release the wound without suture, and take care of it, so that it dries out and contracts. For the eyelid is elevated during the sealing of a wound and its adhesion; but it will be better later on.
This method of healing was taught by the ancient Ataxmires.
However, there is concern for the sick person in this, and it comes from a good operation, and there is no fear in it.
And another method is in the Ataxmires also: it is to mark signs on the eyelid with a figure like that of the leaf of the myrtle, as we have said.
Then lift the eyelid with three separated or joined combs in the following shape, then cut off what is excessive with small scissors according to this shape with equal incisions.
If it is not possible for you to hold the comb and it does not fit, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the middle of the figure; and insert another thread near the greater tear duct, and a third thread near the smaller tear duct; and gather the threads with equal tension between your fingers.
Then lift your hand evenly with an elevation; and lift the skin over which is marked the wound, as we have said.
Then gather together two edges of the wound with a suture; and take care of it until it heals.
If an abscess occurs at your incision or your wound, use wool to soothe it with pitch and similar substances from soothing ointments.
And sometimes the eyelashes also turn over.
Therefore, it is necessary to use what we have said for an incision; but a suture is more artificial for both. Treatment for Ataxmir with dogs.
It is to turn the eyelid and cut the cleft that is inside, as I have said before. Then, using art, make two dogs or two thin sticks of wood, their length being the same as the eyelid's length and their width narrower than that of the spatula's; and you have already cut on both ends at the places where you hold the thread from each side.
Then gather one of them with a spatula on that which overhangs from the eyelid of the eye and tie the two dogs from each side with strong binding, and release it after several days. For the tightened skin will die, darken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
If it slows down (the dead skin), then cut it with scissors. Then take care of it until it heals.
When it hardens, lift the eyelid and do not pluck the hairs.
And this is the shape of the two dogs that you will make according to this form and its size (dimensions).
Chapter 12.
Treatment for plucking hairs from the eye with a needle.
The procedure is to take a fine needle and insert a thin silk thread into it gently. Then gather its ends and tie them both with a very thin knot; and the length of the threads should be one palm (of the hand).
Then prepare another thin thread called Alinxotati underneath it briefly and knot its ends if you wish.
Then place the sick person's head on your lap and bring it close to the sun so that the operation may be visible; because this is a delicate or minor operation.
Then insert the needle with Alinxotati into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then draw out the needle above the incision: and insert the needle into the incision; if it is one, or two, or three, not more than that.
Then draw your hand along with it, until the needle comes out of the incision together with the hair and the surrounding skin along with its natural hair.
If the incision is drawn and no hair comes out with it, draw the incision downward with the thread you have prepared in it, until the incision comes out of the upper opening, and you see it with your eyes; then you draw out the incision and the thread, and extract both, and close the eye, and leave the closed one for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place, and flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then tie a long hair from the natural hairs to it and pull them out together; or leave it alone until it grows out, and then pull it out.
Chapter XIII.
When this xanthelasma occurs in the eye, it is called "Leporina.
And this xanthelasma is either natural or acquired.
Therefore the acquired one arises from the consolidation of a wound, or a cut, or a cauterization, and similar things.
And the method of operation in it is to open the consolidation and separate its edges, and put a piece of cotton from flax in it, and tie it until it heals.
And it is not necessary to use in the treatment of this xanthelasma things that dry and tighten; for if you do so, the xanthelasma becomes worse than before; rather use things that soften, such as fenugreek: and embrocation with water, in which althea has been boiled, along with flax seed; and unguent of dyaquilon, which has been melted with some oil; and apply cotton soaked with it, and treat with it.
Thy treasure of care is that thou should endeavor with all thy skill, so as not to heal in its former shape.
This operation which we have said, is indeed a correction of the Alexis, so that not the shape of the place should return as it was altogether.
Of the care of Alexis which is done on the lower eyelid, and it is a thickening or contraction upwards towards right and left.
Chapter XIV.
This which is done below [on the lower eyelid], is indeed what is truly named Alexis. And it is natural, and it is accidental.
And the accidental [Alexis] is made from a wound, or a split, or cautery, and similar things.
And the way of operation in this is that thou takest a needle with double thread, and dost dip it into flesh, and maketh it pass from tear-duct on the left unto tear-duct on the right, until the thread reach the ends of the flesh.
Then extend the flesh upwards with a needle, and cut it with a broad knife. If therefore the shape of the eyelid return as it should be, it is good.
And if not, take a burnisher, and put it in the split, and turn with it the eyelid; and make two splits on the inner side of the eyelid, and let the ends of the two splits be from the corners of the incision, until they meet and make an angle: until when they gather together this shape is made, and it is the Greek letter lambda.
Then remove that flesh to its sharp lower part from what follows the eyelid. Then gather together the separated parts; or it with a yarn thread.
Then care for them [the splits] with what we said, from softening medicaments and linen, until they heal.
If Alxatrati occurs from a fissure, either by suturing or cauterizing: then it is necessary to explore the fissure flat under the eyelashes, as before. Then separate between two lips with a linen cloth, as we said before.
The summary of the treatment for Alxatrati, whether it is above or below, is that the operation should be performed on it, according to the preparation as described for Alxatrati.
Indeed it (Alxatrati) is full of many diversities in shape: and the skillful artisan prepares his art with whatever means is possible to him, so that he makes it return to a natural or nearly natural figure, and himself who is sick, according to what is suitable for him from the operation and instruments in various dispositions.
Chapter XV.
Chapter on the adherence of the eyelid with the conjunctiva, or cornea.
When this consolidation happens to many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres with the white of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.
Therefore, it is necessary that you introduce the tip of a radius under the eyelid and pull it up; or extend it with a hook; then cut the adherence with a thin spatula, which should not be sharp like a spatula's edge, but rather dull slightly; so that the sick person is not disturbed during the operation, and the spatula is removed, and it does not harm the eye with its sharpness; and your incision should be as if you are scraping off the adherence with ease, until when the eyelid returns to its natural shape, and the adherence is completely healed.
Then pour salted water into the eye, and rinse it with water; or drip it onto him from a syringe made of sheep's horn with water mixed.
Then separate with a linen thread between the eyelid and the eye: and place on the eye wool soaked with egg white: and after three days use it or with solidified ointments, until it heals.
On the Incision of the Toenail and the Protrusion of Skin around the Eyes.
Chapter XVI.
Know that a toenail is according to two modes. Or it is horny and resembles the hoof of an ox, being hard but fine. Or it is not horny, resembling the consistency of frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron or attempted to be picked up with a nail, is torn off and cannot be gripped by the nail.
And neither of these types begins, except from the greater tear duct, until it gradually reaches the eye, covers the vision, and prevents light and movement of the eye.
And the method of operation in the incision is: that the sick person places his head in your lap. Then open the eyes of the patient and pull back the eyelid with your hand. Then gather the toenail with a small nail, and extend it upward. Then take the awl and insert a hair from the horse, ox or sheep into it, let it be a thread, and bend the end of the awl slightly, and fix it in the middle of the toenail: and pierce it with the awl, and tie the toenail with the thread, and extend it upward: and scrape with the hair the side of the toenail that follows the pupil, as if you were holding it with the hair until its end.
Then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a sharp small knife or tweezers: and let out the natural skin of the tear duct so that there is not a persistent flow of tears from the incision.
And sometimes the nail is extended with a spatula alone; or with thread, as we have said. Then it is scraped with a soft spatula, whose form is this.
Be careful, lest the spatula touches the horny coat and causes a break there, and the pupil is pierced through.
Then after the incision, cast into the eye something crushed salt or made from cumin and leave it for another day. Then care for it as necessary until it heals.
If the nail is not nerve-connected and you cannot insert an awl into it nor does a spatula fit there, then this type of nail is repeatedly treated with medicines until it heals as I narrated in the division.
If you wish to cut it (the nail), then open the eye of the sick person, and take a thin, soft, delicate, blunt spatula according to this shape: And grind the nail from above with a sharp razor. If you see that it is becoming rarefied and crushed, and the razor presses upon it, then distill from your hour into the eye from cumin made of zinziber, or red cumin, or crushed salt; and close the eye until another day.
Then repeat this procedure until the whole thing is removed. Unless it should be a hot abscess in your eye, then leave the former and care for the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat this procedure on it with the razor until it heals.
However, a growth of flesh near the tear-duct, if it causes great harm in the eye, is suspended with a spatula and cut from that part of it; not to the end, so as not to interrupt the flow of tears.
Then milk, whether white or red, or made from cheese, should be applied until it heals.
On incision of the eyelid, and flesh born in the eye.
Chapter XVII.
There sometimes arises in certain human eyes red flesh composed or laid over, until it covers the pupil, approaches, or contracts upon the eyelids and perhaps turns the eyelids towards the outside; and it resembles a rosebush.
And the treatment for it is that the weak one should place his head in your lap. Then open the eyes of that person and collect all that flesh together with appropriate forceps; and hold it with one forceps or scissors.
Then make an incision in the flesh first, until you have finished cutting it all off with a knife. Be careful not to harm the eye during the operation; and let your cut be such as we described in the incision of the nail, or with small forceps, as are used for extracting an asebel [a kind of cyst], according to what its form will be after this chapter.
When your incision is completed and the entire alguardenic [the red flesh] is removed, then fill the eye with ground salt or pour in a reddish powder and similar substances from corrosive medicines; and place on the outside of the eye a warm cloth with egg white to protect it from infection.
If any part of the alguardenic remains or if a hot blood flows and you fear a hot infection, then leave the eye alone and treat that which cures an abscess.
Then repeat the procedure until it heals.
And do similarly with the added flesh that occurs in the eye of this kind.
It is necessary that every weak eye of an alien, whether by natural or accidental way, be treated with iron; and you shall not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that the member can endure such operation.
On collecting Sibel from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
Chapters on Sibel (red veins over the eye that hinder vision and weaken the eye over days).
Therefore it is necessary that first you consider if the eye with Sibel is strong and there is no other disease except Sibel; then collect Sibel from it.
And it is to command the weak person to place his head on your chest.
Then suspend those veins with a single hook or two according to your judgment; and let the hook be subtle and double, in this shape, or there should be two hooks in one body, in this shape.
Then collect with subtle forceps those veins and remove blood hour by hour until you see the veins are removed from the eye and resolved; and beware not to harm the eye with the points of the forceps.
And let your operation be at midday facing the sun, and be very firm during your operation so as not to cut except the veins.
And when you have finished, then distill into the eye either green or red; so that it burns what remains from Sibel with its own acidity.
If it is not possible for you to collect all of it in that hour, then plaster the eye with what soothes the pain of the eye; and leave it for several days until the pain subsides; then cover it warmly; afterward apply it again in the same way until it heals.
This is the form of a pair of forceps.
On reducing an Ariessus (nasal polyp) to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
The surgeon named Arisset cures a fistula with cautionery or sharp medicine burning, according to the narrative that precedes it.
If it is not cured, then there is no skill in it, unless to find upon the abscess at its birth and draw out all the moisture that is in it and pus, until the bone appears.
When the bone appears, and you see corruption or blackness in it, then file it with an instrument whose shape is this.
It is called the rasping of the skull.
Make it from iron and its head should be round like an azir (a type of file), pierced with the punctations of a rasp or a fine, subtle rasp; and place it on the corrupted bone.
Then move it back and forth with your fingers, and press your hand gently on it until you know that the corruption is now filed away; do this repeatedly.
Then restore the place with most powerful astringents.
If the place consolidates and flesh grows there, and the course of pus is cut off; and it remains for forty days without recurring, without abscessing, and no incident occurs in it; then you know that it has been cured.
If not, then there is no skill in it, unless to reduce the fistula to the nostril opening, according to this shape:
It is to expose the second bone with iron or sharp medicine; and when the bone is exposed, then take a trepan (a surgical instrument for boring a hole in the skull) according to this shape: its tip should be iron, triangular; and its handle should be a pyramid extended to the tip, as you see.
Then place it on the bone itself; and let it be close to the lacrimal (eye tear duct); and extend your hand slightly from the eye. Then turn your hand with the lancet until it penetrates the bone and feels weak; by this, when you hold your hand over his nose, you will know that wind is coming out from it.
Therefore, restore the place with cauterizing medicines, as I have taught you.
When the flesh is born and the place hardens; then the matter that was flowing outwards returns to the nose; it is therefore lighter above the weak one.
Chapter on Reducing Protrusions of the Eye.
Chapter 20.
When the eye protrudes completely and there is no damage to vision nor decrease; then it is necessary to loosen the weak one. Then apply leeches. Afterwards, place poultices on the neck without scarification but with suction.
Then place over the eye a liniment made from acacia, aloes, frankincense and gum Arabic. Then bind the eye on top with plasters full of many fleas.
And the method of fleas is: that you take soft cloths, many, and fold each one four times; make many from them; then place one on top of another according to the size that the eye needs; then bind them together with a strong bandage.
And repeat the poultices without scarification but with suction.
Then remove the poultices and let the eye be bound day and night.
If the binding becomes soft again, then it is necessary to bind it tightly; then remove the binding after a day and night, as said before.
If you see that the eye has returned to its usual color; it is good; and if not, then repeat the poultices, fleas, bindings, and poultices until it heals.
On the incision of the tunica vaginae.
Concerning the extraction of the stone from the bladder
When the bladder is ruptured, then the stone comes out like a grain of the vagina and stains the human form because of it, and there is a desire to incise it: then the operation should be performed on it, as I have told you before; it is to insert a pointed instrument from the root of the bladder, from the lower part to the upper part.
Then insert another pointed instrument with a double thread from the lachrymal side and make it penetrate; then release the first needle according to its position.
Then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the bladder around the needle; and pull it tightly.
Then take out the needle and place wool soaked in oil on the eye; and release it until the thread comes out with the bladder.
Then take care of the eye, because it is comforting to itself, until the wound heals.
And sometimes the bladder is tightened from all sides with a bandage made of cloth until the eye protrudes greatly.
Then it should be pierced with a sharp instrument so that it reaches the depth of the eye and the moisture of the eyeball is let out, and the eye descends and enters immediately; then tighten it until it heals.
On the treatment of ulcers.
Concerning the operation for removing a piece from a malignant
This disease called Alcomnati is nothing but pus that accumulates in the eye, similar to water descending and it itself is not.
And the way of operating on it is for the sick person to sit on a prepared chair or directly.
Then take the head with both your hands from two sides and move it until you see pus reaching the lower part of your eyes. Then it figures and does not descend, and the light is freed: and let the sick one see as he saw before: and if it does not descend lower, know that there is water.
If the descent of pus is not prepared with what I have said, then make the sick one sit between your hands. Then take a subtle spathule and bore with it on the cornified cushion near the junction of the conjunctiva with the corneal layer at the crown, until pus comes out.
When it comes out, then pour warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or warm water in which you have already cooked barley and honey; then treat it with the remaining treatment until it is healed.
Chapter on the treatment of water that descends into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have said the type of water in division, and what suits for perforating with a declaring and explaining speech, then take it according to health.
Then it is necessary that you make the sick one sit between your hands with a square position facing the light and near the sun; tie his healthy eye, and squeeze it very hard; then close the eye of the water with your right hand, if the eye in which there is water is the left eye; or with your left hand, if the eye is the right.
Then take your right hand (if the affected eye is the left) or your left hand (if the affected eye is the right).
Then place the tip of your thumb near the crown and the thickness of a radish on the white part of the eye visible as the smaller lachrymal; then push with power; and you revolve your hand together, until it penetrates into the cornea of the eye; and feel that your thumb has reached an empty place.
And it is necessary that the measure of the journey (of an instrument) be large enough for depth, the measurement of the space from the pupil to the end of blackness; and it is the eye's corona. You will see (the line) in the very pupil of the eye, on account of the clarity of the cornea layer.
Then place (the instrument) large enough to reach where there is water. Then press it downward once after another.
If therefore water flows out immediately, then the sick one sees (the object) above what opens his vision immediately, and large enough in his own eye.
Then rest for a while. If water flows out again, then remove it (the instrument) after it has flowed out large enough.
When it is stuck and does not rise up: then remove large enough with ease; and you turn your hand slowly.
Then dissolve something from clear salt in water, and clean the eye within with it. Then place outside the eye the whole of wool soaked in rose oil and white egg yolk; and bind with it the healthy eye.
We and those who are of our time place over him (the affected part) crushed cumin with egg white.
If large enough does not obey you in entering the eye because of its hardness, since it is a man whose eye is very hard: then it is necessary that you take a spatula, which is called Alberid, and this is its shape.
Therefore bore only the conjunctiva with it (the instrument), and do not push your hand into the hole; and there is no other purpose but to make a subtle way to the large enough place.
Then insert large enough, as we said.
On the completion of your work, prepare for the sick one a bed well-made, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark house; and prohibit from all movements, and from coughing: and place food for him such as soothes his nature; and do not move his head to right or left at all.
And let the suture be according to its arrangement until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark dwelling, and test its sight: make it see things. Then bring the suture back until the seventh day.
It is not proper for him to do it during the hour of cure, or immediately after incision; rather, let a stranger do it: therefore, because water rises quickly through a violent wound.
If however a hot abscess occurs: then it is necessary that you dissolve the eye before the seventh day; and correct it with what soothes the abscess, until the abscess subsides; then remove its sight, and place over his oral cavity what regulates his vision for some days, while he remains in that dark dwelling.
Then let him go out of the house gradually, and convert himself to his cases (bandages).
And know that in the case of lancets, the student is not permitted to look away from the sight often; then he dares upon the operation.
And indeed, one of them who are from Aleppo has reached us, who said that a large cistern was made in Aleppo, through which water is drawn.
Therefore, I have not seen anyone in your land who made that; nor have I read it in any ancient books; and it is possible that it is new.
These are the forms of the species from the large cistern, to stand over him who does not know them.
Make them of bronze; and let their ends be with this same triangular subtlety, and the end sharp.
Chapter XXIII.
Chapter on the care of born flesh in the nose.
Whenever diverse fleshes are born in the nose, among which there is something resembling a scorpion of many feet; and from that is the cancerous flesh, stone-like, dark colored; and from that is the soft flesh, not dark colored.
Therefore, for the soft flesh among these, not fraudulent, nor cancerous, it is necessary that you make the patient sit opposite the sun with his nose open, and throw a hook into those fleshes; then draw them out towards the exterior, and cut what you have grasped from them with a thin subtle spatula on one side until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
If something remains of that which cannot be removed: then shave it with one subtle instrument with ease until nothing is left from it. If blood dominates you or a hot abscess occurs: then oppose it with what is necessary; or if it is from malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize him until the blood is separated and all fleshes are removed.
Then vinegar, or water, or wine should be thrown into the nose after the incision. If the nose opens and moisture proceeds to the palate, then you know that he is already well.
If the moisture does not penetrate as it should be, then you know that within him there is flesh born in the upper bones of the nose, which was not reached by the incision instrument.
Then it is necessary to insert a linen thread with some thickness and many knots; and place between each knot an amount equal to or less than a finger: and make the patient do it so that he sends one end of the thread into the nose with a rod, or with whatever is possible for him after he has made himself similar to an azer [a surgical instrument]; and draw out the smell until it reaches the back, and come out on his throat.
And indeed often do boys in schools make this like that of Attotus; and it is a matter easy to him who wishes.
Then place two ends of the string, one which comes out on the nose, and the other which remains inside the nose. Then, as an assistant, the skin incision with the knots that are in the thread. Do this until you know that the flesh is now with the thread knots.
Then withdraw the thread; and place on the nose after bleeding linen which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment; do this for three days or more until the ointment has completely dissolved all that remains of the flesh.
Then place at the end of the procedure a lead cannula into the nose for some days until it heals.
If however it requires drying treatment, use that.
For making the head-pouring when olive oil and other medicines are distilled into the nose, make it from silver or brass; which is similar to a small lantern, open like a snail's shell; and the channel should be similarly shaped.
And if you wish to make a closed cannula, do so like a reed.
And the snail-shell instrument for head-pouring should be full and perforated; which has a handle at the end, with which you hold it when heating oil or whatever you wish in it, and liquids that flow easily.
Chapter XXV.
Often a Thelul is born at the end of the nose and grows and increases with days until it becomes unsightly to look at it.
And for this reason, it is necessary to cut it off at the beginning of its appearance and remove all of it. Then place on the spot, either a cautery or a medicine burning in its place.
If the incision does not progress as expected until it is enlarged, then consider if it is hard, of a dark color and few senses; then do not touch it with iron, because it is a cancerous ulcer.
For often I have seen that one who has cut an abscess has encountered great evil upon the one who possessed it.
And if the abscess is soft when touched and not dark in color, and you see that it is possible to cut through it entirely, then evacuate the weakened part, and cut it without fear or hesitation; and care for the place with it so that it drains and constricts until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Chapter on stitching the nose, lip, and ear.
Know that when continuity of one of these cartilages is disrupted, the operation does little good, unless in some men.
Therefore when something happens to anyone from one of these, you should consider if it is a fresh wound with its own blood; and then join together the edges of the wound with stitching; then care for it until it heals.
And if continuity of the lips has been separated and each part has become healthy, then it is necessary to scrape off all the part appearing from its own skin until it bleeds. Then join together the two lips with stitching and bind them, and sprinkle over it powder of dragon's blood and pulverized olibanum; and place on top of the powders a fragment of plaster called diaphyton, and of another consolidating plaster; and leave it bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it, and change the medicine; and leave it until the stitches are dissolved by themselves. Then care for yourself with an ointment until you are healed.
The method of suturing is to gather the solution of continuity, or with needles as we have mentioned in the abdomen suturing; or gather the solution with thread, as I told you before.
Chapter XXVII [of Albucasis's book].
Chapter on the removal of lip nodes.
Many people often have hard ulcers on the inside of their lips similar to the seeds of a plant; and some of them are smaller, and others larger.
Therefore, it is necessary to turn the lip and search for every node on it; and hang it with a hook and cut it in all directions.
Then fill the place after the incision with boiled vinegar until blood is separated.
Then clean with vinegar, and care for the place where there is stiffness until the wounds heal.
Chapter XXVIII [of Albucasis's book].\]  Mult
Chapter on incising the skin of a newborn baby over the gum.
Many times flesh is born above the gum, which the ancients called ablus.
Therefore, it is necessary to hang it with a hook; or hold it with forceps and cut it at the root and let pus run out or blood.
Then place on top of it boiled vinegar or other stiffening powders, dried.
If that flesh returns after treatment, many times it returns, then cut it a second time and burn it; for it does not return after burning.
Chapter XXIX [of Albucasis's book].\]
Chapter on tooth shaving with iron.
Sometimes cavity forms on the surfaces of teeth from inside and outside and between gums with rough cortex; and sometimes they turn yellow and green, and when corruption reaches to the gum, and they become foul teeth through that.
Therefore it is necessary that you make the sick man sit between your hands, and his head in your bosom, and scrape the mole and tooth, where the bark appears to you, like sand: until nothing remains of them, and similarly do with blackness, and greenness, and citron-color, and others until they are cleaned.
If what is in them is removed at the beginning of the reasoning, it is good: if not, then repeat the reasoning upon them on another day, on the second, and on the third, until finally the study comes to that which you desire.
And know that the tooth requires scapellers of various shapes and forms, according to which it is prepared for your operation: because the scapeller with which the tooth is scraped from below is different from the scapeller with which the tooth is scraped between the teeth, according to other shapes.
And these shapes of the scapellers be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter 30.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary that you cure the tooth from its pain with all your skill, and you are slow in its extraction. For there is no substitute for it when it is extracted, since it is a lofty substance: until there is no excuse for the extraction of it, then if the sick man is compelled to extract it himself, he must be made firm and certain by you that the painful tooth is to be extracted.
For often pain deceives the sick man and he believes that there is wormwood in the tooth and extracts it himself: then the pain does not subside until the sick tooth is extracted.
We have already seen this from the operation of phlebotomists.
And when the sick man is made certain by you that the painful tooth is to be extracted, then it is necessary that you make an incision around the tooth with a spatula, in which there is something of virtue, until the gums are loosened from all sides: then move it with your fingers, or with subtle forceps firstly gently, until you shake it.
Then place the large forceps well in those places [of the patient], and hold the head of the weak [patient] between your knees so that it does not move; then pull out the tooth along the straight path, so that you do not break it.
If it does not come out [the tooth], then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is perforated or corroded: then it is necessary to fill that hole with a cloth and bind it with the end of a thin radius so that it does not break during your hour of extraction with forceps.
And you should take great care with the incision around the gums from all sides.
And keep your strength so that you do not break it [the tooth] and leave a part of it, and return over the weak one with that greater pain which was first there.
And be careful not to make the same mistake as ignorant bloodletters do in haste and their audacity with its removal, besides what I have told you [about administering something].
For many times they bring great weaknesses upon men, which are difficult to break and leave all of its roots, or some of them; or they extract it with certain bones of the jaw, as we have often testified.
Then it is washed after its removal [of the tooth] with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If there should be bleeding from the place (for it often happens), then rub something with wax and fill the place; if not, cauterize it [the area] if you do not have wax.
The tips of the fine forceps by which a tooth is moved should be long in length, short in handle, thick, so that they do not split when pressed upon the tooth; they should resemble the handles of large forceps, until when you tighten them, they do not bite themselves, nor split; the handles should be short, and made of iron or brass well-made, straight tips; and in their tips there should be teeth, some of which enter into certain places and tighten with a decent constriction, strong.
And sometimes they (the veins) become like the shape of a bird's beak called ciconia, and are very constricted.
Chapter 31.
On the extraction of teeth, and the removal of broken jaw bones.
When a piece remains in the socket of the tooth that is fractured, then it should be covered with lard on the spot for one or two days until the place softens; subsequently introduce into it algasti, or forceps: whose extremities are similar to the mouth of the bird named ciconia. The form of this is as follows (for the forceps):
The extremities are made as if with a rasp from within: or as if with an aliskilfegi.
If, therefore, it does not obey you with these forceps, then it is necessary that you be cautious on the root and separate the entire flesh and introduce an instrument called a Small Palanca, whose shape is as follows.
Let the end of it be short, somewhat thicker: and let it not be swollen so as not to break.
If, therefore, the root comes out through it, that is good; and if not, help with other instruments whose shapes are as follows.
The first shape is a triangle, in which there is some thickness.
The shape of the fine triangle.
And with other instruments and tools which preceded in the ratio of teeth.
And also helps with this instrument resembling a large nail, whose form is a twisted triangle, having some thickness to avoid breaking and not swollen.
And know that there are many instruments for teeth: and similarly the other instruments are not counted, and the skilled craftsman, skillful in his art, finds himself an instrument according to what the operation signifies and the illnesses themselves.
Because of the variety in the types of ailments for which the ancients did not make an instrument.
If the bone breaks from the jaw, or from other bones of the face, or rots: then examine it on its own place with that which is suitable for it from the instruments and forceps I mentioned for root extraction, and help with this gesture, whose shape is as follows.
Let there be some thickness in it gradually, so that the bone can be held or tightened with it and not escape and move away until the bone comes out; and restore the place with suitable medicines for this.
If there is a little rottenness in the bone, then scrape it off from its rottenness, and treat it until it heals.
Chapter XXXII.
On the lock of projecting teeth over others.
When teeth project not according to their natural course, the form becomes ugly because of it; and this is especially true when it happens in women and girls, namely in those who are menstruating.
Therefore, one must consider. For if a tooth is born after another tooth, and it does not fit or its locking mechanism or grinding mechanism is possible, then pull it out; and if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it with this tool, the shape of which is as follows:
It resembles a small beak and is made from hard iron with a very sharp tip.
And your cut should be such that you cut it over many days, and because of the hardness of the tooth, so as not to disturb any other teeth.
If it is a projecting tooth exposed to grinding, then grind it with a file made from iron, the shape of which is as follows:
The entire instrument is made of ivory, and its handle is small, full of large holes, like a file with which points are made: with which the hard tooth is gradually filed down over many days with ease, so that it is not disturbed, and falls out: then smooth it gently at the end, polish it with some files.
If it is a tooth that breaks and injures the tongue, then it must be filed with a file until the roughness of the fracture is removed and it is made smooth; and it should not injure the tongue nor corrupt speech.
Chapter XXXIII.
On filing teeth with gold filaments.
When there is concussion and agitation of the front teeth due to a blow or accident, and a weak person cannot hold what he eats so that it does not fall out; and if you have treated them with medicinal adhesives, but the treatment has not helped: then it is appropriate for them to be bound with a gold filament, because silver turns green and decomposes after days, but gold never changes.
And let the filament be of intermediate thickness and coarseness according to its quantity that it may hold between the teeth.
And the shape of filing is that you take the filament and insert its double between two healthy teeth; then wrap it with its ends around the mobile teeth, whether one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side with the needle. Then return the wrapping to the starting point; and bind your hand with delicacy and wisdom until it is not completely removed; and let your binding, which you bind the filament, be near the roots of the teeth so that it does not come off.
Then cut off the excess ends of the filament with scissors; and bring together both, and fold them back with a twist; and hide these in between the healthy tooth and the mobile tooth so as not to injure the tongue; then release it when it is bound tight enough.
If it is opened or cut open, bind them with another thread and let it remain in that state for the entire time.
This is the form of teeth, and the figure of the interlocking of two healthy teeth, and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that a tooth returns to its place after the loss of one or two in their respective locations, and remains as we have said; this is not done except by an artist, wise, and experienced.
And sometimes a piece is prepared from the bones of a calf; and it is made into the shape of a tooth, and placed in the position where it is protected and bound, as we have said; and it remains, and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
Sometimes this ligament that occurs under the tongue is natural, with which man is born, or accidental, from a wound that has already healed.
The operation in it is to open the mouth of the sick person at the head of his neck in your bosom, and lift out his tongue; then cut that nerve-ligament across its width until the tongue is released from its constraint.
If there is something hard and knotty, and it is from the consolidation of a wound; then throw a hook into it and pierce it across its width until you cut the ligament, and the knot is released.
And be careful that there is no tear in deep flesh, and do not cut an artery there, and let blood flow out.
Then it is cleaned in the trace of the incision with rose water, or vinegar, or cold water.
Then place a cloth made from flax under the tongue that the sick person holds all night; so that it does not consolidate again.
If however there occurs a bleeding, then place upon the place zagi crushed. If it is cut (by a knife), then cauterize the place with a lentiginous cautery that suits the wound; afterwards take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter XXXV. (Chapter 35)
Sometimes there occurs under the tongue an aposteme resembling a small Ranula which hinders the natural movement of the tongue and perhaps becomes swollen to the point of filling the bone.
And the operation on this is that you open the sick person's mouth facing the sun; and examine the aposteme.
If you see it of a dark or black colour, hard and insensitive to the touch; then do not touch it, as it is cancer.
And if it is sloping towards whiteness, where there is moisture; then plunge a hook into it and cut it with a thin spatula, and release it from all sides. If it bleeds during your operation, then place upon it crushed zagi until the bleeding stops; afterwards return to your operation until you extract it with its contents.
Then wash it with vinegar and salt; afterwards take care of it with the rest of the treatment that suits the wound until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of two Aphthae (aphtha is an ancient term for a canker sore).
Chapter XXXVI. (Chapter 36)
Sometimes there appear in the throat nodes which resemble glands that appear externally and are called two Aphthae; when you treat them with what I have said above and they do not heal, then examine them.
If it is a hard aposteme of dark colour, with little sensation; then do not touch it with iron.
If it is red in color and the root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing bleeding, rather leave it alone until it matures. Then either you will pierce it yourself or it will burst by itself.
If it is white in color and round and the root is subtle: then it must be cut.
And the operation on it is that you consider before its operation whether its aposteme is quiet and warmly completed, or if it decreases in some way: then therefore make the sick person sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your lap; and open his mouth, and let a servant hold him by hand, and press his tongue downwards with an instrument, whose form this is.
Let it be made from silver or brass, which is as subtle as a scalpel.
When therefore you press his tongue with it and the aposteme is shown to you and falls upon him: then take a hook, and fix it in a pea-sized lump, and extract it as far as possible, apart from pulling something out of the tunics along with it.
Then cut it with an instrument, whose form is as follows: It resembles forceps; however its extremities should be rounded, so that the opening of each of them is directly opposite another's point: therefore it should be made of steel or alum treated with oil.
If this tool is not available, then cut it with a spatula, whose form is as follows: One part should be sharp, not the other.
And after you have cut one pea-sized lump, cut another according to this same cutting pattern.
Then the sick person should rinse his throat with cold water or vinegar and water.
If bleeding occurs, let him gargle with water in which the bark of pomegranates has been boiled; or with myrtle leaves and similar ones from other plants, until the bleeding stops; then take care of him until he is healed.
And sometimes boils appear in the throat besides the two tonsils. Cut them equally according to what I said in the incision of the two tonsils.
I myself have already cured a woman from a boil that had been born in her throat, which was dragging toward swelling, few senses, which almost closed her throat; and the woman was breathing through a narrow opening, and she had already prohibited food for herself, and water; and by then, if it had remained for one or two days, death would have occurred.
The boil had risen only so much that it had released two branches until they came out through the two nasal openings.
I rushed quickly and fixed one of its hooks. Then I pulled it, and a large piece was drawn out from it.
Then I cut it off where it could be taken from the nasal opening.
Then I did what came out from the other nasal opening.
Then I opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; then I fixed a hook in the boil; then I cut off a piece of it, and nothing but a little blood came out from it; so the woman's throat was healed, and she immediately began to drink water, and then she started eating.
Therefore, I did not stop cutting from that boil for a long time; and the boil succeeded in place of what I was cutting, until it became too prolonged and with that [something else].
So, I made an incision, and burned the boil in the throat.
Therefore it stood after addition: then I walked on the side, and I did not know what God had done with it after me.
On the Incision of an Apostemat in the Uvula.
Chapter XXXVII.
When a catarrh descends to the uvula, and is excised when it is long, then it is named perpendicular; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is called a nodule.
When it is cured along with what has been said in the division, and cure does not help; and you see that the apostemat is warm and has subsided from there, and is soft; then one should incise it.
And what has been gathered round from it, and is not long, and is bloody or of a dark or black color, and has no sensation; then one should cut an incision into it. For in it there is fear for the weak.
Therefore when you see it according to the way I have said in its whiteness and length, you should make the weak sit before the sun; and press his tongue with the instrument whose description has been given earlier; then insert a hook into the uvula, and pull it downwards; and incise it with one of the two instruments that were mentioned in the incision of the two amygdalae.
And one should not incise from it unless what is added exceeds the natural limit without addition.
For if you incise more than this, you will damage the voice and speech.
Then after the incision use what has been said regarding the incision of the two amygdalae; and care for it until it is healed.
If, however, the weak is afraid of the incision; then one should use art in its cauterization without fear or dread.
The method of cauterization in that case is not except with sharp water: and it is, that you place the head of the sick person in your armpit. Then press his tongue with the instrument mentioned before. Then take water as I said in the chapter on cauterization and make a non-extinguished mortar with it, and do not fill it thick or too thin, and fill the depression of this instrument with it, which has this form:
Let the end of the instrument where the medicine is placed be concave like a conch shell's radius.
Place the instrument with the medicine on the wound itself: and let the sick person lie on his side so that the saliva from his mouth runs out through the intrinsic medicine, so that nothing from it falls into his throat and harms him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you apply it on the wound by handfuls for half an hour until you see it darkened and the biting of the medicine ceased.
And if you want to take a cataplasm, and wrap it around the end of the radius, and pour the cataplasm with medicine over it, and insert the radius with the cataplasm into the tube above until the cataplasm adheres to the wound.
Do that repeatedly until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the vein. Then release it: for indeed it will char and fall off after three or four days.
If you need to repeat the medicine, do so: and after cauterization clean it around the vein with cataplasm soaked in butter, and clean it with that which is in the vicinity of it from the medicine: and rinse it with cold water.
Externally it will be treated with ointments, and internally with emetics, until it is healed.
This therefore is a more beneficial treatment by incising (cutting) and at a greater distance from fear.
And sometimes the ulcer is also cured with a method that is more subtle than cautery and incision; it is cured by suffumigation (suffocating), according to this method. Take camomile, hyssop, origanum (wild marjoram), rutum (rue), sseah (probably an error or misspelling), chamomilla (chamomile), abrotanum (meadowsweet), and similar herbs from plants; gather all of these together, or some of them in a pot, and submerge them with vinegar, and boil; let the pot be well-coated with mortar; and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which an instrument is placed according to this method.
Make it from silver or brass; insert the end, where the grain is, into the sick man's mouth, until the vapor reaches the ulcer through the cannula (a thin tube), until the ulcer is covered a great deal.
Then repeat this many times, until it burns (or heals).
And be careful not to perform this treatment at the beginning of the appearance of an abscess. Usually, however, you should add (something) in an abscess; and it is not appropriate to do this unless near the opening of the abscess at its warm point.
If this instrument is not present with you, then take a cannula and prepare its end with the rind of an ox's horn; so that the bone of the sick man is not burned; because the ox's horn rind prevents the vapor from burning the bone; and this is part of good treatment with benefit.
Â§ On the extraction of thorns and bones from the throat.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Multitiimes an bone adheres to the throat, or a fish spine, or something else.
Therefore, it should be extracted whatever appears visible over which the sight falls after pressing the tongue with the instrument in the sun, and it becomes clear to you that it is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, it should be done with a purgative before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps the thing attached will come out through vomiting.
Or the sick person may swallow a piece of ginger, or the root of lettuce, or a mouthful of dry bread; or he may take a piece of soft dried sea sponge; and tie it up in thread, then swallow it. When it reaches the place where the spine or bone is located, and it is extracted, then it comes out.
If it does not come out as we said; then use an instrument made of lead in this shape.
Make it thicker than the radius a little, and at its end have a bend so that it may be introduced into the throat with ease; and let it have its head raised upward.
And let him beware of touching his epiglottis, lest he coughs, and pushes with it the bone or spine, or the doctor may insert it by hand.
Indeed, what the sick person introduces is better; because of his knowledge of the place of the attached thing; and he pushes downward or draws his hand with the instrument upward, all that according to its quantity which is prepared for him until it comes out.
Chapter on the Extraction of Leeches.
Chapter XXXIX.
When the leech is treated with what I said in the division of cure with medicines, and it does not work; then consider in the throat of the sick person in the sun or after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you, whether anything appears visible over which the sight falls.
If therefore your sight falls upon a leech, remove it with a small hook or with finely pointed tweezers.
If it is not possible with them (the hook or tweezers): then take a concave tube and insert it into the throat of the patient as far as the throat; then insert into the hollow of the tube hot iron with fire. Do this frequently: and let the patient abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take a mouthwash full of cold water, and open his mouth in it; and rinse his mouth with it, and do not swallow anything from it; and move the water one hour after another with his hand. For the leech immediately drops (falls out) when it feels water.
If it does not come out with what we have said, then fumigate the patient with bedbugs or with an asa (fumigantium instrument) that I mentioned for fumigating the ear.
Do this frequently, because it will drop (fall out) by itself.
And the method of operation in fumigating is that you take a pot with live prunes and fire; and let the pot be covered with a cover, in the middle of which there should be a hole; and place the end of the instrument in this hole.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the patient place his mouth at the end of the tube, and close his mouth, so that the fumigation does not escape, until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For the leech will immediately fall out.
If it does not fall out, then repeat the fumigation frequently.
Let the patient endure thirst, and eat salt and other things, but do not let him drink water.
Therefore it is necessary for it to come out with this regimen (treatment).
