And this is the form of the instrument with which a leech is drawn from the throat, when it falls upon it.
It resembles forceps as you see, except that it has a curve which is introduced into the throat. And its tip resembles the beak of a bird called ciconia (cormorant), which has the roughness of a file; when it captures something, it does not release it completely.
Chapter on the opening of abscesses, and their cutting and treatment in general.
Chapter 40.
The species of abscesses are numerous, various according to their remembrance, that is, one and one in this book; and they are different in perforating them, and cutting them from two ways.
One of them is the species of abscess within itself, and that which it encloses due to moistures.
And the second mode is because of places where it happens from the body.
Since an abscess happening on the head is different from an abscess happening in the anus; and an abscess happening in a fleshy place is different from an abscess happening in joints: and each of them has its own judgment according to the operation.
And from abscesses there are some that should not be perforated unless the pus in them has matured and completed; and from these there are some that should be perforated while they are raw, and do not mature according to completion.
As abscesses which are near joints.
Since when an abscess happens near a joint and prolongs to be there until it putrefies what is around it perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, therefore it is the cause of the closer contraction of that member.
The boil is an aposteme in the main member: because if you delay its opening until it matures, it will harm either him or the principal member.
It is near the anus; therefore perforate it while still immature: it is not necessary to perforate a raw aposteme before complete digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply and extend towards the interior of the anus, becoming a fistula or one that will not heal at its end.
You must know the hour of perforating the boil, when it is mature according to its completion; and this is in sedation of pain, withdrawal of fever, decrease of redness, and pulsations, and acuteness of the head of the boil; and the rest of the signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same opening in a lower place of the boil and of greater protrusion: and the perforation should run along the length of the body, if the boils are in parts of the hands and feet, and places of shoulders, and necks, and tendons, and nerves, and finally in all places where there is no reflection.
In those which are reflected, go with the perforation according to that member.
When the boil is in fleshy places: then it is better to delay the opening of it until its digestion has consolidated, as we have said according to its completion.
Because if you perforate it before that, the course of the virus from it is prolonged and there are many dirt and dirty places, and perhaps its lips harden and its depth.
And some boils are opened according to the length of the body for necessity, or according to that which the member needs.
And it is necessary to administer a small opening for small boils and a large opening for large boils; or many sections according to the similarity of the size of the boils.
And there are among the tumors, where the skin should be concave: and it is to be cut when already made like a cloth, and it has become at its end, what is already dead: as that which happens frequently with many, to shrink, and with buboes.
And there are those which are to be cut by a section having three angles. And there is one of them, where it is to be cut like the shape of a myrtle leaf.
As an inguinal tumor.
And there are those in which a circular section and crescent-shaped section is administered, and similar ones from sections.
What is without a head, such as superficial tumors, it is necessary to pierce through it with a surface perforation, or only flat one.
And it is necessary, when the tumor is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, so that it does not burst out and extract all the pus in that hour: instead, extract a part of it from it. Then, open the tumor until another day (for further treatment). Then, extract something again from the pus.
Do this many times according to the degree, until it comes out: especially if he is weak in strength, or a woman pregnant, or a small child, or an old man worn out: for the animal spirit is often resolved with the discharge of pus; and perhaps the sick one dies, and you do not perceive.
Be careful of this chapter, with great caution.
And after your perforation, where you pierce the tumors, it is necessary to clean the wound: and examine. If therefore the wound of the tumor is small, or the section is flat, then administer a linen cloth, or an old copper sheet. If there is a large abscess and many openings of the perforation, then it is necessary to insert linen into every opening until they meet each other.
If you have removed a part of the skin from an abscess or if you have hollowed it out around it, then it is necessary to fill it with old cloth, or as when a fabric is sewn, or shorn with linen wool without wetness; and tighten it for three days.
Then remove it (the cloth or dressing), and care for that place with whatever is necessary from an ointment until it heals.
If there is bleeding during your operation hour, then administer cold water and vinegar; after it has been soaked in them, place a cloth on the site of bleeding multiple times.
If the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer a treatment and cure, and powders which I have mentioned in many places of this our book and from division (of the body).
If it is winter time and the abscess site involves many nerves, then it is necessary to pour powders with warm wine and oil on them; and place them on the locations.
And if it is summer and the sites are fleshy, then it is necessary to place powders soaked in water, oil, or with wine and oil, and make everything cold. Until the third day, as we have said, it is necessary to solve the abscess, remove it, and administer whatever is appropriate for its cure until it heals.
This is therefore what is generally necessary for the knowledge of treating abscesses universally.
According to the method of division (of the body), I have already said about every abscess, how is the way to treat it individually and chapter by chapter.
Cirurgia de baculo manibus et pedibus
On the sectioning of skin tumors that occur on the head.
In the head small tumors called nodules occur, which are contained by sacs of the skin that resemble pouches of a hen's egg.
And their types are many.
Among them are the fat ones; among them are those that contain moisture like mud; among them are those that contain moisture like ointments and powders; and similar to these, and among them are hard stone-like ones.
And in the section of all, and in their extraction there is no fear, as long as their section does not oppose an artery.
The operation in their section is to test it with the instrument, whose form comes after these, which is called Intromissum, until you know what it contains.
For if that which it contains is wetness, then cut it with a section according to its length with a surface section: according to this shape.
And begin with a section from line b to line g. For when the wetness escapes, then scrape off the bladder which contains that wetness, and do not leave anything inside of it.
For many times it returns if something remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt; fill the wound with it, and leave it until another day. For it corrodes what remains from the bladder.
Then repeat over the wound with second Egyptian ointment, and third, and if necessary, until you are confident that nothing remains from the bladder, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If an abscess contains a thick knot: then cut it according to this shape, with a section having the shape of a cross; and throw the hooks between the two parts of the section, and scrape off the entire thing from every part; and try your strength in the extraction of the covering that contains it.
If, however, it opposes an artery for you, then do what I will tell you afterwards.
And the same applies to an abscess if it is stone-like, by section and the same treatment, as we have said.
The section on a stone-like abscess is easier: because there is little blood and wetness. And sometimes there are some of these abscesses that are in the head in certain men, in whom there is not deep moistness.
I have cut over an abscess on an old woman's head, and I found the abscess to be as hard and solid as a stone, rough, white, which could not be broken: and if anyone struck it with something, he would wound himself.
In other cases of abscesses in the head (except for these abscesses that happen on children's heads and at the roots of the ears), the cutting of all of them should be a superficial cut.
Or, make a perforation in them always from the lower part, so that the course of pus may be directed downward.
Then care for it with what is suitable to it from the cure.
Chapter on the incision of goiter (enlarged thyroid gland) in the neck.
Chapter 42.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, and under the shoulders, and groins; and sometimes they occur elsewhere in the body.
And on those that occur in the neck, there is one and many; they originate from opposite sides; and every goiter arising from them is within its own layer, like a knot or abscess of the head, as we have said.
And the types of these goiters are many. For they are hard (lapideae): and there are those that contain moistness: and there are evil ones, which do not obey the cure.
Therefore, when you see a good disposition in the touch of one of them (which is evident by its proximity to the skin color and moves in all directions and is not attached to the neck muscles, groin or artery, and is shallow): it should be cut off with a superficial incision from the top to the lower part of the body along the line, b. to the line, g. And remove the scab from all sides: and spread two layers of skin with an uncured or with many uncured, if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head, and slowly extract it.
And it is above the cautery, that a vein or nerve should not be cut.
And the blade should not be very sharp: so that it does not injure your hand during the incision or distress the sick person, and you cut what is not necessary.
If, however, you cut a vein or artery, then stop the operation, place on the wound some crushed antimony or certain powders that dissolve blood, and tighten the wound, and leave it alone until the sharpness of the cautery subsides and the wound becomes soft: or it begins to putrefy.
For blood is drained through the ligature, therefore go back to your operation when you have finished.
Then ask your index finger if anything remains of the stylets or other small things: therefore cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the root of the stylet, then it should not be cut from its root: rather, it should be tied with strong doubled thread and left to fall by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with a lining of old cloth that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then care for him (the patient).
If the stylet is completely cut through, then join together the lips of the wound: and suture it immediately, after you see that there remains no excess.
If, however, you see that there remains an excess due to the size of the stylet, then you should aim at cutting its root and pulling it out: and apply the suture as we have said.
And what contains humidity from the stylets, pierce it through a superficial perforation: so that you can see the maturity of its place: and position the perforation below the following part of the body, as we have said.
After perforation, administer linseed with ointment, and similar substances, to consume what remains from corruption, until you see the wound already clean: then care for it with regenerative flesh ointment, until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
On the trachea cut due to an ulcer within the throat.
The ancients said this trachea cut, and I did not see anyone in our land who has done it; and this is their writing.
In those with synangiosis (tongue-swallowing), it is necessary to avoid trachea cut; for there is no advantage in doing so because all the veins and lungs are weak.
In those who have a hot ulcer in the mouth, throat, or both tonsils, when there is no sickness in the channel, it is necessary to use trachea cut to prevent death from suffocation.
Therefore, when we wish to cut the trachea, it should be cut under three or four circles of the trachea, with a small cut across its width, in that which is between two circles, and the cut should be in the cartilage, not in the bone: this place is suitable for cutting because it is without meat, and blood vessels are far away from it.
If the doctor is afraid, then it is necessary that he stretch the throat skin with a hook. Then he should cut the skin until he reaches the channel; he should avoid blood vessels if he sees any of them.
Then he should cut the cartilage as we said; it is indicated by the phlegm that comes out from the channel when it is ruptured, and by the voice being lost.
And leave the open wound for some time.
When therefore the hour is removed in which perforation is feared, join together two lips of the wound's skin, and its own sole without cartilage.
Then administer medications that make flesh grow, until it heals.
Says Albucasis. The conclusion of the story we have told is as follows: Albucasis says that if any one of these abscesses has already opened the throat of a sick person, and he is raised up above death and wants to cut his breath, they go to cut the Epiglottis so that the sick person may breathe over the place of the wound with some breathing, and thus be saved from death. And for this reason they commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease is consumed, and its malice lasts three days, as if it were itself. Then, therefore, they commanded to close the wound and take care of it until it heals.
And that which I have seen with my own eyes is the following: a maidservant seized a knife and sent it into her own throat, and cut a piece of the windpipe of the lungs.
And I was summoned to heal her, and found her moaning, as is the moan of the dead.
Therefore, I looked at the wound, and found that blood had come out from the wound, albeit in small quantity. Consequently, I was convinced that she had not severed the vein or the windpipe, and air was coming out from the wound.
I approached therefore, and closed the wound, and healed it until it was well; and nothing happened to the maidservant, except hoarseness of voice; and she returned after some days to a better condition.
From this I say that there is no fear in cutting the Epiglottis.
On the section of hernia of the throat.
Title XLIV.
This swelling named hernia of the throat is a large swelling, according to the color of the body; and it occurs much in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either it is natural; or it is accidental.
Certainly, in the natural one, there is no birth defect.
Accidental is, according to two modes: one of which is similar to fatty nodes. And the other mode, is similar to an abscess that occurs due to a knot in an artery. And in the same (accidental or abscess), there is fear, and it should not be presumed with iron unless it is small: and you examine it and investigate it with a probe. If you find it similar to a fatty node and it is not suspended by any veins: then cut it, as knots are cut; and remove it with the surrounding tissue from a chest, if it is in a chest: and if not, then examine the entire area thoroughly. Then care for the place with what is necessary for treatment, until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
Chapter on the Surgical Treatment of Knots.
Chapter XLV: There are many kinds of knots, and I have already said all their species in the division: it is necessary that here I explain the difference between a knot and an abscess, when there is doubt.
Therefore, when an abscess is hot, and fever, and violent pains, until the boiling of the excess subsides and the rotting is completed: then the fever and heat subside.
However, when there is no heat, nor fever, nor pain in a knot, and it contains them within a chest or sac that is proper to it: and it is closed like a pea, and made like a bun, and larger or smaller.
And they are of two kinds: either fatty; or containing moisture. And the colors of moistures are many, according to what I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you approach the treatment of a knot, it is necessary to examine and investigate it first with an instrument called a probe, according to what its form will be, as it will come in the chapter that follows this one.
The method of investigation for boils and all nodes is to receive this tool and insert it into the moist place you find in the boil: and you rotate your fingers with it gradually until you know that the tool has already penetrated the skin. Then, lay your hand according to the measure of the size of the boil.
Then remove what has been inserted and observe what comes out as its trace.
If therefore moisture running out comes forth, whatever its color is: then cut it off with a superficial incision, according to what I said in the other boils.
And if moisture does not come out as a trace of what has been inserted, then you know it is greasy: so cut above it with an incision in the shape of a cross, according to this form, just as I taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and scrape off the skin from all sides easily: and keep a box if possible over it, so that you extract the healthy one along with the node.
But if it bursts open in the box during the operation and it is not possible to extract the healthy one, then remove it fragmentarily until there remains something of it.
For if something remains little or much, the node returns to a great extent.
If it overpowers you and something remains little: then fill the wound up to your completion with some corrosive sharp powders: and bind the wound, and place on it what sits the boil warm, and care for it with the rest of the cure until it heals.
If therefore the node is large, then cut open two lips of it and care for it with that which fills in.
But if it is pulsating vein for you or not pulsating, then hurry and fill the place with lime powder: and leave it compressed for two or three days until the wound putrefies and the boiling of blood quiets down: then return to cut what remains from the node.

Chapter on the care of human breasts resembling women's breasts.
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to defile during sleep), becoming like women's breasts and remaining abscessed with a foul smell.
Who, therefore, recoils from it (the procedure), should cut across the mammary gland according to the shape of a crescent moon, following this form from line b to line g. Then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat and administer what I said about stitching and powders necessary for treatment until it heals.

On the perforation of an abscess which occurs under the titillicus (a part of the cheek or jaw).

These abscesses which occur under the titillicus are of the types of stubborn boils that contain pus, and there are those that contain moisture.

Chapter 49.
Chapter on the section of tumors due to an artery or vein.
When an artery ruptures and the skin above it consolidates, there often occurs a tumor; similarly, this happens with veins so that a tumor and swelling occur in them.
And the signs by which it is known that a tumor and swelling are due to an artery or vein are as follows: because when the tumor is due to an artery, it is long, aggregated in the depth of the body; and when you press the tumor with your fingers, it feels like there is a grating sensation.
What concerns the vein is round in evident body.
And the incision upon this boil is an error, especially if it is under armpits, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very great. Therefore, its care must be avoided with the iron, and what is also from them in the extremities or head, it must be avoided.
Therefore, above that which arises from the swelling of the orifice of the Artery, find incision in the skin's length. Then open the incision with scissors, then the Artery; and release it from tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert a needle beneath it and make it penetrate to the other side; and tie the Artery with double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in extracting two Arteries which are in temples.
Then pierce the place between two ligaments with a lancet until all the blood comes out, and the boil is dissolved.
Then administer a treatment that produces pus, until the ligaments fall; then care for it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the boil is from the incision of a vein, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand what possible for you from the boil along with the skin. Then insert a needle beneath the place which you held with your hand; and make it penetrate; and let there be double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then bind with the same boil a good ligament; according to what I told you in ligating a vein, with two parts and two ends of thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be drawn out, then insert another needle with a different thread beneath the entire boil near the incision; press and tie your threads in four places.
Then cut the boil in the middle of it, until when it comes out what is inside: then cut the excess skin and release what was bound from it.
Then place on top of the boil that you have immersed in wine, and oil. Then administer the cure, which is made with lints and oils, until it is healed.
Title: L. (Presumably "Libellus
Chapter on boil occurring from twisting of nerves.
As it happens with boil on the Artery and Vein, similarly it happens with boil on Nerves: which occurs from strike or excessive labor or similar: it mostly occurs at places of joints, ankles or any place where joints are moved: and the boil is heavy.
It resembles the color of the rest of the body, and is in many positions without pain: and when it is squeezed with great force, one feels weak like faintness in it.
And the boil is not gathered deep within the body, rather it is under the skin, and itself moves to every part, and does not reach forward or anterior nor backward to posterior areas.
Therefore, what is in joints should not be penetrated with iron. For perhaps it may be a contraction.
However, in that which is in the head or forehead, puncture the skin with a lancet. If the boil is small, then hold it with forceps and remove it from the root.
And if it is large, then hang it with a hook and remove the covering: afterwards remove it, and close the wound with suture: then treat it until it is healed.
Title: LII (presumably "Libellus
Chapter on incision of boil occurring in abdomen.
Occur frequently to some men in their bellies, and in the remaining parts of their bodies, a growth called "Fungalia," resembling fungi.
Its root is subtle, and its head is thick, and they have turned lips. And there is something small from them, and there is something from them that is greatly increased.
I myself have already seen a man, and in his belly there were two growths, which resembled fungi more than anything else; there was no difference between them, white, with small roots, and their lips were turned back, and they were swollen, and liquid flowed from them constantly.
I cut them, and found that one weighed approximately 10 â ounces and the other approximately 6 ounces. For many times blood is expelled during the cutting of it; therefore, if blood overpowers you, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak, fearful, and timid person from the cutting with iron, then take a well-made lead thread, and bind it with it to the athelul; whose method is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add to the narrowing of the lead. Therefore do not cease to bind the lead, as long as it presses into the growth, until it is cut off and falls out by itself without effort.

Chapter LII.
Chapter on the care of umbilical hernia.
A protrusion of the umbilicus occurs for many reasons. It arises either from hernias of the sciatic vein, which is above the abdomen, and exits through the anus, or it is intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. It arises either from blood flowing from a vein, or from an artery, as was mentioned before. It arises from a constricted wind there.
But if it is due to a hernia of the sciatic vein and the passage of worms: then it has the color of an abscess, similar to the body's color; it is soft, without pain; and its position appears to be diverse. And if it is due to the exit of intestine: then its position, as we have said, has a more violent diversity. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden; then it returns and perhaps there is a sound; and it swells greatly at the opening of the bath and causes strong pain.
If it is due to moisture: then it is soft; it does not hide when pressed with your hand, nor is it constricted, nor does it swell.
If it is due to blood: then with these signs appears an abscess turning black from the navel.
But if it is due to fleshy matter: then the abscess is heavy, large, hard, and heals in one portion.
If it is due to windiness: then when touched, it is soft.
The operation in this case is to determine whether the protrusion of the umbilicus is due to blood from an artery or vein, windiness, or moisture. Then it is necessary to prevent treatment of it. For there is fear and terror, as I taught you in the chapter where I said abscesses due to an artery and vein.
If the protrusion of the umbilicus is due to the intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you instruct the sick one, so that he holds his breath and stands extended. Then mark with the hot iron around the entire umbilicus. Then instruct him to lie down beneath your hands on his back. Then circle with a broad spatula around the umbilicus over the place you marked with the hot iron. Then stretch out the midriff of the incision upward with a large hook. Then bind him around with strong thread or silk cord, and the knot should be the knot of an embroiderer's knot.
Then open up the extended midriff incision above the ligament. If indeed you find it already seized by the ligament: then extract it (the hernia), and insert your index finger into it and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen; and if you find a hernia, then take it with a hook and cut off the excess of it.
But if it is an artery or vein against you: then tie it (the hernia) tightly. Then return to your operation. And take two needles and insert strong threads into them; and insert two needles into the circle you made around the abscess in the form of a cross, which you pierce through.
Then stitch the abscess in four places over the needles; and if you wish, remove the needles and leave the place until the rotten flesh extends and falls off by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and rots.
Then take care of him with the things he needs from unguents until he is healed.
If the protrusion of the umbilicus is from a tumor in him or due to moisture: then make a hollow in the abscess, as we have said. And draw out blood or moisture which you find there.
Then care for it with what solidifies the place.
Chapter LIII.
Chapter on the Care of Cancer.
We have already said in the division of species of Cancer, and how the way to its treatment with medicines; and it must be cautioned against using iron for its treatment lest it is wounded; we have also said that Cancer is generated in the matrix, and warned against cauterization in its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes Cancer is at a place where it can be eradicated; such as cancer which is in breasts or hips and similar limbs, which are situated to extract its entirety; especially when it begins small.
But when it becomes old and large, one should not approach it closely.
For I was unable to heal anyone from that; nor did I see anyone before me reach that point.
And the operation on it, when it is situated as we have said, is to precede and dissolve a weak person from black cholera several times. Then phlebotomy that person if you find him with manifest congestion.
Then prepare the sick person with a preparation in which the operation is performed.
Then thrust awls into the Cancer which fit it. Then hollow out the person from all sides with skin, according to examination, until nothing remains of its roots; and let the blood flow, and do not cut or tear it quickly, rather press on the places, and remove the thick blood entirely with your hand, or as much as possible with instruments there.
If, however, the flow of thick blood from an incision of an artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then, take care of yourself with the rest of the treatment until you are healed.
On the treatment of Hydrophysis.
Chapter LIV. We now narrate on the division of types of Hydropsis, and how water accumulates; and the signs of all its species, and its cure along with medicines.
And the one that is to be cured with iron, is not but the sole species of ascites; it does not approach with iron the species of tympana; neither deeply the species of hypoascia, for that is fatal.
When you are already treated with medicines for this species of hydropsis of the tympana and your treatment has not helped; then consider. For if the patient has already been weakened or there is another ailment apart from hydropsis such as cough, bowel looseness, and similar; then beware of treating him with iron, for it is dangerous.
But if you see the patient overflowing with strength and no other ailment except hydropsis alone; and he is neither a child nor an old man; then there is a method of operation in him, that you raise the weakened one standing between your hands, and a servant after him presses out his abdomen with his hand forcing the water down towards the lower part of the chest.
Then take a thorny catheter (spathulum spinosum), shaped like this. It should have two pointed parts, long, with sharp tips like a catheter. However, there should be something shortening it slightly, so as not to penetrate with it up to the intestines during the operation and harm it.
Then consider. For if the hydropsis is generated from the intestines, then you should extend with a section of three fingers' length below the navel towards the lower part beyond the chest.
But if the hydropsis is generated from a liver ailment; then your section should be on the left side, three fingers' length below the navel.
If the generation is due to the spleen, then let the section be on the right side: and it is not necessary that the section also be on the side towards which the sick man lies, lest excess fluids flow towards the weak location.
Then pierce the skin completely with the instrument. Then insert your hand into that incision, and push the Spatula-like instrument under the skin, as if you are scraping it; and let the quantity scraped off be equal to a fingernail or about that much.
Then pierce the Spatula until it reaches the empty place; and that is the watery location. Then remove it (the organ), and insert the instrument into the opening, which has this form. And it resembles a cannula: made of silver, copper or gold, cleaned; at its lower part there is a small hole, and on both sides there are three holes, two from one side, and one from the other side; its end is cut in the manner of a incision of a reed, as you see; at the upper end of it there is a strap.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then the water immediately descends upon the instrument, therefore evacuate from the water a middle amount (of urine).
Because if you evacuate more than necessary from it (the water), perhaps the sick man will die from resolution of his animal spirit; or he may have a fainting spell approaching death.
But evacuate from it (the water) according to its potency, and according to what the dispositions of the sick man indicate through his pulse, and the quality of it.
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
This is because it is immediately retained due to the skin that holds the hole above the Spatula; which I told you to pierce in this manner.
Then on the second day, if you see that the patient can bear it, repeat the operation; and extract also a small amount from water.
Be careful in the days to come, and avoid error; until there remains in water only a little.

It often occurs that these Albathars happen in the penis, and it is a swelling of foul flesh.

Chapter LVII.
Section on the cleansing of infants and treatment due to an error occurring in them.
Circumcision is not a solution for continuity, as are other wounds; nevertheless, since it comes from our operation, our will, and its use is proper to boys, it is necessary that we mark in it an improvement in the operation and an easier way leading to health.

I have found that most artists and blood-letterers use cleaning by circumcising with a knife and with forceps: they employ the application of ointment, binding with thread, and cutting with a nail.
And indeed I have already proven all those methods, and I did not find a better cleaning method with forceps, or binding with thread.
Because in circumcision with a knife, the skin is often missed. Because the foreskin has two layers of skin: perhaps the outer layer is cut and the inner layer is torn: it is therefore necessary to make an incision to cut the other one, and pain will result. And when cleaning is done with the application of ointment, that is, digitally (as surgeons do), it is not cut off at the tip of the male organ: because perhaps it enters its opening.
But in circumcision with a nail, perhaps the iron will enter and ruin your operation: and indeed the skin of children is naturally short, and often such cases occur that do not require cleaning: I have already seen this.
But the cleaning with forceps and binding with thread showed me a good experiment: because the forceps are proportionate to the incision: therefore, the sharpness that is above is like the sharpness that is below. And since you press your hand together, the two sharpnesses are proportionate, and they cut according to one operation in one time: and a compression is made in a similar shape, containing the skin of the penis from all sides, with which there is no possible mistake at all.
The method of the operation is that you shall make him estimate, primarily a boy if he understands slightly, which you do not do except that you tie a thread on his rod alone; and you shall release him until another day.

Then peel off the skin quickly upward, and extract the head of the rod. Then let the blood flow slowly (for it is better), and place powder on top; and on the powder place a cloth in which a boiled lamb's wool has been spread out, mashed with fresh rose oil; and leave him on this until another day; and take care of the rest of his healing until he is healed.
The form of the scissors for cleaning is as follows.
Let them have two sharp points, and let them be concave; let no branch of the nail come out on them; and let the length of two cutting edges be equal to the length of two handles equally.
However, if an error occurs in cleaning, it is because perhaps the inner skin escapes completely or a part of it near the incision.

If you cannot hold it with your nail, then pull it out with a forceps and cut it.

It will not harm him that.

Therefore take care of it with that which we have said until it heals.

Retention of urine in the bladder is caused by an obstruction made of stone, congealed blood, pus, flesh born, and similar things from those which we have said in the treatment methods in division.

Chapter LX (Roman numeral for sixty)
[Title: Extraction of a Stone]
We have already said about the nature of the Stone and its treatment with medicines, and the difference between the Stone generated in kidneys, bladder, and its signs altogether; we have also said that the operation on the Stone is performed by hand and section; and it is the Stone generated specifically in the bladder that is meant; and he who is formed in the penis; and I am telling this with manifest explanation and abbreviation.
The Stone generated in the bladder happens most often to children.
And among its signs is that urine comes out from the bladder similar to water in thinness; and it appears there white sand, and the sick man rubs his penis, and labors with it, and often hangs down. Then it erects, and comes out together with the anus in many of them.
The cure for children is easy until they reach the age of fourteen. And it is difficult in old people. In young men it is of medium difficulty, because it is between that and its size; and the larger the Stone, the easier the cure; and if it is small, the reverse is true for the cure.
When we arrive at the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the sick man with an enema, which removes all feces that are in his bowels; because sometimes it hinders the discovery of the Stone during the investigation.
Then the sick man is received with his feet, beaten, and moved downward; so that the Stone descends to the bottom of the bladder or sometimes jumps from a high place.
Then make him sit between your hands, and his hands should be under his hips; so that the bladder becomes completely descended towards the lower part.
Then examine him and touch him externally.
If therefore you feel a stone in the space, then hurry immediately with cutting upon it.
If it does not fall under your touch entirely, then you should push aside the finger of the right hand with oil, if the patient is a weak child; or the middle finger if the patient is an adult man; and insert it into its own anus, and inquire about the stone, until it lies beneath your finger; and gradually turn it towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger and push it towards the outside against the place where you wish to make an incision; and command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another attendant to extend the testicles of the right hand upwards; and with the other hand, remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part from the place where the incision is to be made.
Then insert a spatula cutting tool, which has this shape. And find it where it is between the anus and testicles, not in the middle, on the side of the left buttock; and make the incision over the stone, and your finger should be in the anus; and make the incision transverse, so that the incision is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the quantity by which the exit of the stone from it may not be greater.
For perhaps the finger presses the stone that is in the anus at the incision, and comes out without difficulty.
And know that from the stone are its corners and edges, for this reason the exit of it is difficult because of that.
And from it is smooth, like a nut, and round; and the exit of it is easy.
To him who has corners and edges, add them into the incision.
If it does not come out in this way, then you should pierce it; or tighten it over it with pliers, whose end is like the moon, which presses on the stone and does not slip off from it; or insert a sharp tool under it, curved at its tip.
If however you cannot go over it, then widen the opening slightly. If something in the blood opposes you, cut it out with scissors.
If there are more than one stone(s), first drive a large one into the bladder bone. Then cut upon it. Then push in a smaller one after that, and do the same if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then ignorance is to cut through it with a great incision. Since it happens to the sick that either one of two things occurs, namely death or continuous discharge of urine; therefore, because there is no consolidation in the place at all.
But administer its expulsion until it comes out; or bind up the fracture of it with forceps, until you draw it out piece by piece.
When you have therefore completed your operation, then fill the wound with turpentine, aloe, and dragon's blood; bind it up and place upon it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water; that the abscess may settle down warm.
Then turn the sick person on his neck and do not unbind the bindings until the third day. When you unbind it, smear the place with oil and water.
Then treat him with diaphinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until he is healed.
If, however, an abscess hot and corrosive is added to the wound, and similar things occur as if the blood congeals in the bladder, and urine is prevented from coming out of it; and it is known that this occurs through the discharge of blood along with urine. Therefore, insert your finger into the wound and draw out the blood. If it remains, it provokes the corruption of the bladder, and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt; and apply any remedy that agrees with its cure until it heals.
It is necessary during the entire period of treatment that bandages be applied to both thighs and joined together, because of the medicaments placed upon the site.
If the stone is small and is in the channel of the spermatic cord, and it obstructs the flow of urine; then treat it with what I have mentioned earlier before reaching the section. For often you are excused from this treatment by means of the operation, for I have already proven that.

Then take thread, and tie it around the spermatic cord beneath the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then introduce the perforating iron into the spermatic cord with ease, until the Perforator reaches the stone; and rotate the Perforator in the stone slowly with your hand; and you will make a hole in it, until you cause it to penetrate from the other side.
For urine is immediately released.
Then press your hand upon what remains of the stone from the outside part of the spermatic cord. It breaks and is released with the urine, and the weak man becomes well.
If this treatment is not prepared for you because of something that prevents it from being done; then tie thread beneath the stone and another thread above the stone. Then cut across the spermatic cord above the stone between the two bindings. Then extract it. After that, loosen the ligament, and clean up the frozen blood which is made in the wound.
It is not necessary to tie a thread under the stone, unless it does not return to the bladder: and another ligament on top, unless when the thread is loosened after the stone's departure, the skin returns to its place, and covers the wound: and for this reason, you must do that when you tie a thread above, in order to lift the skin towards the higher parts, so that it returns to its complement, and covers the wound, as we said.

Chapter 62.

A watery tumor is not anything but an accumulation of moisture within the albucocycle, which is situated under the skin of the testicle and is called albucocycle.

Chapter on the Care of Branches, which is about Vine.

Then make a cut with a broad sharp transverse saw, until the vessels are exposed.
Then scrape off from all sides, as we told you in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Then insert into them a hook with double thread and tie it at the first knots where they occur (knots called vites): and tie it again at the end of them. Then cut it through a central straight section according to the length of the body and pull out what accumulates from foul, rotten humors.
Then take care of the wound as you would other wounds that generate pus, so that the vessels supplying one testicle are cut off. It is not bad through it (in the sense of an operation or treatment).
If all the vessels are affected by knots, then they must be removed for this reason, because the testicles will not receive nourishment due to the incision, and it will rot or burn, and not be useful with them.
Chapter LXV (Roman numerals).
Chapter on the care of the intestines.
The passage of the intestines occurs by a cut that happens when the sigmoid colon is extended over the abdomen in the inguinal part of the stomach.
Why do the intestines fall out from that rupture towards one testicle. And this hernia is either through the scrotum (sifach), or by its extension.
These two types of hernia occur through many causes: either by striking, jumping, shouting, lifting heavy objects, and similar things.
The sign is when it is from the extension of the scrotum (sifach). It occurs gradually over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; it is an abscess equal in size to the depth; for this reason, the scrotum compresses the intestine.
The sign of it (hernia) is when it is from the section of the scrotum, because it causes a sudden severe pain at the beginning; and it is an abscess different, appearing near the skin; and this is due to the exit of the intestine, and its flow to the outer parts of the scrotum.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine (intestines), and this is called an Intestinal Branch, and a worm; and sometimes it happens with diarrhea.
And sometimes feces run into the intestine and are retained there; and it is with this that the danger of illness occurs; because it causes severe pain, especially when pressed.
And in the treatment of the types of this disease with iron there is fear; therefore, one must be careful about accidents in it.
And the method of operation is to command the sick person to put the intestine back into his own concavity with his own hand, if he obeys the return. Then he lies on his back on top of his neck between your hands; and elevate his legs.
Then extend the skin following the skin to the upper part, and cut the entire skin of the testicles along its length. Then make two hooks at the lips of the incision, according to what is needed for opening the incision with them; and the incision should be according to its quantity so that it can come out from there an egg (ovum).
Then scrape the scrotum, and what is beneath the skin of the testicles, until the scrotum becomes white all over: then insert your index finger into the area following the testicle, into that which is between the white part of the scrotum, which is under the skin of the eye, and between the second part of the scrotum, and without any adherence to it from the posterior part of the eye.
Then with your right hand move towards the inner skin of the testicles: and as you do this, stretch the white part of the scrotum upward, with your left hand: and lift the egg with the scrotum to the cutting part: and command the servant to extend the egg upward: and you separate the adherence that is behind the complete separation.
And examine your fingers whether there is nothing there from the rolled-up intestine in the hard white scrotum. If, however, you find anything from it [the egg]: then push it down to the lower belly.
Then take a sharp instrument with a thick thread made of linen from ten threads, and insert it into the last part of the scrotum, that is, the covering which follows the skin of the testicles: then cut the ends protruding from the thread until there are four threads. Then make some of them [the four threads] crosswise with a figure in the form of a cross and tie the scrotum that we spoke of, which is the covering of the testicles with a strong ligament, so that no juices that nourish them can pass to it: lest there be a hot abscess. And place another ligament outside the first one at least two fingers' length away from it. And after these two ligaments, release from the scrotum, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity equivalent to the size of a finger: and cut the rest all around in a round shape and remove the egg.
Then cut off the lower part of the scrotal skin with a section where blood and pus run, as we said in what was mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound; and apply the bandage as we said. And sometimes cauterize the white pus of leprosy (sifach) which we mentioned, after making an incision, fearing blood flow. It often happens this way. And remove the bandage until it falls off by itself.
If the case lingers, then foment with warm water; and place on top of it what we said, until it falls off.
Then care for the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until it heals.
Chapter 66.
Chapter on Bloated Abdomen.
In this swollen abdomen, I have not seen anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
And indeed, the first ones said that it happens as we described in swollen abdomen which is associated with worms (Vite).\] That is to say, to tie the vessels after cutting them below, then cut in the middle; and finally treat it with what opens it until the vessels fall out; and care for the wound as we said, until it heals.
Chapter 67.
Chapter on Dislocation that happens in the thighs.
When dislocation occurs in the thighs as we said, and a place appears and something from the intestines does not come out towards the testicles; and if it comes out, it is little and returns to its place every hour; but if it persists for a time, a fissure is added in leprosy (sifach), until the intestines descend into sifach.
And this happens due to the extension of leprosy (sifach) in the thighs as we said. That is, because it is extended, then it is softened, and the place is excised, and it protrudes.
And its care is with the cautery, as its previous narrative has said.
And at times it is cured with iron, in this manner: and it is that it lies weak on its back between your hands. Then cut the place of Rupture and protrusion, with a cut in width, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then bind the sifak and what is under the skin until when the white sifak appears, which is under the skin following it.
Then take a probe, and put it on the protruding place from the sifak, and press it to the depth of the intestines.
Then two places protrude at the end of the radius from the sifak, and connect them with a suture one to another: then extract the end of the radius.
And do not cut the sifak at all, nor stretch the egg, nor anything else, as I have taught you in the cure of intestinal branches.
Then take care of that with the treatment of wounds. And when you cut threads, clean it, and restore the wound, until it is consolidated.
Indeed, sifak contracts and no protrusion of rupture is added.
And the cautery is better in this place: because it is closer to health.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Chapter on the softening of the scrotum skin.
Many times the scrotum skin is softened in certain men, on account of which the meat that is between them is softened, and its appearance becomes foul.
Therefore it is necessary for him who is asked about its cure to make it lie weak on his back, and to cut the entire skin that has been softened over the natural skin.
Then gather the two lips together with a stitch; and if you wish, or rather to remove excess skin softened, use three or four stitches, and make a firm one.
Then cut between the stitches.
Then take care of the treatment of the remaining wounds until they heal and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXIX.
Chapter on Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden by our law; and on account of this, it was permissible for me not to mention it in my book; and it is unnecessary to remember it except for two reasons.
One reason is that it should be known by the physician when he is asked about it; and so that he knows its treatment when it happens to someone.
And the second reason is that we often need castration of certain animals for our benefit through it, such as sheep, goats, and cats and similar animals from among the animals.
I therefore say that castration is done in two ways. Or by attrition (castrating with a rough cloth).\]  Aut Or by making a cut and sectioning (surgical castration).\]  Ubi prius amputatum
In the case of castration by attrition, the method of operation is that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and become relaxed and hang down; then you rub them with your hand until they resolve and are no longer noticeable when touched.
In the case of surgical castration, it is necessary to hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then bind the suspension, and cut through everything above the egg with one section until when two eggs come out; then cut that part after you scrape off the scrotum of both, and do not leave anything on top of it except the thin sifaket, which is over vessels.
This method of castration is better than the one done by grinding: because grinding perhaps leaves something from the testicles, therefore the animal desires copulation.
Then, care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter LXX.
Chapter on the care of Hermaphrodite in two ways.
Hermaphrodite is from men according to two modes. One of them is that it appears in him what follows the space or in the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, in the form similar to a female vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine flows out of it from the skin of the testicles.
But in women there is one form and it is a female vulva on top of the comb-like structure like those of small male testicles protruding to the outside; of which one is like a priapus of man, and two like two male testicles.
And the care of three forms, two from men and one from women, is: because it is necessary that you cut the added flesh, until the impression of them disappears. Then, care for them with the care of other wounds.
But in the second form of men, from which urine comes out, which is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation and no care at all for it.
Chapter LXXI.
Chapter on the incision of warts and protruding flesh in female sores.
Warts are added over the natural thing, until it becomes ugly and its appearance is disfigured; and sometimes they become enlarged so much in some women that they spread like in men, and they reach copulation.
Therefore, it is necessary that you hold the surplus of warts with your hand or a hook and cut it; and do not go to the end in cutting, especially in deep roots: so that blood flow does not occur.
Then care for it with wound treatment until it heals.
A boil that arises is the flesh which is born in the opening of the matrix, until it fills itself up; and perhaps it goes out to the outside similar to the tail; and because of this some call the illness 'tailed'. Therefore, it is necessary that we cut it like we would cut a boil, and treat it until it heals.
On the treatment of an Alratic ulcer, which is an unperforated woman's ulcer.
Chapter LXXII.
An Alratic ulcer is when it is a woman's unperforated ulcer or there is a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
An accidental Alratic ulcer is due to an illness that has preceded; and it forms either from flesh born added to it, or from subcutaneous tissue, or from the skin; and it forms either in the depth of the matrix, or in its sides, or above it, or below it; and it prevents coitus, impregnation, parturition, and perhaps menstruation.
Its recognition is made through the examination of an obstetrician if the opening appears near.
If it is not visible, then search for it with your fingers or with a probe.
If the opening is from subcutaneous tissue and is near two lips, then apply pressure and break it open.
It is, so that you place poultices on top of two lips.
Then place your fingers of both hands together and the woman should be over her back with her legs spread out. Then separate the two lips with force until the subcutaneous tissue is broken and the opening is opened.
Then take wool, wet it in oil and place it on the location; and let the woman sit there every day so that the location does not harden due to another illness.
If however the boil is large and thick: then it is necessary that you cut it with a broad lancet, similar to a myrtle leaf.
If the boil is born from flesh, then suspend it with hooks and cut it; have medicines that stop the flow of blood without causing pain, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
Then administer a wide cannula made of lead to prevent the wound from closing quickly; hold it for several days; then apply linen cloth, followed by the usual treatment until it heals.
And sometimes a birth of flesh from the matrix occurs for others: it is therefore necessary to cut it according to this method: until there is no abscess; because an abscess that is cancerous should not be opposed to iron in any way.
Chapter LXXIII.
Chapter on the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil and Bothor for women with red wounds.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the opening of vein orifices until blood continuously runs out in large amounts.
When hemorrhoids have become chronic, they turn into thrombus; and I have already said about their kinds, and the signs of them; and here I will say what receives treatment from them and what does not.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids that are in the opening of the matrix and do not appear to the senses: then there is no treatment with iron.
But those from them that are in the opening of the matrix over which sensation falls can be treated.
It is therefore necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then stretch out Athehelil with hooks or with rough cloth and cut them from their roots.
Then pulverize it over them at the flow of blood from one incision without biting: as acacia, and dragon's blood, and asafoetida, and similar ones.
Then push his feet against the wall at one hour. Then put her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and of pomegranate bark, and of tannins, and similar ones.
Then take barley flour, and knead it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If the blood is cut off along with it, that is good: and if not, make adhesive bladders or breasts, without scarification.
Then take wool, and dip it in the juice of thistle, or the juice of argol, or the juice of alaoult leaves, that is, aglant root, wine from Pontus, and make it stick to the wound.
When the abscess is quiet, then take care of the place with ointments until it heals.
Albarth however is red and resembles the heads of alhassa, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore it is necessary to cut what appears from it, as I said in thelil equally: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIIII.
Section on the Perforation that occurs in the womb (uterus).
Various appearances of abscesses occur in the matrix, such as cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati, alekilati (herpes), fistulae, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thelil, and warm abscess.
And indeed I have already said all these diseases and their species, and the signs of them, and their cures are divided: it is necessary that in this treatise I say about the warm abscess that occurs in the matrix, when it is from the abscesses that gather pus, and to know how its opening with iron.
Therefore, one should consider. Then if the pain of the abscess in its beginning is sharp with striking and flame, and fever, and you see it redden, if it falls upon the sense, then do not press with piercing, and cure it with that which helps for maturation until when the acuteness of the incidents ceases.
Then one should make the woman sit on a seat that has two arms, and recline or lie upon her back, and bring her feet to the lower part of her belly: and let her thighs be open, and put her arms under her knees, and bind each with a bandage fittingly to that.
Then let the midwife sit on the right side, and administer the instrument for opening the matrix's orifice.
And it is necessary when you wish to administer this instrument, that you strike with a long rod the matrix of the woman, so that what enters from the instrument is not greater than the depth of the matrix, and does not harm the weak.
If the instrument is too deep, then one should place feathers on the cover of the matrix depth: to prevent the entry of the entire instrument into the depth of the matrix: and one should hold the instrument and turn the worker's reel, until the depth of the matrix opens up.
When it appears to be excised and touched with the hand, and it is soft and tender, then it is necessary to cut it off at its head with a broad lancet.
When pus is discharged from it, then put linen soaked in rose oil or green oil containing some styptic substance into the wound; place the linen and extract the incision deep within the matrix.
Put it (the wound) externally on the matrix and on the comb a clean fleece soaked in water where molasses have been boiled.
Then it should be treated with an ointment suitable for that after two days until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix and the wound are washed so that it is cleansed with water and honey; then with water in which the root of the lily or long aristolochia has been boiled, and then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden internally within the matrix, then it is necessary to prevent any treatment with iron for that one; rather treat it with what I said in the section on incisions.
Chapter LXXX.
Section on obstetrics: how to treat living embryos that have exited in an unnatural way (according to their figure).
It is necessary for the obstetrician to first know the shape of a natural birth.
Therefore, among the signs of it (the unnatural birth) is that when you see a woman pressing towards the lower parts and yearning to smell the air, and a strong urge comes over her for the exit of the embryo; then know that this birth is in accordance with its natural shape, and it is an exit above its head and secondary (membrane) with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press the woman's abdomen so that the embryo descends quickly.
When it descends upon his head, the second one descends with it, and it is to be cleaned from those excesses with good cleansing.
But that which follows this birth is unnatural, not to be praised.
For at times the fetus comes forth upon its feet and its body comes out before its head; and the feet of it, and the hands of it come out one or only one foot: or the head of it and the hands of it: or the belly comes out: and perhaps it turns over on its neck, and similar unnatural shapes.
Therefore it is necessary that the midwife be prudent, skillful in these matters, and take care to avoid error and deception; and I show every figure of them, and what is the meaning of it, and it will be made clear through that, and it shall stand upon him.
When the fetus comes forth upon its head with its natural exit, and it becomes vigorous on the woman, and childbirth is difficult for her, and you see its strength already weakened; then make her sit on a chair, or women hold her: and warm her vagina with a decoction of fennel and with moist oils.
Then the midwife introduces a small spatula between her fingers, and scrapes it with it, and cuts the second one with her nail, until what is in it runs out from its wetness; and press the woman's womb, until the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with a decoction of fennel mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then command her after the cleansing to be pressed: and make her sneeze with pepper, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour. The fetus shall come out immediately.
If two hands emerge from the fetus first, it is necessary that you draw them back gently. If it does not obey during the delivery, then place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet upward; then strike the chair on the ground; and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the striking.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies; then cut them and remove the remaining fetus; and tie her hand with a cloth, and remove it with equal effort; for it will also come out.
The emergence of an embryo is above its feet. When the fetus comes out above its feet, then push them upward; then gradually turn it over; finally straighten it.
Then take one of his feet and stretch it gently.
When they come out as far as the hips, then command him to press and make her sneeze with powder; it will come out if God wills it.
And if it does not come out as we have said, then gradually pull the fetus back until you place it in its natural position. It will then come out easily with an easy delivery.
If you are forbidden to do everything as we have said; then take althea mucilage, sesame oil, and dissolved gum; grind it well in a pestle; then smear the woman's vulva with it and below her belly. Then make her sit in warm water until she feels relief in her womb.
When you see that the lower parts are already warmed up, then give her something to sniff from myrrh and place it beneath her nose. When an hour has passed, then make her sit on a chair. Then make it sneeze: and tighten its own bone and nose: and press the lower part of the abdomen with easy compression. The feces will exit immediately.
The birth takes place above the knees and hands. When it exits in this manner, then he should introduce his hands gradually. Then the woman lies on her back on her neck and let her feet hang downwards; and she should lie on the bed and fold her hands. Then press above her abdomen gradually. Then extract what is below her feet from the anus until it is ready at the lower part. If the fetus does not exit, then seize his feet and move them with strong movement. Then press what is above the pubis gradually until the fetus rises to the upper part. Then introduce his hands and equalize the fetus gradually; and command the woman to press herself until the fetus exits.
The birth takes place laterally hanging from the hands. He should introduce his hand for reduction (reducing a prolapsed organ). If it cannot be reduced, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then let her lie on the bed and strike her legs with strong impact.
Then apply the liniment you have prepared from mucilage (a gummy substance made from various plants).
If it receives her in childbirth, then let her sit on a chair. Then strive to reduce the hand, and equalize the fetus according to its natural form; and make the woman sneeze and command her to press herself until it exits.
The birth takes place on the back of the neck with spread hands and the face of the fetus is towards the back of the mother. The obstetrician must hold the fetus and then gradually turn it, and equalize it with ease.
When it is evened out, place it on the opening we have mentioned, with oil and mucilage.
Then command him to move it slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a chair, and command her to lean towards the right side. Then command him to press: and make her sneeze with powder.
The preparation of the fetus is on the side. When it descends to the opening of the matrix in this manner with the second one, then divide the second one with your nail until it is evacuated due to moisture.
If the fetus is suspended over the face and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the fetus towards the inside until you place it as necessary: and command the woman to press herself several times; for it will come out with an easy exit.
The birth of twins or many children. Know that twins are born frequently: and sometimes three, and even four. However, this is unusual and rarely occurs.
Five are indeed outside nature and do not live long: and they contain one second only, which separates them through a siphac, distinguishing between them bound at the navel of each of them.
And sometimes they come out just as a single fetus comes out with a natural and easy exit: and they come out with an unaccountable exit, as we have mentioned.
If some of them are difficult at birth and reach what I have said in unnatural positions, then care for them as we have mentioned: let the midwife be skillful, and do what she does with ease and slowness, and proceed according to every position with him who is prepared for it by his intelligence leading towards health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos, and they miscarry.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it is confirmed by me that a woman, while miscarrying, has emitted seven, and another fifteen, all formed.
What was done by measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore this whole matter should be in the knowledge of Obstetrics. Perhaps it will reach a similar case; therefore let him compare with it what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you take care of a dead fetus, along with what I said in the division and it does not come out, and you will be compelled to use an operation by hand, then you should consider the following.
If the woman is healthy and there are no accidents that cause fear of loss for her: then she should lie down on the bed on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs elevated; and a nurse should hold her from both sides or tie her to the bed so that her body does not be pulled out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with moist oils such as olive oil, mucilage from althea, fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Then the obstetrician wets his hand with these oils and mucilages; then he introduces it into the womb with ease. Then he seeks out a place to insert hooks from the fetus, and places that correspond to it.
Therefore consider whether the fetus is prepared to descend upon its head: then insert hooks into its eyes, neck, mouth, palate itself, beneath its beard, in its armpits, or near its ribs, and under its navel.
If it is a descent below his feet, then on the breastbone and his middle ribs.
And it is necessary that he holds the hook with his right hand: and places the sore in that which is between the fingers of the left hand: and introduces with his hand easily, and pierces the hook in one of those places which we said, until it reaches the hollow place.
Then pierce another or third hook, if necessary: so that the contraction is equal, and it does not lean to one side.
Then it is extended with an equal extension, and it should not be an extension only along the straight, but rather move to all parts, so that the opening is relieved: as it is done with a tooth in its extraction.
And it is necessary in what is between them, that the extension is softened. If a part remains in it, then it is necessary that the midwife binds certain fingers with oil, and introduces them from that side, to turn with them what remains.
If then a part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks are changed to another higher place: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If then a hand comes out before the others, and it is not possible to return it because of its contracture: then a cloth should be wrapped around it. Then extract it until when the whole comes out, cut it at the ankle or elbow: and thus you should do in the other hand, and in both feet.
If the fetal head is large or there is a contracture at exit, or water has accumulated in its head: then a sharp pointed spatula should be introduced between the fingers and pierce the head, and extract the water; or it should be broken with the instrument called Almisdac, whose shape comes with the shapes of the remaining instruments in the chapter that follows this.
Similarly, do as follows if the fetus is large-headed by nature, then it is necessary to cut off the membranes around the head; or else pull it out with forceps, as we have said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
If the head emerges and becomes stuck at the neck, then it is broken open to release the moisture that is in the chest.
If it does not twist or yield to exit, then the head is cut open piece by piece, as far as possible for you.
If there is an abscess or hydrops below the abdomen, then it is necessary to pierce it until the moisture runs out of it.
If the fetus is above its feet, then its extraction is easy and its direction towards the birth canal is light.
If it is stuck at the abdomen or chest, then it is necessary to pull it out with the cloth that you have wrapped over your hand; and break open the abdomen or chest until what is inside runs out of them.
If the other limbs are removed and the head returns, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If the birth canal is open, then the hand should be inserted deep into the birth canal and searched for the head, and pulled it with the fingers as far as the birth canal; then a hook can be inserted into it, or two hooks, and pulled out along with them.
If the birth canal is stuck due to a hot abscess that has occurred there, then it is not necessary to exert force on it; instead, administer bloodletting of moist substances and ointment, and apply plasters; and sit in warm water that softens and moistens.
If the fetus is on its side, then it may be possible to turn it; then what was said about a living fetus should be administered.
If it is not possible to do that, then make a shallow cut and extract it.
And you must absolutely not leave anything from the second layer inside at all.
When you have completed your procedure, then give what we said about warm cauterizations that occur in the wombs.
If bleeding occurs, let it go into cold water and give the rest of the treatment.
I myself have already seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus; then she became pregnant again on top of that, and another dead fetus was also born. So after a long time, she had an abscess at her navel that became swollen until it opened and began to emit pus.
I was therefore summoned for her treatment, and I treated her over a long period of time; but the wound did not heal.
So I placed some strong adhesive plasters on it, and the bone came out from that place. Then several days passed, and another bone came out. I was amazed then, since there was no bone in the womb.
So I thought, because the dead fetuses were from bones.
I therefore asked about the wound, and extracted many bones from it, while the woman was in good condition; and she lived thus for a long time, but emitted little pus from that place.
I did not fix this foreign object here unless there was knowledge about it and help for that, which the medical craftsman administers with his hand in treatment.
Chapter LXXVII.
Chapter on the shapes of necessary instruments for the extraction of a fetus.
The form of the Spindle which opens the Matrix.
Here below is the form of the Stricture Instrument, where books are evened, which have equally two spindles at the ends of two woods. Nevertheless, this Spindle should be more delicate than the Stricture Instrument: and to make it so, either from Ebony, or from Wood of Box.
And let the width of all the wood be as two fingers: and the edge of each of both is like one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and half, or more: and in the middle of two woods there are two additions of the same type of wood, which are already firmly fixed in each, whose length is half a palm, and less: and the width of each is as two fingers, or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the Matrix, so that it opens with them when you turn the two Spindles.
Another form similar to it, more delicate and lighter.
Make it from Ebony wood, or Boxwood, according to the likeness of forceps. Nevertheless, at the end of it there should be two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is as a palm: and the width of each is as two fingers.
When therefore you wish to open the Matrix with it, then make the woman sit on a bed, with her legs apart, opening what is between her thighs. Then insert these two additions together into the Matrix: and you are holding the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity you want from the opening of the Matrix, until the Midwife does what she wants.
Form of Dizziness Other Than That Which the Ancients Called Form of Pushing, by Which the Fetus is Pushed.
The form that crushes the large head: and it resembles a pair of forceps, which have teeth at the end, as you can see.
And sometimes it becomes oblique, as forceps according to this form, as you can see, which have teeth like the teeth of a saw, with which it cuts and crushes.
The form of a Scissor having one spine.
The form of a Scissor having two spines.
The form of a Spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form also of two wide Spatulas.
These instruments are all operated with the fingers, and as more of their forms multiply and are prepared by the craftsman, it is quicker for its operation, and higher among people, because of their quantity.
Therefore, do not disregard an instrument from among them, as if it were not prepared by you. Indeed, their necessity is inexcusable.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Chapter on the Second Extraction (C-Section).
When the Second Extraction (C-Section) is retained during labor, then it should be ordered that the weak ones (midwives) hold their breath. Then make her sneeze with a spoon and press your hand over her mouth and her own nostrils. If it (the baby) exits through this, that is good.
If not: then take a pot and make a hole in the mattress; put in there opening herbs for the womb, such as calamint, rutabaga, anise, chamomile, sesame, cassia wood, centaury, immerse all these herbs or some of them with water, and place them over the fire.
Then place the plunger of reed upon the opening of the pot's cover, and hold the other end against the bone of the matrix; and hold it until the vapor reaches the concavity of the matrix.
Then make her sneeze, as we have said. For secondarily, it will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then command the midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow root juice. Then insert into the vagina, and search for the Secondary one (baby). When she finds it, then take it, and slowly stretch it out.
If it is attached deeply in the matrix, then insert the hand as we have said, until when she finds the Secondary one, and pulls it out slowly along with right and left movement to avoid falling of the matrix due to strong attraction; indeed, it must be changed easily to the right and left side; then add more for the strength of the attraction. It (the baby) then yields itself, is preserved, and comes out from the attachment.
If the bone of the matrix is crooked, as we have already said: treat it with sneezing and with medicine from the pot with herbs.
If it does not come out as we have said, then be careful not to tire yourself by repeated attempts at extraction.
It is necessary that what comes out from the bone of the matrix, you tie it to the woman's hip (afterbirth). Then purge her with the ointment four-powder (purgative). It will rot it after days, and dissolve, and come out.
However, when it rots, raise the foul smell from her stomach and head, and injure that weak place. Therefore, it is necessary that suitable fumigations are administered for that purpose.
Some of the ancients have already tried fumigations with nasturtium and dried figs.
The shape of the instrument used to fumigate a woman during retention for afterbirth and menstruation.
