Make an instrument similar to an alembic or a jar, and place the wide end over the fire; let the fumigation be placed on plums; hold it until the fumigation is consumed; then another one should be held.
Chapter LXXIX.
[Chapter] On the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many male children are born whose anuses are not perforated, which the sharp flint has already cauterized. Therefore, the midwife should perforate it with her finger; and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp spatula; and be careful not to touch him [the child] with her arm.
Then place linen soaked in wine and oil on top of him [the child]. Then care for him with unguents until he is healed.
If one fears that it may perforate [the anus], then place a lead pipe in the hole for many days, and remove it when the child wishes to defecate.
And now it happens that perforation of the anus also occurs from the consolidation of a wound or boils. Therefore, it is necessary to cut off that consolidation, then care for it as we have said in the treatment and with lead.
Chapter LXXX.
[Chapter] On the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are those that are nodose and swollen that occur near the anus outside; or in a space of one part; and there is one fistula, or more than one.
When therefore that ancient Nodation is opened, there runs out from it moist watery whiteness or subtle pus.
At times there are penetrating ones among these fistulas. Therefore, the penetrating ones are recognized by what comes out from the discharge, and by wind, when the sick person uses the discharge; perhaps a worm may come out of them.
These fistulas are among them when they penetrate into the space and reach the bladder, and the muscle of the penis. There are also penetrating ones among these that penetrate until the junction of the hips and as far as the node of the tail.
From that which is recognized as the penetrating fistula until the anus, even from the non-penetrating one, it is to insert your little finger into the anus and insert a thin probe into the fistula made of metal or iron; provided there is no twisting.
If there is twisting in it, then insert a thin probe made of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe, or the hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it fully, nor does anything come out from the discharge, nor wind, nor worm as I said; then you will know that it is not penetrating - approach for treatment.
When the fistula is penetrating to the bladder or the urinary muscle, then its sign is the outflow of urine from it; and its prohibition is that the location should not be made firm with medicines.
If it is penetrating to the junction of the hips or the hip bone; then its sign is that the probe reaches there, if there is no twisting up to the bone; and the pain appears around the area and that pus always comes out from it; also, treatment cannot be administered in it nor should it be made firm with an ointment.
In these fistulas penetrating there is no cure at all: and the cure of them is labor and vanity to him, on whom it is formed by foolish physicians.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing is hoped for with a lance: as I tell you, and I have already proven it: and it is so that the sick one lies on his back under your hands upon his back: and the legs are raised up to above his hips: and the hips of his are inclined towards his stomach. Then insert lead or air, if there is a winding in the fistula, until you know where the probe has reached.
If, however, the sick one feels it around the anus, then it is necessary that you insert your thumb into the anus.
If therefore you feel the probe itself has already penetrated through the one found by itself, besides what you feel between your thumb and there or the flesh: then you know certainly that it is penetrating: do not labor in it because its healing does not exist, as we have said.
They say that the flesh heals in certain men, and the help expected from the medication is that small cautery iron be heated to the size of the fistula, as I have said earlier, and then it is inserted into the fistula while burning until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those added fleshes filtered, which are similar to a feathered pipe, have been burned.
Then treat it with linen wrapped in butter until the burnt flesh comes out: then treat it with ointments producing and consolidating the flesh.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it will never be healed with any other treatment.
If it [the probing] goes out [of the anus], but does not reach your finger, which is inside, and there is a thick membrane of flesh between it and the probe, or if you see that there is a fistula following the skin surface - then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula. And you proceed to cutting with the probe that is in the fistula until you reach where the tip of the probe ends, and the probe is released and falls out.
Then clean those fleshy parts resembling the quill of a bird's feather, so that nothing remains from them.
If blood defeats you and dissolves the bond between you and your operation so that the flesh should be separated - then it is better to burn it with fire or sharp medicine.
Because the cautery with fire produces good conditions, burning of those fleshy parts is added, as well as the coagulation of blood and drying of moisture.
Then treat it with linen strips wrapped in butter or heated earthenware vessels until the place produces pus, and those burned fleshy parts are expelled into the pus.
Then treat the wound with ointments that harden the flesh, producing tough skin; and there are medications containing astringents and drying agents.
For when it [the wound] is repaired, then it is healed; do not fear repetition.
If the fistula has already reached the deep part of the anus and is prolonged from the body - then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
Therefore, if you feel a probe, and between it and yourself is a membrane of flesh or skin, and it is approaching perforation - then there should be no operation on it, except according to the way of faith and hope.
That is because it is administered in him one of three methods: either to cauterize it itself, as we have said; or to excise it, until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert the linen, and cure it from nearby. And do not proceed much with the excision, lest you cut the flesh containing the anus, and an unwanted evacuation occur. Then treat that with what I have said.
Perhaps it will heal: or stretch the membrane and clean it after you cut it up to near the anus, as we have said, or with a probe, or with another sharp-tipped instrument. Then clean those flesh particles that are in the incision, as far as you can with examination.
Then try the healing of the whole wound with the incision, and with the upper opening where it heals; and a fistula remains open in the interior part of the anus, and it will be easier on the sick.
And sometimes a fistula is drained in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the fistula; and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and edge of the anus; then take a perforated probe tip, which is like an awl point, that is prepared ox hide, in this shape. And insert into it a thread wound around five strands and about that [size]. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula, until you reach its concavity.
If it is penetrating into the edge of the anus internally, then pull out the thread from that hole; so that you insert your finger into the anus, and pull out the tip of the thread, and bind both ends together; and tighten each one, and leave it for one or two days; and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, the better tighten it, until those tissues between the two ends of the thread fall off and drop out; then treat the wound, until it heals and recovers.
If, however, the opening of the Fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrable in any way prepared for you, unless it is in a very deep place. You have no need to do so (that action), lest you cut the arm itself.
Then proceed as we said, until it heals.
Make a beak-shaped spatula, sharp on the part that enters the Fistula, whose edge is very sharp; and the other part is not sharp, so as not to cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter LXXXI.
On stitching Piles (Hemorroids), from which blood flows when they are cut; and on the treatment of cracks.
There are Hemorroids in two ways. Or they are inside the anus, similar to coal blisters or prune stones; or as if they were like grains of wheat. And among them are small ones and large ones; and blood always flows from them, and there is one and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are mostly few in moisture, from which yellow water or a small amount of blood flows continually; and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus, is to command the patient to sit in hot water, and it is squeezed out until it appears at the anus, and you see it. Therefore also hang them with hooks; or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held in by hooks due to their moisture and softening; then grasp them with a rough cloth or a double-layered woolen fabric, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them (the vessels) and sprinkle some warm powders over them after the incision as a substitute for cautery. Cauterize them according to what has been described in the previous chapter on cauterization. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey the enema, then administer a gentle enema with an emetic substance to cleanse what is in the anus and make it quickly obey the evacuation when it discharges.
If they are external ulcers from the anus, then their condition is light and easy: and it is to seize them with your nail or with a pair of forceps and cut them. Then care for them as we have said, until they heal.
And if the incision is resisted by iron, then it is necessary to administer a suture for them in this way. Take thread wound around a needle and insert it into the point (of the ulcer). Then draw out the ulcers towards the top and make it penetrate with the needle into the root of the other side: and wind up the two ends of the thread, on the lower part of the needle, and let them be wide: and tighten the ulcer with a strong ligature. Then tie the thread and pull out the needle.
Do the same with all the ulcers, and leave one of them: do not seize it to avoid excess bleeding from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch on the anus and put it on the anus: and tell the patient to rest. Then dismiss him until he falls asleep.
When the ulcers fall off, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment, until they heal.
Treatment of Fissures. For they often occur from evacuation of feces and constriction of nature.
When they have grown old and medicine is of no avail: then it is necessary to shave with spatula or nail, until they become moist and the superficial layer which prevents their healing is removed. Then care for them until they are healed as required.
If they do not heal: then treat them again with a stronger reason than before, until they bleed much, and then care for them until they are healed.
On the treatment of Almirmar ulcers, and not ulcers: and Athelil sores, and Formicae.
Chapter LXXXII.
Know that Almirmar is not anything but a round nodule similar to the color of the body, like the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers: and pain occurs during walking from them.
Therefore it must be cut that which is on the edge of the nail, and held with forceps or tweezers, and uprooted from its root.
Then care for that, and if you wish to cauterize it as mentioned in the previous chapter.
Athelil is one of the dry sores: and there is a small projection that is rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And its treatment is to stretch Athelil, and cut it itself: or sew it with silk thread: or with wool, until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it as mentioned before with fire or sharp medicine: and now Athelil ulcers, and not ulcers are uprooted with the tool that I will say.
Formica is also a small, filtered projection, coarse on the surface of the body, penetrating very deep: and when it is found cold, it feels like biting by an ant, and occurs throughout the body: and most often it occurs in the hands.
And its treatment is to take a reed from the goose feather or strong vulture feather: and place the reed on Formica until it holds the circle of the reed from its parts. Then turn your hand with the cannula until you reach what is around the Ant (Formica). Place it into the depth of the flesh and root out the Ant from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a metal or iron cannula in this manner.
Place the cannula on top with a pull towards its highest point to loosen the deaf person's swelling around the finger and its subsequent rotation.
And if you wish, cauterize the Ant according to what has been said before in the chapter on cauterization of Athelil.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on the shapes of instruments used for administering enemas in diseases of the anus, and of the solution of the abdomen, and colics.
Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or gold plated, or brass melted, or hammered.
And sometimes these instruments are small, and large, according to those in which they are administered.
Therefore, the enema given for the treatment of small children should be small. And those for weak or painful anuses should also be small.
Large enema.
The cannula of this (enema), that is the upper part where the uterus is tied, should be wide according to this method: and it should have a division so that the uterus can be tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be blunt, not open, soft, very thin, extending to subtlety. And on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the size of the hole should be according to the thickness of a ray, and somewhat coarse but not too much. The uterus in which the medicines are placed should be that of an animal's bladder or a sheep's parchment, shaped like a small asafoetida bag, whose root should be one palm.
The incisions should be made in numerous holes as is customary, and the space between each hole should be of the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a thread made of raw silk, which should be about ten threads, or approximately that, and wrap it around with wool as one does with asafetida. When the uterus is placed inside, it should be tied at the top with a strong constriction using a clyster. Then administer a clyster to it.
And this is the shape of the circle and the holes as depicted here.
The quality of administering a clyster to it is as follows: fill the wool or bladder with medicine that has been heated to the quantity that the patient can tolerate; and be careful not for it to be excessively hot or excessively cold.
Then the patient lies down on his back, and raises his legs towards the top; and place under him a bed, that is to say, a skin or cloth upon which people lie.
Then anoint the end of the clyster with olive oil, or with lard, or with mucilage from fenugreek, or similar things. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then receive the assistant with both hands, and squeeze it out with force, until all that is in the clyster is expelled into the intestine.
Then remove the clyster and raise the patient's legs towards the wall.
If the medicine forces him to evacuate, then hold him as much as possible. And if he sleeps through the entire night with this, it is more beneficial for his recovery.
If you administer the clyster to him in cases of abdominal illness and he evacuates quickly: then repeat the clyster until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or wounds in the anus, then let the clyster be very subtle and gentle, from the clysters with which children are clystered.
Let this be the form of the subtle clyster upon which the skin is tightened.
Head, number LXXXIV.
I have already said in the division on the treatment of wounds that it was appropriate for a book, and here I will speak of their treatment by hand, and with medications as a supplement.
Therefore, wounds are differentiated according to the cause by which they occur, and according to the place upon which the wound falls.
Thus, the causes of wounds are as numerous as the throw of a stone: or a cut by a sword, or a knife: or a thrust with a spear, or wood, or arrow, and similar things from many other things.
Wounds that occur according to the body parts are as follows: a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or abdomen, or back, and similar things from those members.
And I am telling the treatment of certain wounds, so that I may present the reasoning and rule for the remaining wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, since the account of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore. When there is a simple wound on the head and no bone fracture has occurred: consider then if it was caused by the throw of a stone or something similar, and only the skin has been broken, and the wound is large and you fear that warm abscesses may occur: then hurry, and perform phlebotomy cephalic immediately: do not delay this, and draw out from him according to the amount of its virtue as much blood as possible, unless something prohibits phlebotomy, especially if little blood is exiting from the wound. Phlebotomy should be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
Phlebotomy should be from the opposite side of the wounded part. Let the sick person avoid self-indulgence, wine and heavy foods.
If something forbids reduction, then it should be reduced from food, not from flesh nor wine.
Place over the wound if it happens to be a hot abscess, boiled cotton soaked in warm rose oil alone, or with wine containing saltpeter.
If you are free from a hot abscess, then place over the wound if it is recent with its own blood and has not changed the air around it. And if the air around it has already changed, then place some ointments over it until it heals. (Followed by a statement about the powder to be used if the air changes.)
If the wound is large or from a sword cut and similar, do not bring the edges together by stitches through holes, but bring them together with sutures as I shall tell you about in wounds of the abdomen regarding their suturing.
If the wound is already from bone and hangs and there is no holding of it except with a small hook, then cut it. Then care for the wound with medicines and restore the hard flesh to its place in the skin, and advise the sick person to eat foods with heaviness, such as bread and cooked wheat, until it is soft; and similar things.
If you find corruption in the skin that is not attached to bone, then cut out the rotten part and throw it away; then care for it afterwards.
If in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it cannot be separated by medicine, then look for the artery. If you find it uncut, then cut it with a Spatula, or tie it. If necessity compels and it does not yield what has been said, then cauterize it until the blood is cut off.
If these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy and light; thus, scatter this powder over them, because it consolidates them before the air changes them.
Method of Powder for Healing. Take one part of olibanum, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburnt lime; grind it all thoroughly, then sift it; fill the wound with it, bind it tightly until it adheres well to it, and let it coagulate with the blood.
Then bind it on top with small bindings and leave it alone, do not loosen it until it does not separate. For the medicine will not be pulled out of him until he is healed.
Sometimes lime alone does it when olibanum and dragon's blood are not available to you at present; moreover, lime performs the same operation in many large wounds when it is to be placed upon them and they are bound, and the wounds are recent with their own blood, which has not been changed by air.
If the air has already changed them by some change, especially during summertime, then this powder is not suitable; therefore, treat it with what I have said, placing some digestive ointments on them or putting on them poultices made from barley flour, prepared with water and honey, until they emit pus. Then treat the rest of it with the remaining cure until they are healed.
But if it happens that there is a fracture of the bone with a wound and it is small, then extract it with Gui (Gesti); I will soon say the cure for fractures of the skull in what follows.
On wounds of the neck.
If a wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple wound of the head.
If the nerve or artery of the neck is already cut: then, if it is a nerve, there is no skill in treating it except to avoid treatment for the strong stiffness it causes, like the ziniar and zegi and similar ones. Because they are harmful and contract them.
And do not place anything cold at all on the wound: because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is above the organs; and let what is used to treat it be made from soft medicines, like limestone mixed with sweet water several times infused with oil, or rose oil, and turpentine, when it is washed even with sweet water; and the remaining mineral stones, in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then administer suture; or strip the edges of its lips with pulpilles. Then take care of it until it heals.
If the wound is deep or occurs in it a cavity on its lower part, where already pus collects, then pierce it at a more depressed place in it.
If the artery is already cut in the wound and there follows a flow of blood from it: then separate it, or cut it off and tie it; or cauterize it, if necessity requires that.
If the windpipe (spondiles) has already been split open, entirely, and the trachea has been saved: then join together the lips of the skin with suture over a reed for the throat, and do not touch the throat, but rather equalize it, and bring it back to its natural shape. Then tie the wound with a suitable suture and let it be for some days. Then treat it with ointments containing astringents and drying agents until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it. If there are pieces of bone inside, remove them all or as many as possible. And whatever cannot be prepared at that time, leave it until the wound rots, separates and heals over.
If the wound is recent, then dust it with the powder I mentioned. If a bone appears in the wound and a fistula is formed: then treat it as described in its respective chapter.
Chapter on wounds using probes.
If it is a wound caused by a spear or knife, and you can see its depth: then examine it. If a gas escapes from the wound when the person is weakly breathing, then you know that the wound is mortal.
If the depth of the wound is not visible and it is recent with blood: then do not apply powder to it immediately nor tie it up, so that the blood does not remain in its depth and returns to the heart and kills the weakened person; instead apply an attracting ointment and dissolve it twice a day.
If the ointment is not available to you, then place on the wound's opening an old piece of cotton to absorb what escapes from it due to moisture; and let the weakened person sleep over the wound so that it runs together and heals.
If three or more days have passed since the wound occurred, and there is no spasm, no bad heart tremor, no shortness of breath constriction, and you can see that its other signs are good: then know that the wound is healthy. Cure yourself and with liniments, and with the remaining treatment, until you are healed.
If it is excised (the affected part), and healing begins again, then you will know that it has become a Fistula. Cure it from its own chapter (part).
And if it is a wound from sword or knife cut, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then cure it with that which preceded (first aid), if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If it has already made an impression on the bone and cut off fragments from it: then search for the wound, and rush to extract those fragments, if they are separated. If they are not separated, then leave them until the wound putsrefies; for extraction of them is deodorized.
For other wounds due to accidents on the remaining members, the judgment in treatment is the same as what we have said.
Chapter on abdominal wounds and the expulsion of the intestines, and their return.
A rupture that occurs in the abdomen is great, middle, or small.
From a great rupture, intestines or their number sometimes come out.
Therefore, their insertion and stitching is made more difficult and forceful.
A small rupture is also difficult in another way. Therefore, its return is more difficult if you do not rush to the site for its insertion immediately; because it swells, opens up and enlarges; hence the entry is difficult.
Therefore, a medium rupture is more beneficial because with it the return of the intestine is not difficult, as it is in these two types (great and small).
You should know that stitching of veins is according to four modes.
Two types of stitches commonly join in stitching the vein, and in stitching other wounds of the body; and two other types of stitches specifically communicate with other wounds. However, they are more suitable for stitching the vein; and I tell you one by one with explanation and clarification.
Therefore, when the wound is small and something comes out of it from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to return it; then this is due to one of the two modes. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said; or because there is inflation in the intestine due to cold air.
When this is so, then it is necessary to heat it so that you immerse a sponge or damp cloth in warm water only. Or cook in water with squill, cyperus, pepper, and myrrh with the intestine until the inflation is resolved.
Sometimes it makes wine that contains strychnos; and this is better than water alone in resolving the inflation.
When you see that the inflation has already been resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which asphodel or mallow was boiled. For this reason, the entrance is anaesthetized with it when the wound is small.
If however the return of it occurs after this treatment, then sew up the rupture with a tool used to cut hemorrhoids.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared than when it is cut; and there should not be a forced action to cut when necessary and lack of tools.
Let one part of it be twisted, sharp, and another part not sharp, and the tip should not be fine with the fineness of a spatula, but rather somewhat blunt; and this is like a scabbard, as you see.
When a wound is extended and enters the bowel, then it should be reduced to its natural shape at its proper place, if possible on top of it: because it is better.
When the wound is wide at the lower part of the belly: then it should be made to lie on its back, and place the legs higher than the head. And if it is at the upper part of the belly, then raise its head and chest higher than its lower parts.
And similarly if the wound is on one of two parts of the belly, then direct your attention and consider always that the part with the wound should be higher than the other part.
In this way it is necessary to introduce this into large wounds and medium-sized wounds.
And in small wounds place it according to what you are prepared for.
Then make the devoted servant be present between your hands who holds the whole wound with his hand and press its lips together. Then take something from that which follows to bind, this is the common method of sewing one part.
And it is to take a needle or the number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then remove from the end of the wound a finger's breadth, that is, of the doctor; and sew the needle one time into the skin at both ends, with the ends of the sinew that is beneath the skin from inside, until you make it penetrate from the other side, and by this time you have joined the two edges of the skin and the two ends of the sinew; and four rows are made.
Then sew with double thread around the needle several times at both sides together until the lips of the wound are joined by appropriate stitching.
Then release the thickness of the digit and also tie another thread: afterwards straighten it with thread, as you did with the first thread. Do not cease to do that with the necessary needles until you complete the closure of the whole wound.
Let the needles be of a medium size between thickness and delicacy; because fine needles easily pierce the flesh, and thick ones have difficulty entering the skin; therefore, it is necessary for them to be medium in delicacy and thickness.
And it is not appropriate that the needle should be folded at both ends of the skin close by; so as not to pierce the flesh quickly and open the wound before its consolidation, nor lengthen even when sewing, so as not to prevent the consolidation of the wound.
Then cut the end of the needle so as not to injure the weak person in his sleep; and place small pieces of cloth from all sides around its ends, which hold the end of the needle; and release them when you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this kind of sewing with needles in such a way is more suitable for small wounds. Because only one needle or two, or about that number, are sufficient for sewing them.
The second sewing is common, to join together the ends of four with sewing; the four ends, two of skin and two of sifac in place of one, with a needle in which there is thread wound equally in delicacy and thickness.
Then, when you penetrate with the needle these four ends, draw back the needle from the side where you entered so that the thread falls down from the upper part of the wound; so that it is sewing as sewing of cloth when they fasten cloth, and place between every stitch a quantity equal to the thickness of a little finger.
Men know this suture.
And with this suture, I stitched the wound that had happened to a man in his abdomen, who was wounded with a knife, and the wound's breakage was greater than one palm; and about two palms of intestines had come out from the middle intestine, and there was a rupture in the middle stomach.
I therefore returned it after the intestine stayed outside the wound for 24 hours.
The wound was therefore healed in the space that was about 15 days; and I cured it, and it got well; and he lived after that for many years, converted to his own ways.
And the physicians had judged that it would not get well.
And by a miracle, I did not cure it with ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment was found, nor anything from the medicines. I therefore put old bread twice a day on the wound, and I attended to its cleansing with water of honey until it got well.
I will now speak about two types of sutures according to the report of the speech.
And it starts with a sharp suture: and you insert the needle from the outside to the inside part.
When the needle goes through the skin and advances according to the length and width of the entire body: release the end of the suture on the side where you inserted the needle, and make it penetrate to the end of another from the inside to the outside at the opposite extreme.
When you make it penetrate as described above on the same side, then make it penetrate from the outside to the inside at the same end: release the end of the suture, which is on this side, and make the needle penetrate to the end on the other side from the inside to the outside; and make it penetrate together with your penetration that you make it penetrate in the suture end, which is at this part, until it goes through entirely.
Then also start from the same side, and take it along with its extremity which is on the other side of sifac, and draw out the point that has penetrated the skin.
Then return it to the same skin, and take sifac's extremity on the other side with this extremity of mirach; draw it out from the skin that is on its part, and do the same for both sides; then do it again after the first time, until you withdraw all of it according to the example given.
The sum of this suture is that the skin of sutures should be smoother than the skins; so that you close sifac with one part of the skin's extremity, and release it with another part from the other side until you complete it.
The second type of suture proper, as Galen said.
This speech is told in a way similar to those who heal, so that they gather all parts together which naturally fit by themselves; and apply the extremity of sifac to its other extremity, and the extremity of mirach to another one of its extremities. And this is done as I am telling you.
You must place the point on the extremity of mirach close to you from the outside part, and make it penetrate to the inside only; then release both extremities of sifac. Then turn the point and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside in both sides of sifac.
Then turn both sides and make both penetrate from the inside to the outside, in the two extremities of mirach which are on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than the common and easy one, and it is the suture whose previous reminder has been given.
This is therefore a saying (or discourse) of Galen as well.
And they said something. The stitching of the abdomen should be made with two needles (or points). That is, so that you insert one thread into each of them (the abdomen): and begin with the introduction of the needle, from what is at hand with you, and make it pass through to the other side according to the stitching of those who sew hide equally.
And know that when the rupture (or tear) is in the middle of the abdomen: then the stitching of it is more difficult than the rest of the places in the abdomen.
The judgment (or decision) of the dressing of a wound is the judgment of other wounds as well.
That is, because when you will conquer a fresh wound with its own blood before it becomes altered by the air: and you reduce (or put back) the intestine, and close (or suture) the wound itself, then place it on a powder of ashes.
If the air has already altered the wound: then place some unguents on it that are present with you, so that they cause pus: and let threads fall and settle, and bandage (or wrap) it with linen cloth and mullein leaves. Then take care of that in the same way as the treatment of other wounds until it is healed.
If there are no remedies present with you: then immediately place on it a warm old cloth: and change it twice a day as I have taught you until it is healed.
For you do not need any other remedy in more complicated situations: when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound communicates with the main limbs due to injury: then it is necessary that you immerse a warm wool in oil tempered to a moderate heat, or in rose oil: and place it in the surrounding area of places that are between the groin, and under the armpits.
If he feels pain or punctures or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often occurs), then clisterize him with warm, black, stirrup wine: particularly if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine and an exit has been made penetrating to its concavity.
And know that what is from the large intestine is easier to heal, and what is from the small intestine is more difficult to heal.
The intestine that is called the Jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is because of its multitude, which is from veins, and their size, and because of the subtlety of its body, and because of the proximity of its nature to nerves.
If what proceeds from the wound is pus and you take it fresh: lead it back as you lead the intestines equally.
But if time has passed and it has become green or black: then you must tie it with thread above the place that has been darkened from it, so that blood flow does not occur. For in pus there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament and place two ends of thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so as to relieve you from its attraction towards you and the extraction of the pus at the site of the wound, and the emission of pus from the wound.
Reminder of a wound that occurs in the Intestine.
When there is a rupture in the Intestine and it is small: then it is possible for some people to be restored: because I have seen one who was wounded in his abdomen with a spear strike, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old: and a fistula was made, and excrement and gases came out of it.
I therefore administered treatment, until I was not confident in its healing; neither did I cease to investigate it, until it was healed and the place was consolidated.
When I saw the place already consolidated, I feared an accident happening to the sick man, that an accidental evil might occur in his stomach; and it did not happen to him from that accidental evil. And he remained in better conditions for himself, eating and drinking, urinating and defecating, and entering the bath, and exercising in his own regimen.
And some of the experimenters said that when a wound occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it should be tied according to this method. It is, to receive large-headed ants. Then join two lips of the wound, and place one ant with an open mouth on top of the two lips of the wound. When its head is on top of them, and it closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it will stick, and it will not be loosened.
Then place another ant next to the first, and do not cease doing that with an ant according to the quantity of the wound in its entirety.
Then reduce it, and close the wound. For those heads remain attached to the intestine until it is eaten, and healed, and no harm occurs to the sick man in his entirety.
And it is now possible to tie the intestine even with a thin thread; which I removed from the animal's intestine, attached to it when introduced into the point.
It is, to take the end of this thread from the intestine and remove much of the flesh. Then tie a thin linen thread at the end of it. Then insert that thread into the point, and suck out the intestine with it. Then lead it back to the incision.
And this method of suture with worms and intestine is not except by way of trust and hope.
Know that a large wound, wide, especially if it is on one of the slender intestines: then there is no artistry except refinement, nor is its healing altogether.
Â§ On the care of the rectum, and fistulas.
Know that every wound or boil when it becomes old and hardens and turns into an ulcer and does not consolidate and always emits pus and is not cut off: then it is called universally in whatever member it may be a fistula, and we call it the rectum.
And a fistula indeed is according to the truth a filtered knot, hard and white: with which there is no pain, which has a hollow of a bird's feather: and for this reason some call it Rata, that is, feather.
And it is sometimes moist, which emits pus. And perhaps moisture is cut off in some hours. And sometimes this moisture is much and is little; and it is thick and is refined.
And I have already said in the division, when I spoke of wounds, that every ulcer which does not heal and is not born in it flesh, is not this because of one of nine causes.
One of them is because of the scarcity of blood in the body; or because it is bad; or because there is hard flesh between it and its edges, preventing the growth of flesh; or because there are many filths and dirtiness; or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter that is sent to it is of poor quality; or because the medicine is inappropriate for its healing; or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where digestion of illnesses becomes difficult, and healing of boils is delayed by nature; or because there is one bone or number of bones in it.
I have now shown you all those causes and their signs, and the treatments of them with medicines in division. Here it is necessary for me to make you know the treatment for a Fistula and a Hernia, which is made through the way of operation by hand.
Therefore, you should know that a Fistula occurs in all the members of the body. For of these are Fistulae which reach the large veins and arteries, or nerves, or bladders; or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs: or to any of the spine bones, or to any of the joints composed; such as the hands and feet: and of these are those which approach the proximity of the main member, and similar ones.
Which of these Fistulas is so according to this manner, is difficult for cure, and does not receive treatment, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
If it is of any Fistulas whose depth does not reach to the places which I said: and you hope, and trust in its cure, and wish to reach the knowledge of it, then take a probe made of brass or iron, if the Fistula tends according to straightness, and explore it with that.
If, however, there is a twisting in the Fistula, then investigate it with a probe made of thin lead. Because lead, with its own softness, is softened and bent around the twisting.
If the Fistula has many openings, it will not be possible for you to indicate over it with a probe. Clysterize therefore from those openings of its own openings.
For moisture which you clysterize with itself goes backwards through the other openings and runs out from them.
Then carefully inquire in whatever way is possible for you: so that you may know whether there is a bone or nerve there, and it is a long deep-set fistula or a nearby one: or it is a fistula with multiple openings, which covers the entire area, when you apply your maximum strength: with your questioning of the patient, when you inquire about pain under compression with your hand on the location, and similar signs and causes of inflammation.
When you have stood over all these things, then proceed to treatment according to your confidence: and it is for you to consider at that time whether the fistula is nearby or appearing in a safe remote location, or near a nerve, artery, vein, or single location as I have mentioned to you: then cut the fistula according to what was previously stated in my account, and remove from it what is present due to filtration, and decayed flesh, which grows in its opening from flesh or membrane, or similar things: and treat it until it heals.
If the fistula is deep-set and straight, then it should be cut as deeply as possible for you. Then cleanse it from all corrupted flesh of its surroundings.
Then apply linen folded in medications that are sharp, and insert it into the depth of the fistula opening that you have grasped with an iron: do this several times until the sharp medication corrodes everything remaining in the depth of the fistula due to decay.
Then restore it with unguents that generate healthy flesh, until it heals.
If it does not heal by this, then cauterize it as I have previously described.
If the cause of the fistula is a bone and this is certain to you: then inquire about it and cut the bone as I have told you: if there is nothing preventing you from doing so, according to what we have said, regarding a vein, nerve or major limb.
If therefore a bone is exposed to you and there is something corrupted within it, and blackening: then scrape it, until the entire corruption is removed from it. Then take care of it with that which cures it, until it heals.
If it does not heal and discharges pus as it was doing: then you will know that you did not achieve complete removal of the corruption.
Excavate therefore above it again, and seek out its reason, and clean it with the utmost strength of your skill.
Then restore it. If it heals, that is good; and if not, then you will know that the corruption is in a distant depth of the body, which you were not able to reach. Therefore, it is not your skill in this matter, but rather to let nature take its course.
If the small bone is corrupted, and it is possible for you to do so, draw it out with fine forceps suitable for that purpose.
If there are many bones, then seek to draw out all of them carefully, without leaving anything behind with your strength.
If on the other hand something opposes you from the humidities and there is no fear or mistake in the cuts: then cut those humidities and flesh, if it is there, and free the bones.
If you do not have the preparation for removing bones from your time, then place over the wound something that will corrupt it; and let it go until it corrupts what is around those bones of flesh and humidities.
And keep the wound so that it does not solidify. And the incision which you made during your procedure should be tied up. Or if you fear, place on it a cloth soaked in powdered sulfur with oil; or a cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment, or in some green ointment.
When those [humidities] namely rot and bones separate from them, let there be an excision of them, and their attraction.
If there is one large bone, like the thigh bone or hip bone and similar to them, and what has been corrupted from it is a large part: then shave it with the final rasp until that blackness and corruption is removed. Then restore the wound.
If what is in it has become a large part and corruption of the bone marrow has already occurred, then it is necessary to saw it, and cut it completely to the place where the corruption has reached: then treat it until it heals.
And I tell you this sign which happens to a man in his leg: place it as an example and aid for your surgery.
There was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg, which moved upon him from within the body, that is, from inside, until the matter reached his leg and an abscess was opened with a large incision: and there was no external cause for it.
Then the time passed with the error of the physicians until the abscess was opened, and many matters gathered around it. And the treatment of him was delayed until the leg became fistulous and many openings were made in it: which all emitted pus and humidities of the body.
A multitude of physicians treated him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hand until I was called upon, and saw his leg, and the matters that were flowing out from those openings with a great flow: even the entire body of the man had become gangrenous, and his complexion was jaundiced.
I inserted my finger into one of the openings and my finger reached a bone.
Then I have examined all the openings and found them to lead into each other from every part of the leg.
I have probed and cut open one of the openings, until I exposed a part of the bone: and I found it corrupted; which had already rotten, decayed, putrefied, and perforated until it penetrated to the marrow.
Then I have sawed what was exposed to me, and prepared it from the corrupted bone.
And I removed whatever was not bone except that corruption which I cut off and sawed. And now I have extracted it.
Then I placed the healing of the wound with strengthening medicines in a long space. And it is not healed.
Then I tried again and exposed on the second bone above the first exposure: and found continuous corruption with the bone; and sawed what appeared to me also from that corruption.
And I made an attempt at healing it. And it is not restored.
Then I exposed it again and did not stop cutting the bone piece by piece and trying to heal it; and it is not restored until I cut from the bone about one palm and extracted that with its marrow.
Then I healed it with medicines and it quickly became consolidated and cured; and this iteration in the operation and section of it was not necessary except for the disposition of the weakness of the patient, and the scarcity of his tolerance, and my fear over him concerning death; because there occurred to him at all hours from excessive evacuation of syncopes bad.
He was therefore completely cured; and new flesh hard grew at the place of the bone, and good arrangement was made in his body, and his strength returned; and he turned to his dispositions; and no harm at all occurred to him from walking contrary to it.
If, however, the protruding bone in the body's location is already fractured: then it is necessary that you grasp it thus: and it is as follows: to take a ligament, and tie it at the end of the protruding bone: and command someone to stretch it upwards: and place another thicker ligament over the first one. Then tie it on the flesh that is next to the bone: and stretch out its end so as to pull the flesh towards lower parts: and expose the flesh over the place where you wish to cut, so that the knife does not hurt the flesh.
Place a stick or a board under the bone below properly: because when you do that, it is not forbidden to cut corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary that the knife be above the corrupted place a little, so that there is no corruption in the concavity of the bone: and it does not appear to the sense in its vision, and compels another to perform the cutting instead.
If the bone is corrupted and not protruding, rather it is continuous with another part, and corruption is in the middle of it or in a part of it: then expose the flesh from all parts completely. Then place a stick below.
Afterwards cut it from the first part where there is corruption, until the cutting is continuous on the other side: and the knife should be according to the length slightly away from the corruption, as we said.
If corruption is at a joint, cut the corrupted joint itself, and cut the bone where it is continuous on the other side.
But if corruption is at the continuity of two joints, then there is no skill but abrasion.
If corruption is in the beak of the hand or in the beak of the foot: then there is a very difficult matter in that. But it is necessary for you to examine how the corruption appears to you. And file (or remove) it (the lesion), and clean it as well as possible for you, and with whatever skill it is corrected for you: when it does not cause you opposition to the Vein, or Nerve.
And know that many incising (saws) and Serrae for cutting these bones are, according to the position of the bones, their preparation, their thickness, and subtlety, their size and smallness, their hardness, and rarity. Therefore, it is necessary that you prepare every kind of instrument suitable for each operation.
And know that these operations indicate to you the type of instrument that you need, when your study is prolonged. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a sign of the nature of diseases; then indeed you will find for yourself what suits it from the instruments for every ailment.
And I am confirming to you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments, which you will put examples on for what you cut, and a test for what you try on others.
The form of another saw.
The shape of a rasp for joints. The head of this rasp should be in the shape of a star key head; and its points should be in the shape of the points of an escarbuncle chisel.
It is not suitable unless it scrapes the heads of joints when they are broken, or a large and thick bone.
Form for a larger razor.
Form for a wide razor.
Form for a razor with a hollowed out center.
Form for another fine razor.
Form for a razor with a curved end.
Form for a small, fine, and flexible razor.
This resembles a saw and its end is like a chisel; it is used in many places for bone cutting reasons.
Form for the razor that fits for the purpose of perforating bones.
Its end is triangular and sharp-edged.
It is made from India. And similarly, everything that I have mentioned should be made of razors, knives and saws.
Section on the incision of extremities and the sawing of bones.
Decay occurs at the extremities, either from an external cause or an internal one.
When you are treated for that corruption with medicinal remedies and it does not improve, and you see the corruption advancing into a limb which is not affected by anything else: then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to where the corruption extends so that the weak one may pass through it from death or from the malice which is greater than the defect of the limb.
And the sign that occurs is that the limb darkens until it seems as if it has been burnt, or else it becomes corrupt after turning black: until the corruption extends to that which follows the limb and creeps over the entire body.
Approach then with the incision, and similarly if the cause of the corruption is from the sting of certain venomous creatures: such as the marine scorpion, viper, weasel, or similar ones.
If the corruption, or the wound, is at the extremity of a finger, then amputate the finger, and do not leave room for the corruption to spread, so that it may not advance to the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it occurs in the hand, then amputate from the root of the wrist, and do not leave room for the corruption to spread, until it takes hold in the arm.
And if it advances to the elbow joint, then amputate the arm at the elbow joint.
If, however, the corruption passes beyond the elbow and you see it as such: then death is imminent for the weak one. And whatever is administered after that for treatment, is the measure of its power.
And similarly do the same with the foot, when corruption advances to a toe: then amputate it at one joint; and if it takes hold in the front part of the foot, then amputate the entire foot. If it rises to the knee, then cut the leg at the joint of the knee.
If corruption has already reached the knee, then there is no skill in that case except for release and leaving the weak to death.
The method of cutting a limb or sewing it is to tighten the ligament below where you wish to cut and tighten another ligament above the place. And extend one minister (assistant) to the lower parts, and extend another minister to the upper parts. And you separate the flesh that is between the two ligaments, with a wide spatula, until the entire flesh is exposed. Then it is cut or sewn.
It is necessary that you place a linen cloth on all parts and the saw not touch a healthy place; and it should happen that an additional injury occurs to the weak and a hot abscess.
If bleeding occurs internally while you are operating, then cauterize the place quickly or place some absorbing powders on top of it to stop the bleeding. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable ligament and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you what happens to a man on his foot; the same thing happens that I told you.
What happened was that there is a blackening on his foot, with a burning similar to fire burning; and the corruption begins first in his toe until it spreads throughout the entire foot.
Therefore the man, seeing the corruption spread in his limb with great pain, which he found from the pain and burning; and he cut it at the joint and was cured.
And after a long time had passed, the same corruption occurred in the index finger of his own hand.
Therefore he came to me, and I attempted to regain the excess with what I had placed on his hand from medicines after the cleansing of his body; but the excess was not found, and it began to progress to another finger: until corruption started in the hand.
He called me to cut his hand; but I did not want it, hoping for a recovery of the excess from my side; and I also feared death itself in cutting his hand. Because the man's strength was above his fall.
After he had given up hope in me, he returned to his own land; and he came back to me concerning him, because he rushed, and cut off all his hand; and he was healed.
I did not bring this story except as help for that which falls under the genus of this illness; and as a signification of what is to be understood, and according to how it should be done.
Chapter on the care of sinuses, and the quality of cleansing with medicines.
When a boil occurs in some fleshly members and the space of the boil extends until it collects pus; then it bursts or perforates and what is inside the boil comes out along with the pus, leaving a void place as if it were a vessel; and the skin that is over it like a cloth that has been worn away; and it does not reach ultimate corruption, nor presses into bone, nor into nerve, nor into ligament: it deserves to be called Sinus; and it is not called Fistula: however, if the space of it extends until corruption presses into one of these members, then it is called Fistula or zukan.
And its care is that you cut the entire skin as it is rolled; and especially when it has been worn away and become like cloth; and trust that it will not adhere to the place due to its corruption.
If however you suspect that it adheres to the skin, and this does not follow from its subsequent corruption: and if there is thickening in the skin from flesh, then treat it with Clisterium; and it is to be considered towards the Sinus.
If it is large and the pus that comes out of it has a foul smell: then clisterize it with Egyptian medicine, which is vinegar, oil, and zinnia (mastic) mixed in equal parts, put them together in a vessel; boil over fire until the medicine turns red; and let it reach the consistency of honey.
Then take from it what you need; dissolve it with water and honey, and clisterize the Sinus with it; tie up its opening and let the medicine remain within for two hours.
Then remove it by pressing; do this daily until the sinus is cleansed and the foul smell removed.
And at times it is to be clisterized with water and ashes, when this medicine is not available; and it is to receive ashes of grape wood or ashes from holly trees; throw water over it. Then boil it and clisterize with it until you believe that the sinus has been cleansed.
If the patient is not able to tolerate Egyptian medicine or water and ashes, then clisterize it with water and honey mixed with some crushed zinnia (mastic). Or clisterize it with honey and wine mixed together because the property of honey is to cleanse and purify; and wine makes the sinus sticky especially when there is excess thickening and dryness in the wine.
When you do this often and believe that the sinus corruption has been removed: then clisterize it with that which causes flesh to grow therein.
And it is to receive from the plaster dyafinicon: and dissolve it with rose oil, and stiptic wine; or purge it with certain medicines, and with other ointments, whose properties I wrote in the treatise on ointments.
If the orifice of the Sinus is narrow and cannot receive a cannula for purgation: then expand it slightly with iron; or place upon it linen wrapped in Egyptian ointment, or in basilicon ointment, until it expands.
And similarly if the orifice is also wide, then gather its lips with stitching; and let out from it as much as the purgation can enter without addition.
And similarly if the orifice from which pus runs is elevated above: then cut it in a lower place that is within it, so that pus can run downwards; since pus when constricted in the depth of the Sinus prevents flesh to grow there.
If it is not possible for you to cut the Sinus below as you wish: then try, so that you prepare a member in such a way that pus can run out from it with ease according to how it is prepared for you. Try, so that nothing from the pus is retained there; and take consolidating medicines which are placed on the mark, suitable for what you wish. Spread them out on a linen cloth. Let the cloth be of such size that there is communication of the entire Sinus. Then cut with scissors a hole in the direct orifice of the Sinus, slightly larger than the orifice of the Sinus. Then spread some gentle ointments over another cloth according to the size of the hole; and place it on top with a long position from the orifice of the Sinus, to ease the exit of pus from there; and do not remove the large cloth unless after several days in one go.
He who is above the opening of the Sinus, is the one to be removed at all times, so that what accumulates in it from pus may exit: and you should know whether what flows out of it is much or little; or digested or undigested.
And again consider the location of the Sinus itself, whether its master feels pain there or not; and whether there is a boil there or not.
When your treatment is performed in this manner and you see the matter that exits from the opening of the Sinus, then know that the Sinus already adheres or approaches adhesion; then therefore dissolve it either on the morning or on the third day: and when you dissolve the wound, then change the linen cloth and renew the ointment.
If, however, a subtle venom flows out of the Sinus after a long interval, then do not despair of its adhesion, for healing is approaching; because there are some men who produce slow flesh generation in their wounds, and there are others who act contrary to this.
If, however, undigested pus flows out of the Sinus after many days, then know that the Sinus is not adhering.
If therefore the adhesion of the Sinus is delayed and its matter prolonged; then add in drying medicines, but let the doctors do so that the medicines are humid in substance and dry in potency; such as unguentum dyafinicon when added to it an excess from zegi.
And from the more remote which is cured, it is that you receive unguentum dyafinicon, and dissolve it with rose oil, and rub over it old wine equal in substance.
Then make a paste from it and use it.
And now he performs an action similar to this one, when you do not have the ointment dyafinicon available, honey, when you cook it until it thickens, and use it. Take myrrh, aloes, and frankincense: grind everything into powder and sprinkle it over honey while it is over the fire. Then, lay linen over it and bind it on a bladder: and lay the linen with the cooked honey, until it thickens: and sprinkle its powdery substance over it and bind it again.
And sometimes, in that case, aristolochia longa, celestial lily roots, and the lily itself are administered: along with wheat flour and chamomile. Use them simply or combined, grind them, and sift the powder: sprinkle it over the honey I mentioned and use it.
If the case of the bladder continues and is not cured with this treatment: then you know that there is corruption in its depth: or it already causes impression on bones, or in hard members, or ligaments: then treat it with fistula cure, as previously mentioned.
Chapter on the treatment of pawrot and worn nails, and the incision and amputation of a finger or toe.
Pawrot is an abscess that develops under the nail of the thumb or big toe, perhaps it arises in other fingers.
When the case of pawrot persists and is neglected and treated with warm abscess incision, it ruptures and releases pus until it corrodes the root of the nail: perhaps it corrodes it completely and corruption reaches the bone, so that there is a foul smell: and the tip of the finger becomes wide and its color turns black.
When you heal the self, with what we said in the division, and your treatment does not improve it: then it is necessary that you cut with iron all the excess which remains from the nail. Then, cauterize the wound after that. For indeed cautery is very beneficial.
If the bone is healthy and also the nail is healthy, and empty additions of the nail already press the flesh towards the inside and begin to pierce it, and hurt it: then it is necessary that you place refined Radium under the angle of the nail which pierces the flesh, and push it upwards: and cut the flesh with ease, and place on top of what remains of the flesh from healing medicines, corrosives, until it is removed entirely. Then heal it with ointments, until it heals.
If already corruption is pressing on the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the bone and extract it: for indeed the bone does not heal while a corrupted bone remains in it.
If you see the corrosion and corruption advancing in a finger, then cut it in one knuckle, according to what was mentioned in its description. Then heal it, until it heals.
If however the nail is worn away or struck, and a strong pain occurs, then it is necessary to use leeches first. Then cut the nail with a sharp Spathamelon crosswise from above towards the end.
And keep, that the cut does not reach the flesh which is under the nail, for indeed you will cause a strong pain above the weak, and it will be the cause of the growth of additional flesh at that location.
Then heal the place with what soothes the pains.
A finger that is born in some human hands may be entirely fleshy; and in some of these there are bones, and in one of them there is a nail: and some of those which are born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in the knots of the finger. The one who is born in certain knots of the finger, does not move: and the one who is born at the junction of the finger, perhaps moves.
Therefore, for the one who is fleshy [from this condition], the cutting [of the affected part] is easy. This means, to cut it at its root with a broad Spatulili [tool].
But the treatment of the one whose origin is at the junction of the root, is difficult. Therefore, refrain from cutting it [the affected part].
However, in the one who is born in the finger at the end of knots, then it is necessary to cut its flesh with a circular incision up to the bone [first]. Then saw the bone with one of those [appropriate] saws that fit for it. Then treat him until he is healed.
Consolidation, which often occurs in the fingers on the other hand, frequently happens either from human birth, that is, being born with it, or from the consolidation of a wound, or from fire burns, and similar things.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural shape. Then place a linen cloth or absorbent cloth soaked in rose oil between them to prevent them from consolidating quickly and separating them; or place a thin sheet of lead between them until the location is healed as required.
And similarly, if there is consolidation in some fingers with the palm, then cut that consolidation according to what is prepared and fitting for the shape of the member.
[Section] On the Vice of Incision.
The veins are enlarged, thick, and filled with melancholic excesses which occur in many parts of the body; and their most common outcome is in the legs, especially in those who travel and exert themselves, and those who carry loads.
Therefore, it is necessary that you administer a purge of the body from black bile at times with strong purging.
Then perform venesection on the patient's basilic vein.
The treatment of these (issues) with iron is according to two modes. One of them is to cut (the vein), and draw out black blood. And another method is, that it should be lifted up (the vein) and completely drawn out.
The section (operation) of this (vein) is according to this method. Pour a lot of warm water on the leg first, until the thick, foul blood is resolved. Then tie the weak (affected) leg from its upper part of the thigh to its lower part of the knee with a bandage. Then cut the vein at one, or two, or three wide sections.
Then lift and draw out (the blood) from the lower part of the leg by hand towards the upper part, and it is necessary that the leech should be applied first to the affected person. Then cut the fingernail towards the lower part: until a quantity of blood comes out that you see is sufficient, and as much as the strength of the affected person can bear.
Then tie it (the vein): and command him to abstain from foods that generate black bile; and repeat the evacuation and leeching when the veins are full, and that is harmful for the affected person.
The elevation (lifting of the blood) is according to this method. Scrape the weak (affected) leg if there are many hairs in it. Then immerse him in the bath; or pour warm water over his leg, until it turns red and the veins swell up; or exercise him with a strong movement (exercise), if there is no bath present for him, until the limb becomes warm.
Then make a longitudinal incision on the skin along the vein section; or at the end of it (the vein) near the knee, or at the lower part of it near the heel.
Then open the skin with a scalpel and scrape off all the vein until it is visible to the senses; and at its appearance, when you see it turn from red to black, there is a decline in sensation (the vein has been completely emptied). When it comes out from the flesh, you see it white like a cord.
Then insert a rod under it until when it is raised and comes out of the flesh: hang it with a blind hook, gently.
Then make another incision nearby that incision with three fingers. Then remove the skin from above the vein until it appears. Then raise it with rods as you did before and hang it again with another hook, as you did first.
Then make another incision or multiple incisions if needed. Then remove it and cut the last incision at the heel.
Then draw out that part above it.
And do this until you draw it out from the above incision or any higher incisions, until it comes out completely: then cut it.
If it does not obey you in drawing and raising: then insert a sharp point with a strong thread and tie it and draw it out itself or insert a rod under it: and turn your hand to every part until it comes out. And be careful not to cut it. For if it is cut, it becomes very difficult for you to raise it and it enters into the patient a great harm from it.
When you draw it out completely: then place a wool soaked in wine and rose oil or olive oil on the wound site and take care of it until it heals.
If it is a vein that has a curvature with turns and is not as we have said straight: then you should make an incision over all its parts of the curvature and the places of the turning.
Then hang it with hooks until you raise it completely: and be careful at your incision site not to cut the vein or wound: for it will become difficult for you to raise or draw it out. Preserve therefore your prudence.
The way to heal a wound is shaped like a vine (or grapevine).
The shape of the bandage for a blind man (or blind eye).
It is not a wound as the others are, nor does it have an acute end to injure the vein; and it has a thick and flexible nature because if it were subtle, it would pierce the vein with its subtlety; but rather excessive thickness is superfluous for it, as we said.
On the extraction of the leg vein.
This vein is produced in warm lands such as Al-Izegi and the Arabian Peninsula, and in dry, warm areas of little softness (or frailty), that is, where no grass or tree grows.
And perhaps it is produced in other parts of the body apart from the legs.
Its generation indeed is from the putrefaction that occurs under the skin, such as what happens inside snakes' or tapeworms' bodies and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the onset of this vein is that which occurs with a violent inflammation in the leg. Then it (the area) is incised. Then the vein begins to emerge from that incision, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When its end appears from there, then it is necessary to roll a leaden tube (or lead weight) of kilogram-keel weight over it up to two drachms and the knot; and let go of the hanging lead from the leg.
Whenever something comes out of it towards the outside, roll that over in lead and knot it. If it extends for a long time, then cut off part of it, and roll up the rest. Do not cut it root-wise before it has completely come out. Because if you cut (it), it contracts and enters into the flesh; and causes an abscess to occur, and pus in the place, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore, it should be treated gently and slowly drawn out until it has completely come out and nothing remains in the body; and from this vein comes out in some people what is in its length five palms and ten (fingers). And now it has reached me, because a man has come out from twenty palms.
If however it is cut during your treatment; then insert a probe into its opening and perforate it with a long probe, along with the body, until all that is in it from the matter has been evacuated; and administer pus-treatment to the place with medicines for some days. Then treat it with the treatment of abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, particularly when it appears at the junction of the foot, or on the foot itself; and many openings occur to it, and a branch comes out from every opening.
Therefore, treat it as we have said in the previous section, and with what has been mentioned before.
Â§ On the cutting of worms generated under the skin, and it is called Bouin disease.
This disease is called Bouin disease in a certain land among us; because it often occurs to cows and there is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it moves throughout the body, going up and down; and it is perceived by the senses during its movement from limb to limb until it bursts open at any place where it bursts, and comes out.
And its generation is from the corruption of certain humors. As worms and snakes, that is, earthworms and roundworms occur in the belly.
And it is feared from its malice. When it enters the body and rises to the head, and reaches the place, then perhaps it opens there and exits, and destroys the eye; this happens often.
When one wants to cure it and extract it, this is done only during his walking and the appearance of the same to the sense.
Therefore, one must bind what is above it and what is below it with a strong bandage. Then cut above it, and extract it.
If it goes deep into the flesh, and you cannot find it; then place a cauterization over the spot with fire until it dies.
And the greater fear is its corruption which corrupts the eye, as we have said.
If you see it has already reached the head near the eye, then bind above it with a good brow-band. Then cut above it, and extract it.
And the sick person must use self-cleansing of his body, with medicines that dissolve bad and foul humors.
And let him be careful to avoid foods causing decay.
Section on the disease called Nakir.
This disease is called Nakir in our land; it is pain that occurs in some members, then changes from member to member.
And I myself have already seen this, as I have told you. I was called to a sick woman in some villages. She pulled out her arm, and I saw a swelling smaller than the vein of the arm.
And after staying for an hour, I saw a swelling moving with a worm-like motion, faster than possible, as if silver running from place to place.
The pain therefore withdrew from that place, and it was fixed in the shoulder.
Then, after an hour, it ran through the rest of the body until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that it was being turned throughout its entire body, as I saw it.
I was therefore amazed by the swiftness of its transformation from limb to limb. And indeed, before that, I had not seen this illness appear in my eyes in such a way. Nevertheless, I have seen many who find pain transform from limb to limb; and I did not see it with my own eyes as I saw it in the woman.
And I do not think that it was anything other than because the woman was one of those who are afflicted with dry bodies and congested veins; therefore, it appears that this windiness was transformed.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist bodies, the hidden veins being concealed.
When therefore you wish to cure it, and the patient feels that pain; then if it appears to you with your eyes as we have said, then squeeze above it and below it quickly; cut above it until that windiness is released, compressed; and cauterize the place.
But if you do not see it with your eyes: then cure it with the body's shaking and with that which expels windiness, and crumble them with foul pills, and pills of myrrh, and similar things.
Chapter on the Extraction of Arrows.
Arrows are classified according to their shapes and the places where they fall from the body.
The diversity of arrows is that there are some which have large points and small ones; concave or straight. And among them are those which have three angles. And from these are tongues. And among them are stars.
Those that are in regard to limbs where they fall, are according to two modes. Or the limbs are from principal convex members such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar. When it falls in any one of these members and shows you signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, then it is necessary that you devote the extraction of this arrow, for death follows it wherever it is, in various positions. And when these signs are not evident to you, and the arrow is not concealed in the depth of the member, then extract it yourself, and care for the wound.
For the signs of brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone, and comes out from what is above the brain, are: because hot flashes occur from it, and scotoma, and vertigo, and redness in the eyes, and swelling, and redness of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of intellect, and vomiting of cholera. And perhaps blood comes out from the nose, or ears. And perhaps speech is cut off, and the voice is destroyed. And from the place of the wound comes out moisture white like plaster. And it comes out similar to meat that has been soaked in water.
If these signs appear to you, then abstain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it does not come out.
The signs of the arrow when it falls on the heart are: that it is near the left mammary: and it feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not in an empty one. And perhaps the arrow has motion similar to the pulse: and blood runs from the wound black. And follows that chill of the extremities, and cold sweat, and fainting. Know therefore, that death approaches without doubt.
And the sign of an arrow wounding the lung is the flowing out of frothy blood from the wound; and vessels that follow the neck are to be tied off, and the color of the sick person changes. And breathes out a great, deep breath; and seeks attraction of cold air.
If the arrow falls into the pleura, which is in the chest; then it is near to the small ribs; and a great gasping with intense pain occurs, with sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders are moved.
If the arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested comes out from the wound.
If the arrow falls into the abdomen and is fixed there, then something of feces comes out from the wound, or pus, or an intestine that has already been ruptured. Therefore there is no hope for his cure nor in extracting the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder and urine comes out; and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger upon the sick person; then know that it is mortal.
