In its dislocation according to its full extent, it is necessary that you make the patient sit upright; and let a strong attendant hold him from behind the middle of his back.
Then you hold his foot with your right hand from above and your left hand below the foot of him in the position of the ankle joint.
Then, pull the foot towards you with your right hand. With your left hand press it (the dislocated heel) in two places.
Then stretch it (the foot) with the left and push the front of the foot (ankle) towards the back with the right hand without effort.
Do this twice as we have said.
Then push the front of the foot (ankle) towards the back for the third time and you pull the ankle joint.
If it returns to its place once or twice according to this method, and you see the foot straightened, that is good; if not, then repeat the operation on him, because he will return to his place.
If the reduction of it (the dislocated heel) is prevented for you with him as we have said, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground and set a pillow firmly fixed in the ground so that he falls between his hips; and you should already have wrapped him in cloth so that he does not injure himself.
Then let the attendant take hold of his thigh: afterwards, let another attendant extend the other leg, either with his hands or with a strap that ties around the neck of the foot. Let every attendant extend himself opposite the stretching of his companion: and let the footstool be standing between the two thighs of the weak one, holding him so that his body is not drawn towards the lower parts during the stretching.
Then let the physician adjust [the dislocated part] with his hands, and another attendant hold the sound leg towards the lower parts. For a dislocation returns swiftly.
When the dislocation returns and the health of its return is made known to you: then apply plaster and pitch, and bind it firmly with bandages, and tie the foot with a strap to the sound leg.
And it is necessary that you be careful or afraid of the nerves which are above the heel at the back, so that the bandage is not too tight and injures them.
Then dismiss him for two or three days. If the bandage softens, bind it again; then unbind him on the third or fourth day; and forbid the weak one from walking for forty days. But if he attempts to walk before that period, there will be no assurance that the dislocation will not recur, and it will be damaged, and will not receive healing after that.
If he has a hot abscess: then it is necessary that you administer to its sedation the remedy which was previously mentioned in another place in the cure, and embrocation until it is removed.
[Section on] Dislocation of Fingers of the Foot and Cure.
It is necessary that it be adjusted which has been dislocated with little extension without effort; and this indeed is not difficult, but rather easy.
If the dislocation is in certain nodes of the foot's back: then it is necessary that he makes his foot sit on an equal place with the ground, or on a table: and he stands as if walking.
Then you stand and put your foot over that which rises from those joints. Then press it with your foot until it comes back, and you see that it is equal, and no longer appears to protrude from its place.
Then put a board under the foot's belly which can hold the entire foot, having two legs. Then bind it with a suitable bandage for three days. Then unbind it and let him rest from walking for many days, until it is bound and secured against relapse.
Chapter on the types of dislocations with wound or fracture.
When something happens to it, and you attempt its cure and restoration, death often occurs multiple times; therefore, one should not presume to treat this type of condition without being wise in the art of long practice, merciful, pious, patient, cautious, not presumptuous, and using only cold medicines at first: and let the sick man be left to divine judgment. Unless you see or hope for salvation from impending destruction with the softening of the sickness, and where something appears to indicate hope. Try its reduction immediately at the beginning, before a hot abscess occurs.
If the limb then returns as we desire, then administer a regime that checks an abscess; and heal the wound with that which is suitable for it from dry ointments.
If the dislocation is with a fracture and there are separated splinters in the bone of the shaft, then try to remove them, and make in that which was said for simple diseases from the place where they preceded.
And be careful according to your virtue, and guard yourself from entering the path of fear: according to what my prediction preceded for you.
That is better for you with your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more safe for your body among them at your time.
